وَأَمَّا الْيَمِينُ بِاللهِ فَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَيْهَا فَيَنْعَقِدُ إِذَا حَلَفَ عَامِداً أَوْ سَاهِياً أَوْ مُخْطِياً أَوْ مُكْرَهَا وَ كَذَا إِذَا فَعَلَ الْمَحْلُوْفُ عَلَيْهِ كَذَلِكَ وَأَمَّا نِيَّةُ تَخْصِيْصِ الْعَامِّ فِي الْيَمِيْنِ فَمَقْبُوْلَةٌ دِيَانَةً إتفاقاً وَقَضَاء عِندَ الْحَصَّافِ وَالْفَتَوى عَلَى قَوْلِهِ إِنْ كَانَ الْحَالِفُ مَظْلُوْماً وَكَذلِكَ اخْتَلَفُوْا هَلِ الْإِعْتِبَارُ لِنِيَّةِ الْحَالِفِ أَوْ لِنِيَّةِ الْمُسْتَحْلِفِ وَالْفَتْوَىٰ عَلَى إِعْتِبَارِ نِيَّةِ الْحَالِفِ إِنْ كَانَ مَظْلُوماً لَا إِنْ كَانَ ظَالِماً كَمَا فِي الْوَلْوَالْجِيَّةِ وَالْخُلَاصَةِ . ترجمہ : اور بہر حال اللہ کی قسم پس وہ اس پر موقوف نہیں لہذا جب قسم کھائی عمد آیا بھول کر یا غلطی سے یا بجبرو اکراہ تو منعقد ہو جائے گی اور یہی حکم جب مخلوف علیہ نے ایسے ہی کیا ہو ۔ اور بہر حال قسم میں عام کو خاص کرنے کی نیت تو بالا تفاق دیا یہ مقبول ہے اور قضاء امام خصاف کے نزدیک اور فتوی انہی کے قول پر ہے اگر قسم کھانے والا مظلوم ہو اور ایسے ہی علماء نے اختلاف کیا ہے کہ آیا حالف کی نیت کا اعتبار ہو گا یا متخلف کی نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور فتویٰ حالف کی نیت کے اعتبار پر ہے اگر وہ مظلوم ہو۔ نہ کہ اگر وہ ظالم ہو جیسا کہ ولوالجیہ اور خلاصہ میں ہے۔
And as for the oath by Allah, it does not depend on intention; it is concluded whether one swears intentionally, forgetfully, mistakenly, or under compulsion. Similarly, if the one on whom oath is taken does likewise. And as for the intention to narrow a general expression in the oath, it is accepted in conscience (diyanatan) by agreement, and in court (qada'an) according to Imam al-Khassaf; and the fatwa is on his opinion if the swearer is oppressed. Likewise they differed: is consideration given to the intention of the swearer or the intention of the one who administers the oath? The fatwa is on considering the intention of the swearer if he is oppressed, not if he is an oppressor, as in al-Walwalijiyyah and al-Khulasah.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage discusses the rasm rule for oaths (yamin). First principle: an oath by Allah is binding (mun'aqid) regardless of the state of the swearer – whether intentional, forgetful, mistaken, or coerced. The oath becomes effective, and breaking it incurs expiation (kaffarah). This is because the oath is a solemn affirmation invoking Allah, and mere utterance is sufficient; internal intention does not affect its validity. This is the established Hanafi position. Second: when a swearer intends to limit a general expression in his oath (e.g., swearing 'I will not talk to Zaid' but meaning only in anger), that intention is accepted diyanatan (between him and Allah) by consensus. However, in court (qada'an), there is a dispute: Imam al-Khassaf accepts it; the fatwa is on his view, but only if the swearer is oppressed (mazlum), i.e., he was forced into swearing or the oath was used against him unjustly. Third: there is a dispute about whose intention counts – the swearer or the one who administered the oath? The fatwa says the swearer's intention is considered, again only if he is oppressed; if he is the oppressor, the intention is not considered. This nuance is crucial for muftis: a litigant who appears oppressed may have his subjective intention accepted in court, but one who is manifestly oppressive cannot evade his oath by claiming a restricted intention.

Key Terms
اليمين بالله (al-yamin billah): An oath invoking the name of Allah, e.g., 'Wallahi I will not do this'.
نية تخصيص العام (niyyat takhsis al-'amm): Intention to restrict the scope of a general expression in an oath.
ديانة (diyanatan): Before Allah; morally binding but not enforceable in court.
قضاء (qada'an): Judicially enforceable in a court of law.
حالف (halif): The person who swears an oath.
مستحلف (mustahlif): The person who administers or demands the oath.
مظلوم (mazlum): One who is oppressed; in context, one who swears under compulsion or whose oath is used against him unjustly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, according to the fatwa, when is the intention to narrow a general expression in an oath accepted in court (qada'an)?
A) Always, regardless of the swearer's circumstances.
B) Only if the swearer was intentionally making a false oath.
C) Only if the swearer is oppressed (mazlum).
D) Only if the oath is administered by a judge.

Key Takeaway
An oath by Allah is binding without intention; narrowing intention helps only before Allah, and in court only if the swearer is oppressed.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Oaths by Allah: Intention and Specification of General Terms
Maxim with exception for specification under oppression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-yamin bi-Allah la yatawaqqaf 'ala al-niyyah' to distinguish between diyanatan and qada acceptance of intention, and identify when the exception for the oppressed swearer is invoked.

Core Idea
An oath by Allah binds even without intention, but an oppressed swearer's specification is accepted judicially.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental Hanafi maxim in the chapter of oaths: that an oath by Allah is valid regardless of the swearer's intention or custom. However, an important exception arises when the swearer later specifies a general term—this is accepted religiously by all, and judicially only if the swearer is oppressed. We will explore the reasoning behind this exception and its practical application in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the core ruling: an oath by Allah does not depend on intention or custom. The oath is valid even if sworn forgetfully, mistakenly, or under coercion.
This is the apparent madhhab of the Hanafi school.
2
Understand diyanatan vs. qada
Diyanatan refers to what is valid in the sight of Allah; qada refers to judicial enforceability. The specification of a general term is accepted diyanatan by consensus.
In court, only the oppressed swearer's specification is accepted, per al-Khassaf.
3
Analyze the exception
When the swearer is oppressed (e.g., forced by captors), his intention to specify the general term is accepted in qada according to Imam al-Khassaf. The fatwa follows this view for the oppressed.
The exception is based on the maxim 'al-darar yuzal' (harm must be removed).
4
Apply the exception to examples
Work through the examples: a captive forced to swear about eating meat, and a person who swears 'any woman I marry is divorced' but intends women of a specific city.
The ruling depends on whether the swearer is truly oppressed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
In general, the fatwa follows the apparent madhhab (no acceptance of specification in court). For the oppressed, it shifts to al-Khassaf.
The mufti must assess oppression carefully.

وَأَمَّا الْيَمِينُ بِاللهِ فَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَيْهَا فَيَنْعَقِدُ إِذَا حَلَفَ عَامِداً أَوْ سَاهِياً أَوْ مُخْطِياً أَوْ مُكْرَهَا وَ كَذَا إِذَا فَعَلَ الْمَحْلُوْفُ عَلَيْهِ كَذَلِكَ وَأَمَّا نِيَّةُ تَخْصِيْصِ الْعَامِّ فِي الْيَمِيْنِ فَمَقْبُوْلَةٌ دِيَانَةً إتفاقاً وَقَضَاء عِندَ الْحَصَّافِ وَالْفَتَوى عَلَى قَوْلِهِ إِنْ كَانَ الْحَالِفُ مَظْلُوْماً وَكَذلِكَ اخْتَلَفُوْا هَلِ الْإِعْتِبَارُ لِنِيَّةِ الْحَالِفِ أَوْ لِنِيَّةِ الْمُسْتَحْلِفِ وَالْفَتْوَىٰ عَلَى إِعْتِبَارِ نِيَّةِ الْحَالِفِ إِنْ كَانَ مَظْلُوماً لَا إِنْ كَانَ ظَالِماً كَمَا فِي الْوَلْوَالْجِيَّةِ وَالْخُلَاصَةِ . ترجمہ : اور بہر حال اللہ کی قسم پس وہ اس پر موقوف نہیں لہذا جب قسم کھائی عمد آیا بھول کر یا غلطی سے یا بجبرو اکراہ تو منعقد ہو جائے گی اور یہی حکم جب مخلوف علیہ نے ایسے ہی کیا ہو ۔ اور بہر حال قسم میں عام کو خاص کرنے کی نیت تو بالا تفاق دیا یہ مقبول ہے اور قضاء امام خصاف کے نزدیک اور فتوی انہی کے قول پر ہے اگر قسم کھانے والا مظلوم ہو اور ایسے ہی علماء نے اختلاف کیا ہے کہ آیا حالف کی نیت کا اعتبار ہو گا یا متخلف کی نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور فتویٰ حالف کی نیت کے اعتبار پر ہے اگر وہ مظلوم ہو۔ نہ کہ اگر وہ ظالم ہو جیسا کہ ولوالجیہ اور خلاصہ میں ہے۔ تشريح اليمين لغة القوة وشرعاً عبارة عن عقد قوى به عزم الحالف على الفعل او الترک (درمختار على رد المحتار ج ۵ ص / ۴۷۰) اللہ کی قسم کھانا نیت پر موقوف نہیں ہے یعنی اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ اللہ کی قسم میں فلاں کام نہیں کرونگا اور پھر اس نے وہ کام کر لیا تو حالف حانث ہو جائے گا اور اس پر قسم کا کفارہ واجب ہو جائے گا بھلے ہی پھر وہ یوں کہے کہ میری مراد تو کسی اور چیز کی قسم کھانا تھا تو اس کی اس بات کا اعتبار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ ہمارے اصحاب کا ظاہر مذہب یہ ہے کہ للہ کی قسم کھانا نیست یا عرف پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔ وفي رد المحتار والحاصل كما في البحران الحلف بالله تعالى لايتوقف على النية ولا على العرف على الظاهر من مذهب اصحابنا وهو الصحيح. (شامی کراچی ج ۳ ص ۷۱۱) فين عقد اذا حلف جب آپ کو معلوم ہوگیا کہ للہ کی م ی ی ع پر موقوف نہیں ہے کہ ا ر ا ر ہے تو گری نے اللہ کی قسم عمد ا کھائی یا بھول کر یا غلطی سے یا کسی کے زبردستی کرنے سے ہر صورت میں قسم کھانے والا حانث ہو جائے گا وكذا إذا فعل المحلوف علیہ : مخلوف علیہ جس کی قسم کھائی جائے جس کی قسم کھائی گئی ہے اس کا فعل بھی نیت پر موقوف نہیں ہے مثلاً کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ فلاں شخص اگر گھر میں آگیا تو تجھے طلاق تو اب جب بھی وہ گھر میں آئے گا تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی چاہے آتے وقت اس فلاں کے گھر میں آنے کی نیت ہو یا نہ ہواس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوگا۔ خواہ وہ فصل فلاں عمر ہو یا بھول کر یا غلطی سے ہو یا بجبر واکراہ گھر میں اس فلاں کو لایا گیا ہو ۔ دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مثلاً مخلوف علیہ یعنی جس پر قسم کھائی گئی ہے وہ کسی کی دوکان ہے قسم کھانے والے نے مقسم کھائی کہ اللہ کی قسم میں فلاں کی دوکان پر نہیں جاؤں گا اب وہ دوکان پر چلا گیا خواہ عمد ادوکان پر گیا یا بھول کر یا غلطی سے یا کبر وا گمراہ ہر صورت میں حانث ہو جائے گا۔ واما نية تخصيص العام فی الیمین : اس مسئلہ کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ کسی نے عام لفظ سے قسم کھائی اور پھر بعد میں تخصیص کی نیت کرے مثلا یوں کہے اگر میں اپنے غلہ میں سے کسی کو کچھ دوں تو میری بیوی کو طلاق اور اس کے بعد پھر یوں کہے کہ میں نے اس سے اپنی ماں کی نیت کی تھی تو اس نے عام میں تخصیص کی نیت کی تو دیا یہ باتفاق علماء تخصیص کی نیت یمین کے الفاظ عام میں جائز ہے۔ امام خصاف کے نزدیک یمین کے الفاظ عام میں تخصیص کی نیت جیسے دیا نہ قابل قبول ہے ایسے ہی قضاء بھی جائز ہے۔ مثلا کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ جس عورت سے بھی میں شادی کروں اس کو طلاق پھر بعد میں یوں کہے کہ میری نیست تو فلاں شہر کی عورتوں کی تھی تو ظاہر مذہب یہ ہے کہ جس عورت سے بھی شادی کرے گا قضاء وہ حانث ہو جائے گا اور اس کی بیوی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی البتہ امام خصاف کے نزدیک حالف کی نیت کا اعتبار دیانہ وقضاء دونوں طرح ہوگا اور فیصلہ اس کی نیت کے اعتبار سے ہوگا۔ والفتوى على قوله : فتوی ظاہر مذہب پر ہوگا یا امام خصاف کے قول پر ؟ علامہ ابن نجیم علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عام حالات میں فتوئی ظاہر مذہب پر ہوگا البتہ اگر حالف ظالموں کے قبضہ میں ہو اور حالف مظلوم ہو تو ایسی صورت میں فتویٰ امام خصاف کے مذہب پر ہوگا۔ مثلاً کسی مسلم کو کافروں نے پکڑ لیا اور کہا کہ تم قسم کھاؤ اگر میں نے گوشت کھایا تو میری بیوی کو طلاق اور پھر بعد میں حالف نے کہا کہ میں نے تو حرام گوشت کی نیت کی تھی تو اس صورت میں امام خصاف کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے گا اور اس کی نیت کے اعتبار سے فیصلہ ہوگا اگر کسی پر زبردستی کی گئی محمدصلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو برا بھلا کہنے پر اور وہ محمد سے اس کی ذات مراد لے جو رسول نہ ہو تو بالا تفاق اس صورت میں خصاف کے قول پر ہی فتویٰ ہوگا۔ فائدہ : یمین کے الفاظ عام میں تخصیص کی نیت معتبر ہے دیا نہ با تفاق علماء۔ خواہ تم عربی زبان میں ہو یا فاری او خانیہ میں سیکو میچ قرار دیا گیا ہے جبکہ بعض فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر تم عربی زبان میں ہے تو تخصیص نیت کا اعتبار
And as for the oath by Allah, it does not depend on it (intention), so it is concluded when one swears intentionally, forgetfully, mistakenly, or under coercion. Similarly, when the one upon whom the oath is sworn does so likewise. And as for the intention to specify a general term in an oath, it is accepted diyanatan (according to religious conscience) by agreement, and in qada (judicially) according to al-Khassaf, and the fatwa is according to his saying if the swearer is oppressed. Similarly, they differed: is consideration given to the intention of the swearer or the intention of the one who makes him swear? The fatwa is on consideration of the intention of the swearer if he is oppressed, not if he is an oppressor, as in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Khulasah. Translation: And in any case, the oath by Allah does not depend on it (intention). Hence, when one swears intentionally, forgetfully, mistakenly, or under coercion, it becomes binding. And the same ruling when the one upon whom the oath is sworn does likewise. And in any case, the intention to specify a general term in an oath is accepted diyanatan by consensus, and in qada according to Imam al-Khassaf, and the fatwa is according to his saying if the swearer is oppressed. Similarly, the scholars differed as to whether consideration is given to the intention of the swearer or the intention of the one who makes him swear; and the fatwa is on consideration of the swearer's intention if he is oppressed, not if he is an oppressor, as is in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Khulasah. Definition of oath: linguistically, strength; legally, it is a strong contract by which the swearer's resolve to act or abstain is strengthened. (Durr Mukhtar with Radd al-Muhtar vol.5 p.470) Swearing by Allah does not depend on intention; i.e., if someone swears by Allah that he will not do such-and-such and then does it, the swearer becomes a breaker of the oath and expiation becomes obligatory on him, even if he later says: 'I meant to swear by something else' – his statement is not considered, because the apparent position of our (Hanafi) masters is that swearing by Allah does not depend on intention or custom. (Radd al-Muhtar, and the conclusion as in al-Bahr: swearing by Allah does not depend on intention or custom according to the apparent madhhab of our masters, and that is correct. (Shami Karachi vol.3 p.711) So when you know that swearing by Allah does not depend on intention or custom, then if someone swears by Allah intentionally, forgetfully, mistakenly, or under coercion, in every case the swearer becomes a breaker. Similarly, when the one upon whom the oath is sworn acts likewise: The one upon whom the oath is sworn – his act also does not depend on intention. For example, someone swears: 'If such-and-such person enters the house, then my wife is divorced.' Now whenever that person enters the house, divorce occurs, regardless of whether he intended to enter the house or not – his intention is not considered. Whether he enters intentionally, forgetfully, mistakenly, or is brought under coercion. Another meaning: for example, the one upon whom the oath is sworn is someone's shop; the swearer swears: 'By Allah, I will not go to so-and-so's shop.' Now if he goes to that shop, whether intentionally, forgetfully, mistakenly, or under coercion, in every case he becomes a breaker. As for the intention to specify a general term in an oath: The summary of this issue is that someone swears with a general word and later intends specification, e.g., he says: 'If I give anyone of my grain, my wife is divorced,' and then says: 'I meant my mother.' So he intended specification of the general. This intention to specify general words in an oath is permissible diyanatan by consensus of scholars. According to Imam al-Khassaf, the intention to specify general terms in an oath is acceptable diyanatan and also in qada. For example, if someone swears: 'Any woman I marry is divorced,' and later says: 'I meant women of such-and-such city,' then according to the apparent madhhab, any woman he marries will cause him to break the oath in qada and his wife will be divorced. However, according to Imam al-Khassaf, the swearer's intention is considered both diyanatan and in qada, and the decision will be based on his intention. And the fatwa is according to his saying: The fatwa is according to the apparent madhhab or according to Imam al-Khassaf's saying? Allamah Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) says: In general, the fatwa is according to the apparent madhhab, but if the swearer is under the control of oppressors and the swearer is oppressed, then in such a case the fatwa is according to Imam al-Khassaf's madhhab. For example, if a Muslim is captured by disbelievers and they say: 'Swear that if you eat meat, your wife is divorced,' and later the swearer says: 'I intended unlawful meat,' then in this case the fatwa is given according to Imam al-Khassaf's saying and the decision is based on his intention. If someone is forced to speak ill of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and he intends the individual named Muhammad who is not the Messenger (i.e., someone else), then by consensus in this case the fatwa is according to al-Khassaf's saying. Benefit: The intention to specify a general term in an oath is considered valid diyanatan by consensus of scholars, whether the oath is in Arabic, Persian, or any other language...
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the maxim 'Oaths by Allah do not depend on intention or custom.' It clarifies that an oath by Allah is valid regardless of the swearer's intention at the time of swearing, and even if the sworn act occurs unintentionally. The author then discusses the exception of 'specification of general terms' (takhsis al-amm), where a swearer later claims he meant a specific subset of the general words. This is accepted diyanatan (religiously) but not in court unless the swearer is oppressed. Imam al-Khassaf's position allows judicial acceptance for the oppressed, and the fatwa follows this when the swearer is under duress. The passage also distinguishes between the intention of the swearer and that of the one who imposes the oath, again giving weight to the oppressed swearer. Practical examples illustrate the rulings: an oath about entering a house or shop triggers violation regardless of intention; but specification of a general term like 'any woman' can be restricted by intention in cases of oppression. The text thus balances general rule and equitable exception, a hallmark of Hanafi usul al-iftaa.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): A strong contract by which the swearer strengthens his resolve to do or abstain from an act, usually by invoking Allah.
تخصيص العام (takhsis al-amm): Specifying a general term in an oath to a particular subset, e.g., intending a specific person or category.
ديانة (diyanatan): From a religious perspective, in the sight of Allah, accepted even if not enforceable in court.
قضاء (qada): Judicially, in a court of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, when does the Hanafi school accept the specification of a general term in an oath in a court of law?
A) Always
B) Only when the swearer is oppressed
C) Only in Arabic oaths
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Oaths by Allah are binding without intention, but the school allows judicial acceptance of specification for the oppressed swearer to prevent injustice.

Takhsis by Attribute Not Considered in Oaths
States the maxim with one illustrative case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim regarding attributive specification in oaths and apply it to a given case.

Core Idea
In Hanafi oaths, a hidden intent to specify by attribute is ignored — the general word binds.

This lesson explores a key maxim from the Hanafi corpus on oaths. The passage draws a sharp line: when someone swears using a general term, any unexpressed qualification is legally irrelevant. This principle protects the outward meaning of the oath and prevents manipulation of the vow. Understanding this rule is essential for muftis when evaluating breach-of-oath cases.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Write the Arabic text of the maxim and its English translation verbatim from the passage.
Memorise the phrasing: 'یمین کے الفاظ عام میں تخصیص صفت غیر معتبر ہے'.
2
Identify the scope
Determine which chapter of fiqh this maxim governs. It is specific to al-ayman (oaths), not ibadat or muamalat.
Apply only when a person utters a yamin.
3
Apply the maxim to the furu'
Take the given case: someone swears 'I will not buy a slave-girl' but intends a specific one (who has a child). The maxim says the oath applies to all slave-girls because the general word 'jaariyah' is not restricted by the unexpressed attribute.
The ruling is clear: the oath is broken if any slave-girl is bought.
4
Note any exceptions
The source does not list any exceptions (istithna). The maxim is absolute within its scope.
If a future text mentions exceptions, note them separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) یمین کے الفاظ عام میں تخصیص صفت غیر معتبر ہے اس لئے لا اشترى جارية ونوى مؤلده . اشکال وارد نہیں ہوگا۔
In oaths, specification of a general word by an attribute is not considered. Therefore, if one says 'I will not buy a concubine' but intended a specific one (her child), no problem arises.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This is a legal maxim from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair concerning oaths (al-yamin). According to the Hanafi school, when a person swears an oath using general words, any subsequent claim that they intended a specific meaning through an attribute is not given legal effect. The example clarifies: if someone swears 'I will not buy a slave-girl' (jaariyah) but in his heart intends a specific slave-girl who has a child (muwaladah), the oath remains general and binding for all slave-girls. This is because the outward words of the oath are authoritative, not the hidden intention. The maxim is a specific rule (sughra) under the broader principle of 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' but with an exception for oaths.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath or solemn vow
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification or restriction of a general term to a particular meaning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The oath applies to all slave-girls.
C) The oath is invalid due to ambiguity.
D) The intention makes the oath a vow, not an oath.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an oath is interpreted by its general wording; a hidden intent to restrict by an attribute has no legal effect.

8 min
The Qawida 'al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' – Tool Proxy in Qisas
Explains the operation of the qawida in jinayat and hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to classify homicide as 'amd or shibh 'amd based on the instrument used, and identify the istithna' where intention is disregarded in hadd penalties.

Core Idea
Intention is central, but when hidden, the tool stands in its place.

The Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) is foundational across all chapters of fiqh. In criminal law, its application is both direct and nuanced. This lesson explores how qisas depends on the killer's intention, but since intention is internal, the Hanafi school relies on the outward instrument as a reliable proxy. We will also see the exceptions: in hadd crimes like qadhf and theft, intention is disregarded entirely.

Guided Path
1
State the Qawida and Its Rank
Recite the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' and understand that it is a major (kubra) maxim governing all fiqh chapters, especially criminal law.
The qawida is derived from the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat'.
2
Identify the Scope in Homicide
Recognize that qisas depends on the killer's intention (qasd). Since intention is internal, the Hanafi school uses the instrument (ala) as a proxy for intent.
The text says: 'lama kana al-qasd amran batiniyan aqimat al-alah maqamahu'.
3
Work Through the Furuat: Tool Determines Classification
If the tool normally severs limbs (e.g., sword, gun), it is 'amd and qisas applies. If the tool does not usually sever limbs but often kills (e.g., heavy stick), it is shibh 'amd – no qisas, only diyah and kaffarah.
The distinction between 'amd and shibh 'amd is unique to Hanafi school.
4
Identify the Istithna' in Hadd Penalties
In qadhf and theft, the hadd penalty is applied regardless of the actor’s claimed intention. The outward act alone establishes the penalty.
The governing qawida for exceptions is 'al-hudud tuddara' bi al-shubuhat'.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Given a scenario of a man hit with a wooden stick causing death, classify as shibh 'amd and state the ruling: no qisas, obligatory diyah and kaffarah.
If the stick is heavy and often fatal, it is shibh 'amd.

Source Text

مثلا کسی نے کسی کے اوپر تہمت لگائی اور پھر حد قذف جاری ہونے کا وقت آیا تو وہ کہنے لگے کہ اے این این کو لگانے کی نہیں تھی یا چور نے چوری کی اور جب ہاتھ کٹنے کا وقت آیا تب وہ کہے کہ میری پوری کی نیت نکات میں تو ان کی [؟می نیست] معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ قذف اور چورنی میں نیت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔

وَأَمَّا الْقِصَاصُ فَمُتوقف على قصد القاتل القتُلَ لَكِنْ قَالُوْا لَمَّا كَانَ الْقَصْدُ أَمْرَا بَاطِيَا أَقِيمَتِ الْآلَهُ مَقَامَهُ فَإِنْ قَتَلَهُ بِمَا يُفَرِّقُ الْأجْرَاء عَادَةَ كَانَ عمداً و وَجَبَ الْقَصَاصُ فيه و إِلَّا فَإِنْ قَتَلَهُ بِمَا لَايُفَرِّقَ الأَجْزَاء عَادَةً لكنَّهُ يَقْتُلُ غالباً فَهُوَ شَبُهُ عَمَدٍ لَا قَصَاصَ فِيهِ عِنْدَ الإمام الأعظم وأمَّا الخطأ بأن يقصد مُباحاً فيُصِيب ادْميًّا كَمَا عُلِمَ في باب الجنايات.

ترجمہ: اور بہر حال قصاص تو وہ قاتل کے قتل کے ارادہ کرنے پر موقوف ہے لیکن فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ چونکا قصد امر باطنی ہے اس لئے آلہ کواس کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا پس اگراس کوایسی چیز سے قتل کیاہے جو عاد اجزا کو جدا کردج ہے تو وہ عمد انہو گا اور قصاص اس میں واجب ہو گا ورنہ اگر اس کو ایسی چیز سے قتل کیا ہے جو عادۃ اجزاء کو جدا نہیں کرتا لیکن اکثر قتل کر دیتا ہے تو وہ شبہ عمد ہے اس میں قصاص نہیں امام اعظم کے نزدیک اور بہر حال خطا ء یہ کہ کسی مہات چیز کا ارادہ کرے اور وہ اچانک کسی آدمی کو لگ جائے جیسا کہ باب الجنایات سے یہی معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح: قصاص قص سے نکلا ہے جس کے معنی ہیں کسی کے پیچھے چلنا یا کوئی استعمال کیا ہے جو عام طور سے جان سے مارنے کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے تو وہ آلہ قتل نیست قتل کے قائم مقام ہوگا جسے تلوار، بندوق وغیرہ ، اس صورت میں قصاص قاتل پر واجب ہوگا اور قاتل کی نیت کا عتبار نہ ہزار درہم دین کے ہیں۔ اور کفارہ مؤمن غلام آزاد کرنا یا دو ماہ کے مسلسل روزے رکھنا۔ اور اگر فقل خطاء ہے جس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ (۱) خطاء فی الفعل (۲) خطاء فی الصواب، کہ آدمی نے کسی انسان کو شکار سمجھ کر غلطی سے مار دیا تو یہ خطاء فی الفعل ہے۔ (۲) یہ کہ آدمی نے اصلا شکار کو مارنے کا ارادہ کیا لیکن نشانہ خطا کر گیا اور کسی انسان کو گولی لگ گئی تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں بھی قاتل پر کفارہ اور عاقلہ پر دبیت لازم ہوگی ۔ قتل شبہ خطاء اس کی دو صورتیں فقہاء نے بھی ہیں ۔ (1) ایک یہ کہ قتل کی یہ غلطی پر اور است اس سے ہوئی مثلا کوئی شخص سوتے ہوئے کروٹ بدلے یا کسی دوسرے کے اوپر گر جائے اور وہ اس کے بوجھ سے دب کر مر جائے تو اس پر بھی قتل خطاء کے سارے احکام نافذ ہونگے یعنی دیت بھی دینی ہوگی اور وہ اس کی وصیت اور میراث سے بھی محروم ہوگا۔ (۲) دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص تلوار اٹھائے ہوئے یا گھماتے ہوئے چل رہا تھایا بندوق کی گولی بھر کر چل رہاتھا اور تلوار کسی کے اوپر گر گئی اور اس کے زخم سے وہ مر گیا یا گولی خود بخود چل گئی اور وہ مر گیا یا سواری نے غلطی سے اسے کچل دیا تو یہ بھی مشاب قتل خطاء ہے یعنی اس پر دیت ہوگی کفارہ نہیں اور نہ میراث سے محروم ہوگا ۔ (هدابه ج ۳ ص / ۵۳۵) اور پانچویں قسم قتل کی قتل بالسبب ہے جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ براہ راست قتل نہ ہو بلکہ قتل کے فعل کا سبب بن جائے جیسے راستہ میں کنواں کھود دیا اور کوئی اس میں گر کر مر گیا تو اس میں صرف دیت واجب ہوگی اور سہ دیت خاندان کے لوگ ملکر ادا کریں گے ۔ (ہدایہ ج ۳ ص ۵۶۳) البتہ قتل عمد کی دیت قاتل کے مال سے ہی ضروری ہے قتل خطاء اور قتل شبہ عمد کی دیت میں قاتل کے ساتھ بطور مدد ونصرت اس کے عاقلہ بھی شریک ہوں گے اور اس کی ادائیگی کے لئے تین سال کی مدت مقرر کی گئی ہے۔
For example, someone accused another of adultery, and when the time for the hadd of qadhf came, he said, 'I did not intend to accuse him,' or a thief stole, and when the time for cutting the hand came, he said, 'My intention was not to steal,' then his statement will not be considered, because in qadhf and theft, intention is not considered.

As for qisas, it depends on the killer's intention to kill. But they said: Since intention is an internal matter, the tool is made to stand in its place. So if he killed him with something that normally severs limbs, it is 'amd and qisas is wajib. Otherwise, if he killed him with something that does not normally sever limbs but often kills, it is shibh 'amd – no qisas according to Imam A'zam. As for khata' (error): intending something permissible but it hits a person, as known in the chapter of criminal acts.

[Urdu translation and elaboration follows, listing five types of murder with rulings, diyah values, difference with Sahibayn, etc.]
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an application of the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) but with important exceptions. The text opens with two cases where intention is not considered: in qadhf (false accusation of zina) and theft, the hadd penalties apply regardless of the accused's claimed intent. Then it turns to qisas, where intention is crucial but is inferred from the tool used. The author explains that since inner intent is hidden, the tool (e.g., sword, gun) serves as its proxy. If the tool ordinarily causes dismemberment, it is 'amd (intentional) and qisas applies. If it is a tool that does not usually dismember but often kills (e.g., a heavy stick), it is shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional) – no qisas per Imam Abu Hanifa, but diyah and kaffarah. Then khata' (mistake) and shibh khata' (quasi-mistake) are detailed, each with specific rulings on diyah, kaffarah, and inheritance. The passage also records intra-madhhab differences: Sahibayn allow diyah payment with cattle and cloth, while Imam Abu Hanifa restricts to camels, dinars, or dirhams. It also notes the position of Imam Malik and Shafi'i (12,000 dirhams). The classification of homicide into five types (including qatl bi-sabab) is thoroughly explained with examples from Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah. The lesson demonstrates how the qawida operates in criminal law: intention is central but externally evidenced, and in some cases (hadd penalties) intention is disregarded entirely.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional homicide or injury, equivalent to the harm inflicted.
عمد ('amd): Intentional killing with an instrument that ordinarily severs limbs or kills.
شبه عمد (shibh 'amd): Killing with an instrument that does not normally sever limbs but often kills (e.g., a heavy stick).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school use the instrument (tool) to determine whether a homicide is 'amd or shibh 'amd?
A) Because the killer's statement is always unreliable
B) Because intention is internal and the tool serves as a practical, objective proxy
C) Because all homicide is presumed intentional unless the tool is harmless
D) Because the tool is easier to measure than the killer's psychology

Key Takeaway
Intention in qisas is determined by the tool's normal effect, not the killer's claim; in hadd penalties, intention is irrelevant.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Intention Transforms the Ruling: Reciting Quran as Dhikr for Junub and Ha'id
Application of qawida to junub/ha'id reciting Quranic verses as dhikr/dua

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine the permissibility of Quranic recitation for a junub or ha'id based on intention, and explain the Hanafi position on apparent inconsistencies in salah.

Core Idea
Intention can remove the prohibition of Quran recitation for junub/ha'id by transforming the act into dhikr or dua.

This lesson explores a powerful application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). The Hanafi school permits a person in major impurity (junub) or a menstruating woman (ha'id) to recite Quranic verses that contain dhikr or dua, provided they intend dhikr or dua, not tilawah (Quran recitation). This ruling demonstrates how intention (qasd) can alter the legal classification of an act. We will also examine a potential inconsistency raised by the fuqaha regarding a speaker in salah and a ma'mum in janazah salah, and how it is resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base qawida and its application
Recognize that the permissibility for junub/ha'id to recite Quranic verses as dhikr/dua is a direct furu' (branch) of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'. The act of recitation is judged by its intention; if the intention is dhikr, it is no longer considered tilawah.
The text states: 'إِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ كَوْنِهِ قُرْآنَ بِالْقَصْدِ' – the Quran exits from being Quran through intention.
2
Examine the legal definition of 'Quran recitation'
Using the legal_definition_dissector, analyze how the same verses can be legally categorized as either tilawah (prohibited) or dhikr/dua (permissible) based solely on the reciter's qasd. The mahall (locus) is the verses containing dhikr/dua, the sabab is the intention, and the mani' is the state of janabah or hayd.
The hukm changes from haram to mubah when the intention shifts from tilawah to dhikr.
3
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
Note that Imam Shafi'i and others prohibit any recitation of Quranic verses by junub/ha'id regardless of intention, because the verses are inherently Quran. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the literal text and its legal categorization via intention.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis permit saying 'Bismillah' or 'Alhamdulillah' in janabah, while Shafi'is do not.
4
Resolve the apparent inconsistency in salah
The text raises an objection: if someone in salah speaks with the intention of dhikr, does it invalidate salah? The answer from Sharh al-Kanz: because the words are already in their proper place (dhikr is part of salah), the intention does not change the ruling. Similarly, a ma'mum reciting al-Fatiha in janazah salah with intention of dhikr is not prohibited, even though reciting it in salah is normally prohibited for the ma'mum.
This shows that the qawida operates within the context of the act; it does not override existing rules of salah.

وَأَمَّا قِرَاءَةُ الْقُرْآنِ قَالُوا إِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ كَوْنِهِ قُرْآنَ بِالْقَصْدِ فَجَوَّزُوْا لِلْجُنُبِ وَالْحَائِضِ قِرَأَةَ مَا فِيْهِ مِنَ الْأَذْكَارِ بِقَصْدِ الذِّكْرِ وَالْأَدْعِيَّةِ بِقَصْدِ الدُّعَاءِ لَكِنْ أَشْكَلَ عَلَيْهِ قَوْلُهُمْ لَوْ قَوَا بقَصْدِ الذِّكْرِ لَا تَبْطِلُ صَلوتُهُ وَأَجَيْنَا عَنْهُ فِي شَرح الكنز بِأَنَّهُ فِي مَحَلَّه فَلَا يَتَغَيْرُ بِعَزِيمَتِهِ وَقَالُوا إِنَّ الْمَامُوْمَ إِذَا قَرَأ الْفَاتِحَةَ فِي صَلَوَةِ الْجَنَازَةِ بِنِيَّةِ الَّذِكْرِ لَا تَحْرَمُ عَلَيْهِ مَعْ أَنَّهُ تَحْرُمُ عَلَيْهِ قِرَاءَتُهَا فِي الصَّلوةِ.

ترجمه : اور بہر حال قرآت قرآن تو فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ وہ قصد کے ذریعہ قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے چنانچہ انہوں نے جنبی اور حائضہ کے لئے ذکر کے ارادے سے ان آیات کے پڑھنے کو جائز کہا ہے جن میں اذکار ہوں اور دعاء کے قصد سے ان کے پڑھنے کو جن میں دعائیں ہوں لیکن اس پر فقہاء کے قول سے اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ اگر
As for recitation of the Quran, they said that the Quran exits from being Quran through intention. So they permitted the junub and ha'id to recite what is in it of dhikr with the intention of dhikr, and supplications with the intention of dua. But there is an issue with their statement: 'If he speaks [or emphasizes?] with the intention of dhikr, his salah is not invalidated.' We answered it in Sharh al-Kanz: because it is in its place, so it does not change by his determination. And they said that if the ma'mum recites al-Fatiha in the janazah salah with the intention of dhikr, it is not prohibited for him, even though reciting it in salah is prohibited.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a focused application of the qawida that actions are by intentions, specifically regarding the prohibition of Quran recitation for a person in major impurity (junub) or menstruating woman (ha'id). The Hanafi position is that the prohibition is tied to the act of reciting with the intention of tilawah (Quran recitation). If the same verses are recited with the specific intention of dhikr (remembrance of Allah) or dua (supplication), the act is no longer considered 'Quran recitation' they are permitted. This is a direct application of the principle that actions are judged by intentions. The text then raises a potential inconsistency: if someone speaks (or prays?) in salah with the intention of dhikr, does it invalidate salah? The answer from Sharh al-Kanz is that the words are in their proper place (i.e., within salah, dhikr is part of the prayer), so changing one's intention does not alter the ruling. Similarly, a ma'mum (follower) reciting al-Fatiha in janazah salah with intention of dhikr is permissible, even though reciting it in salah is normally prohibited for the ma'mum. This illustrates the power of niyyah to transform the legal nature of an act.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (e.g., after sexual intercourse or seminal emission).
حائض (ha'id): A menstruating woman, subject to same prohibition as junub regarding Quran recitation.
قصد (qasd): Intention or purpose that determines the legal nature of an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does reciting al-Fatiha with the intention of dhikr become permissible for a ma'mum in janazah salah?
A) Because janazah salah has different rules than regular salah.
B) Because the ma'mum's intention changes the act from prohibited recitation to permissible dhikr.
C) Because the ma'mum is not required to recite anything in janazah.
D) Because the prohibition only applies in obligatory prayers.

Key Takeaway
Intention (qasd) can alter the legal category of an act: reciting Quranic verses with the intention of dhikr or dua removes the prohibition otherwise attached to tilawah for a junub or ha'id.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Intention and Locus: The Interaction of Qasd and Mahall in Hanafi Law
Expansion of the maxim with application to funeral prayer and the case of menstruating/junub persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to distinguish when intention changes the legal nature of Quranic recitation and when it does not, by evaluating the role of mahall (locus).

Core Idea
Intention changes the ruling only when the act is outside its proper locus; inside its locus, intention is overridden.

This passage builds on the foundational Hanafi maxim 'actions are by intentions' by examining a critical nuance: the effect of intention depends on the context (mahall). When a Quranic verse is recited outside its proper place — such as in funeral prayer, where Quran recitation is not prescribed — an intention of dhikr converts the recitation into dhikr, making it permissible even for those otherwise prohibited. But within the proper locus (salah), intention cannot alter the nature; the recitation remains Quran regardless of intent. This lesson unpacks the principle and its practical furu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
Recognize that the passage applies 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to Quran recitation. Note the key addition: mahall.
The maxim alone is not sufficient; the context of recitation is decisive.
2
Define the role of mahall
Understand that mahall (locus) is the prescribed context. When the act is in its mahall, intention does not change its legal nature; when outside, intention can transform.
Salah is the mahall for Quran recitation; funeral prayer is not.
3
Apply to funeral prayer
The passage states that reciting Fatihah with dhikr intention in janazah is permissible because janazah is not a mahall for Quran recitation. The intention turns it into dhikr.
This is a direct furu' of the maxim.
4
Contrast with obligatory salah
In salah, the same recitation remains Quran even if one intends dhikr, because salah is the mahall.
Intention does not affect the nature when the act is in its proper locus.
5
Examine the derivative rulings: junub/ha'id and partial verses
Note the extension to menstruating women and the dispute over madoon al-ayah. The passage shows how the maxim is applied to determine permissibility based on necessity (hardship).
The later Hanafi fatwa uses the maxim to allow recitation with dhikr intention outside salah, but only for parts of verses in cases of hardship.

کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا: لا يقرأ الجنب ولا الحائض شيئاً من القرآن . باتفاق علماء جنبی اور حائضہ کے لئے قرآت قرآن حرام ہے۔ پھر پوری آیت پڑھی جائے یا مادون الآیتہ امام کرخی کے نزدیک دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں صاحب بدائع الصنائع نے عام حالات میں علماء متاخرین کا فتویٰ امام کرخی کے قول پر نقل کیا ہے امام ترندی نے لا يقرأ الجنب ولا الحائض شيئاً من القرآن کو حسن قرآن دیا ہے استدلال اس اس لئے کہ احادیث میں آیت و مادون الآیتہ کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے بلکہ مطلقاً آیت و مادون الآینہ کی قرآت حائضہ اور نبی کے لئے حرام ہے اور تعلیل نص کے مقابلہ میں قابل رد ہے اور اگر حائضہ ونفساء بچوں کو تعلیم دیتی ہے اور چونکہ ان کا زمنہ حیض و نفاس کا طویل ہوتا ہے اور ترک تعلیم میں چونکہ حرج عظیم ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں امام طحاوی کے قول پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہوگی ۔ اور اگر ترک تعلیم کی وجہ سے حرج نہ ہوتو امام کرخی کے قول پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ لكن اشكل عليه قولهم. اس جگہ ایک اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ جب قرآت دعا ء یا ذ کر کے ارادہ سے ذکر یا دعا کے درجہ میں ہو جاتی ہے اور قرآت قرآن ۔ قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتی بھی وہ قرآت قرآن ہی رہے گی کیونکہ یہاں قرآن اپنے محل میں پڑھا جا رہا ہے لہذا نیت اور عزم کے بدلنے سے بھی اس پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑیگا ہاں البتہ اگر قرآت قرآن غیر محل قرآت میں ہو تو نیت ذکر سے قرآن قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے۔ وقالوا ان الماموم اذا قرأ الفاتحة : ماز جنازہ میں قرآت قرآن مشروع نہیں بلکہ ذکر و دعا مشروع ہے اس لئے فقہا، کہتے ہیں اگر مقتدی نماز جنازہ میں ذکر کی نیت سے سورہ فاتحہ پڑھے تو ممنوع نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قرآت غیر محل میں کر کی نیت سے وہ قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا نماز جنازہ میں ذکر کی نیت سے جائز ہوگا نوع نہیں نماز جنازہ میں قرآت قرآن غیر مشروع ہے اور اگر قراتها في الصلاة “ میں صلوٰۃ سے رکوع وسجدہ والے نماز مراد ہوتو مقتدی کے لئے رکوع وسجود میں امام کے پیچھے قرآت قرآن ممنوع ہے خواہ ذکر کا قصد ہو یا قرآت قرآن جن میں خاموش رہنا مطلوب ہے بخلاف نماز جنازہ اس لئے کہ وہ محل دعا ہے اور محل قرآت نہیں ہے اگر چہ قرآت نماز جنازہ میں امام کے پیچھے دعاء کی نیت سے جائز ہے۔
If someone recites [Quran] with the intention of dhikr, his prayer is not valid; and we in Sharh al-Kanz have given this answer: that it is in its proper place, so by his intention it does not change. Also the jurists say that in the funeral prayer, if the follower recites Surah al-Fatihah with the intention of dhikr, it is not prohibited for him, even though reciting it in the funeral prayer is prohibited. Explanation: Allamah Ibn Qayyim al-Misri says that verses which comprise dhikr or supplication, if recited with the intention of dhikr or supplication, they become outside of being Quran. The evidence for this is that the jurists have permitted a menstruating woman and a junub to recite these verses with the intention of supplication or dhikr. If these Quranic verses did not exit from being Quran, they would not be permitted to recite them, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The junub and the menstruating woman should not recite anything of the Quran.' By agreement of scholars, reciting Quran is prohibited for the junub and menstruating woman. Then, whether the entire verse is recited or less than a verse (madoon al-ayah): according to Imam al-Karkhi, there is no difference between the two. The author of Bada'i' al-Sana'i' has transmitted that the later scholars' fatwa in normal circumstances is upon Imam al-Karkhi's statement. Imam al-Tarandi has graded the hadith 'la yaqra al-junub wa la al-ha'id shay'an min al-Quran' as hasan. The deduction from this hadith is that 'shay'an min al-Quran' is in the scope of negation, and the indefinite noun in the scope of negation gives benefit of generality. Therefore, for the junub and menstruating woman, reciting both a verse and less than a verse is prohibited. While Imam al-Mahawati has declared reciting less than a verse permissible for the menstruating woman and junub. And in Khulasah it has been declared as prevalent. The conclusion is that there is a difference of opinion regarding less than a verse. Considering Imam al-Karkhi's statement as preponderant is more appropriate, because the hadith does not differentiate between a verse and less than a verse; rather, absolutely reciting a verse and less than a verse is prohibited for the menstruating woman and the junub. And rational reasoning (ta'lil) in the face of text is rejectable. If a menstruating woman or a woman in post-natal bleeding is teaching children, and because her period of menstruation and post-natal bleeding is long, and in abandoning teaching there is great hardship, then in this situation acting upon the statement of Imam al-Tahawi will be permissible. And if there is no hardship due to abandoning teaching, then act upon Imam al-Karkhi's statement. But there is an objection to their statement. At this point an objection arises: When recitation with the intention of supplication or dhikr becomes of the category of dhikr or supplication, and exits from being Quran, then if someone during prayer, while reciting Quran, intends dhikr or supplication, his prayer should become invalid, because recitation in prayer is obligatory (fard) and it has not been found. The answer to this is that here, even with intention, that recitation will remain Quran, because here Quran is being recited in its proper place; therefore, changing intention and determination has no effect on it. However, if Quran is recited outside its proper place of recitation, then with the intention of dhikr it exits from being Quran. And they said that when the follower recites the Fatihah: in the funeral prayer, Quran recitation is not prescribed; rather, dhikr and supplication are prescribed. Therefore, the jurists say: if the follower recites Surah al-Fatihah in the funeral prayer with the intention of dhikr, he is not prohibited, because recitation outside the proper place, by intention, exits from being Quran. So reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the funeral prayer with the intention of dhikr will be permissible, not prohibited. Quran recitation in the funeral prayer is not prescribed. And if in 'qira'atuha fi al-salah' the word 'salah' refers to the prayer with bowing and prostration, then for the follower, reciting Quran in the presence of the imam in one's bowing and prostration is prohibited, whether the intention is dhikr or Quran recitation; in those acts silence is required. Contrary to the funeral prayer, because it is a place of supplication and not a place of Quran recitation, even though recitation in the funeral prayer behind the imam with the intention of supplication is permissible.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage expands the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) by applying it to the issue of reciting Quranic verses with the intention of dhikr or du'a. The core teaching: the legal effect of intention depends on the locus (mahall). If the recitation occurs in a place where Quran recitation is prescribed (like in salah), the intention does not change the essential nature of the act—it remains Quran and fulfills the obligation. But if it occurs outside that locus (like in funeral prayer, where dhikr is prescribed but not Quran recitation), the intention converts the recitation into dhikr, making it permissible even for those who are prohibited from touching or reciting Quran. The author discusses historical scholarly differences: Imam al-Karkhi held that both full verses and parts of verses are treated similarly, while others allowed parts of verses for menstruating women. The passage also addresses the practical issue of teaching children, where necessity (hardship) allows following the more lenient view of Imam al-Tahawi. The key lesson: the same action (uttering the words of a Quranic verse) can be classified differently based on context and intention, demonstrating the flexibility and nuance of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Key Terms
محل (mahall): The proper place or context in which an act is prescribed; e.g., salah is the mahall of Quran recitation, funeral prayer is not.
مادون الآية (madoon al-ayah): Less than a full verse, e.g., a part of a Quranic verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim discussed, why does reciting Surah al-Fatihah with the intention of dhikr in funeral prayer become permissible, while doing so in the obligatory prayer would not invalidate the recitation?
A) Because funeral prayer is shorter
B) Because in funeral prayer, Quran recitation is not prescribed, so intention turns it into dhikr; in salah, it is prescribed, so intention has no effect
C) Because the follower's intention is always binding
D) Because funeral prayer requires silence

Key Takeaway
The intention can transform the ruling of Quranic recitation only when it occurs outside its prescribed locus, demonstrating the nuanced interaction of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' with the concept of mahall.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Liability Does Not Arise from Mere Intention
Explaining that daman (liability) is based on action, not mere intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'la yatarattabu al-daman bi-mujarrad al-niyyah min ghayr fi'l' to cases of ihram penalties and trust liability.

Core Idea
Liability requires an overt act; no financial or penal responsibility arises from mere intention alone.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi controlling rule (dabt) regarding liability (daman) and penalties (jaza'). The rule states that liability does not become established by mere intention without an accompanying action. Through the examples of a muhrim (one in ihram) wearing a sewn garment and a trustee wearing entrusted property, we see how intention interacts with action to determine whether a penalty multiplies or whether liability continues. The underlying principle is that the law looks to external conduct, not internal resolve, for imposing financial and penal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its scope
Locate the core legal maxim: liability does not arise by mere intention. Note that it is a dabt (sub-rule) that restricts the broader maxim 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' in the context of daman.
2
Examine the first furu‘: muhrim wearing sewn garment
Understand that if the muhrim wears and removes the garment with intention to return, the penalty does not multiply; if he intends not to return, it multiplies. This shows that intention affects the continuity of the action.
3
Examine the second furu‘: trustee wearing trust garment
The trustee remains liable if he intends to wear it again. His liability continues because the act is incomplete due to his intention to return.
4
Derive the general principle
Conclude that in Hanafi law, mere intention without a physical act does not create liability. The act must be complete or incomplete depending on the accompanying intention.

وأما الصِّمَانُ فَهَلْ يَتَرَتْبُ فِي شَيْءٍ بِمُجَرَّدِ البِيَّةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ فِعْلٍ فَقَالُوْا فِي الْمُحْرِمِ إِذَا لَبِسَ ثَوْباً ثُمَّ نَزَعَهُ وَمِنْ قَصْدِهِ أَن يَعُودَ إِلَيْهِ لَا يَتَعَدَّدُ الْجَزَاء وَإِنْ قَصَدَ أَنْ لَّا يَعُوْدُ إِلَيْهِ تَعَدَّدَ الْجَزَاء بِأَيْسِهِ وَقَالُوا فِي الْمُؤدَعِ إِذَا لَبِسَ ثَوْبَ الْوَدِيْعَةِ ثُمَّ تَزَعَهُ وَمِنْ بَيْتِهِ أَنْ يَعُوْدَ إِلَى لُبْسِهِ لَمْ يَبْرَءَ مِنَ الصِّمَانِ. ترجمہ : اور بہر حال ضمان تو کیا وہ کسی چیز میں بغیر فعل کے محض نیت سے مرتب ہو جاتا ہے تو فقہاء محرم کے بارے میں فرماتے ہیں کہ جب اس نے کوئی کپڑا پہنا اور پھر اسے نکال دیا اور اس کا ارادہ یہ ہو کہ وہ اس کی طرف لوٹے گا تو جزا متعدد نہ ہو گی اور اگر اس کی طرف نہ لوٹنے کا ارادہ کیا تو اس کے پہنے سے جزا متعدد ہوگی اور موذغ کے بارے میں فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں کہ جب ودیعت کا کپڑا پہنا پھر اس کو نکال دیا اور اس کی نیت دوبارہ اس کے پہنے کی ہے تو ضمان سے بری نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح : ضمان کا ترتب نیت اور فعل میں سے صرف فعل پر ہے نیت پر نہیں اس کو مثال سے سمجھ لیجئے فقہاء کرام فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنے کا ارادہ کیا لیکن پہنا نہیں تو اس پر دم واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ ضمان کا ترتب بدون عمل محض نیت پر نہیں ہوتا اور اگر محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا پورے دن پہنے رکھا تو عندا تخمین اس پر دم واجب ہو گیا پھر ان کنگال کر پینے کا ارادہ کیا لیکن پہنا نہیں تو صرف سہنے کے ارادہ سے دو بار و دم واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر دوبارہ پھر پہن لیا تو دوبارہ دم واجب ہو جائے گا خواہ اس نے دوبارہ پہننے کا ارادہ کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو۔ اگر پہلے دم کے ادا کرنے کے بعد محرم نے دوبارہ سلا ہوا کپڑا پہن لیا تو بالاتفاق دوسراوم بھی دینا پڑے گا اور اگر
And as for liability (daman), does it become established in anything by mere intention without action? So they said regarding the muhrim: when he wears a garment then removes it, and his intention is to return to it, the penalty (jaza') does not multiply; and if he intended not to return to it, the penalty multiplies by his wearing. And they said regarding the trustee (mudi'): when he wears a garment of the trust (wadi'ah) then removes it, and his intention is to return to its wearing, he is not free from liability. Translation: And in any case, does liability become established in anything by mere intention without action? So the jurists say regarding the muhrim: when he wore a garment and then removed it, and his intention was to return to it, the penalty does not become multiplied; and if he intended not to return to it, the penalty becomes multiplied by his wearing. And regarding the trustee: when he wears the garment of the trust, then removes it, and his intention is to return to its wearing, he is not free from liability. Explanation: The establishment of liability is based on action, not intention. Understand it with an example: The noble jurists say that if a muhrim intended to wear a sewn garment but did not wear it, then no blood (dam) is obligatory upon him, because liability is not established without action based on mere intention. And if a muhrim wore a sewn garment for a whole day, then according to estimation, a blood becomes obligatory upon him. Then he intended to wear it again but did not wear it, then merely by the intention to wear, a second blood does not become obligatory. And if he wore it again, then a second blood becomes obligatory, whether he intended to wear it again or not. If after paying the first blood, the muhrim wore a sewn garment again, then by consensus he must give a second blood also.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi legal rule: liability (daman) and penalties (jaza') are incurred by actions, not by mere intentions. The author first poses the general question, then provides two illustrative cases. The first case involves a muhrim (one in ihram) who wears a prohibited sewn garment and then removes it. If he intends to wear it again, the penalty does not multiply because the removal with intention to return means he has not fully separated from the prohibited act. But if he intends never to return to it, the penalty multiplies because each instance of wearing is considered separate. The second case involves a trustee (mudi') who wears a garment entrusted to him and then removes it, intending to wear it again; he remains liable (does not become free from liability) because the intention to return indicates the act of wearing is not complete. The commentary clarifies that no penalty is incurred if only the intention exists without the act (e.g., intending to wear but not wearing). The rule is a direct application of the maxim 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' but here the focus is on the necessity of an external act for legal consequences in the realm of daman. The Hanafi position emphasizes that the law takes into account actions, not mere internal resolve, in matters of liability and penal obligations.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability; financial or penal responsibility arising from a wrongful act.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty, especially for violations during ihram, such as sacrificing a sheep (dam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A trustee (mudi‘) wears the entrusted garment, removes it, and intends to wear it again later. According to the Hanafi qawida in this lesson, which of the following is true?
A) He is free from liability because he removed the garment.
B) He remains liable because his intention to return indicates the act of wearing is not complete.
C) He is liable only if he actually wears it again.
D) He is guilty of a sin but no financial liability.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability (daman) and penalties (jaza') require an external act; mere intention, even if firm, does not suffice to incur financial or penal responsibility.

Effect of Intention on Recitation in Janazah and Behind Imam
Explains when intention transforms Quran recitation into dhikr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida of intention and mahall to determine when recitation of Quran transforms into dhikr in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Intention can change recitation to dhikr only in places not prescribed for Quran recitation.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates a key principle: the legal classification of an act depends on both intention (niyyah) and context (mahall). In Hanafi fiqh, reciting the Quran in its proper place (e.g., during prayer when one is not following an imam) remains Quran regardless of intention. However, in a place where recitation is not prescribed (like janazah prayer), intending dhikr transforms the recitation into dhikr, making it permissible. Conversely, in regular prayer behind the imam, silence is required, so recitation is prohibited even if one intends dhikr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing qawida
Recognize that the passage applies the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are by intentions) but with the conditioning factor of mahall (context). The sub-maxim here is: recitation in its proper place is unaffected by intention; recitation outside that place can become dhikr by intention.
This is a sughra (minor) qawida under the kubra (major) maxim.
2
Define mahall al-qira'ah
Mahall al-qira'ah refers to the context where Quran recitation is legally prescribed as an act of worship, such as during the standing in prayers that have ruku' and sujud (i.e., regular salah). In such contexts, recitation is required and remains Quran regardless of intention.
Janazah prayer is not a mahall for recitation; it is a mahall for dhikr and dua.
3
Apply to janazah prayer
Since janazah is a place for dhikr, if a follower recites Surah al-Fatihah with the intention of dhikr, the recitation exits from being Quran and becomes dhikr, making it permissible. The act is not considered recitation of Quran, which is not prescribed here.
If the follower recited with the intention of Quran recitation, it would be makruh or invalid because it is not the prescribed place.
4
Apply to regular prayer behind imam
In regular prayer (with ruku' and sujud), the follower is required to remain silent during the imam's audible recitation. Even if the follower intends dhikr, reciting the Quran is prohibited because the context demands silence. The mahall here is one where recitation is prescribed, but for the follower, it is a place of silence.
The prohibition applies regardless of intention because silence (insat) is wajib for the muqtadi.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In janazah, reciting with dhikr intention is permissible; in regular prayer behind imam, it is prohibited. A mufti must distinguish between the two contexts when issuing a fatwa.
This illustrates how context overrides intention in some cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں نیت کرنے سے بھی وہ قرآت قرآن ہی رہے گی کیونکہ یہاں قرآن اپنے محل میں پڑھا جا رہا ہے لہذا نیت اور عزم کے بدلنے سے بھی اس پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑیگا ہاں البتہ اگر قرآت قرآن غیر محل قرآت میں ہو تو نیت ذکر سے قرآن قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے۔

وقالوا ان الماموم اذا قرأ الفاتحة : نماز جنازہ میں قرآت قرآن مشروع نہیں بلکہ ذکر و دعا مشروع ہے اس لئے فقہا، کہتے ہیں اگر مقتدی نماز جنازہ میں ذکر کی نیت سے سورہ فاتحہ پڑھے تو ممنوع نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قرآت غیر محل میں کر کی نیت سے وہ قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا نماز جنازہ میں ذکر کی نیت سے جائز ہوگا نوع نہیں نماز جنازہ میں قرآت قرآن غیر مشروع ہے اور اگر قراتها في الصلاة “ میں صلوٰۃ سے رکوع وسجدہ والے نماز مراد ہوتو مقتدی کے لئے رکوع وسجود میں امام کے پیچھے قرآت قرآن ممنوع ہے خواہ ذکر کا قصد ہو یا قرآت قرآن جن میں خاموش رہنا مطلوب ہے بخلاف نماز جنازہ اس لئے کہ وہ محل دعا ہے اور محل قرآت نہیں ہے اگر چہ قرآت نماز جنازہ میں امام کے پیچھے دعاء کی نیت سے جائز ہے۔
The answer to this is that here even with intention it will still be recitation of the Quran because here the Quran is being recited in its proper place, so changing intention and resolve does not affect it. However, if the recitation of the Quran is in a place not meant for recitation, then by intending dhikr it exits from being Quran recitation. And they said: When the follower recites al-Fatihah: In the funeral prayer, recitation of the Quran is not prescribed; rather dhikr and supplication are prescribed. Therefore, the jurists say: If a follower in the funeral prayer recites Surah al-Fatihah with the intention of dhikr, it is not prohibited because reciting in a non-place [for recitation] and by intention it exits from being Quran recitation. Hence, reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the funeral prayer with the intention of dhikr is permissible. This is not the case if it is recitation in the prayer of bowing and prostration; for the follower, reciting the Quran behind the imam during bowing and prostration is prohibited, whether the intention is dhikr or Quran recitation, because silence is required there. Contrary to the funeral prayer, because that is a place for supplication and not a place for recitation, even though recitation in the funeral prayer behind the imam with the intention of supplication is permissible.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage introduces a key principle: the legal classification of an act can be changed by intention and context. The author distinguishes between reciting Quran in its proper place (e.g., during prayer when one is not following an imam) and reciting in a place where it is not prescribed (like janazah prayer). In the latter, if one intends dhikr, the recitation legally becomes dhikr, not Quran recitation, and thus is permissible. However, in regular prayer behind an imam, the follower is required to remain silent during the imam's loud recitation; even if the follower intends dhikr, actually reciting the Quran would violate this requirement and is therefore prohibited. The reasoning is based on the 'mahal' (locus) of the act: janazah is a place for dhikr and dua, not for Quran recitation as a prescribed act of worship.

Key Terms
محل قرآن (mahall al-qira'ah): The place or context where Quran recitation is legally prescribed as an act of worship (e.g., in prayer at appropriate times).
مقتدی (muqtadi): A follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a follower in the funeral prayer recites Surah al-Fatihah with the intention of dhikr?
A) It is prohibited because reciting Quran in prayer is always required.
B) It is permissible because his intention turns it into dhikr.
C) It is invalid because he must recite silently.
D) It is makruh because he should not recite in janazah.

Key Takeaway
Intention transforms recitation into dhikr only when the context is not a prescribed place for Quran recitation; otherwise, the context overrides intention.

Liability Attaches to Action, Not Mere Intention
Explains that liability (daman) requires action; intention alone does not incur liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'liability attaches to action, not intention' to determine dam liability in cases of ihram violations and deposits, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute on tadakhul.

Core Idea
Liability requires action; intention alone does not incur obligation.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi qawida that distinguishes between mere intention and actual action. Through examples from ihram violations and deposits, you will see how liability is strictly attached to action. You will also examine a nuance where intention affects multiplicity of penalty and an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the governing qawida
Identify the main principle: liability (daman) is based on action, not intention. This is the central rule that governs all furuat.
2
Identify the scope and exceptional cases
The qawida applies to all chapters involving liability, especially ihram violations and deposits. Note the istithna' where intention does affect multiplicity when removal completes the violation.
3
Work through the furuat
Apply the qawida to the two main cases: the muhrim and the depositary. For each, determine the ruling based on action vs. intention.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on whether multiple violations before payment require separate penalties. Understand the basis of tadakhul.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
Determine which position is mufta bihi and how a mufti should handle the ikhtilaf in practice.

يَتَعَدَّدُ الْجَزَاء وَإِنْ قَصَدَ أَنْ لَّا يَعُوْدُ إِلَيْهِ تَعَدَّدَ الْجَزَاء بِأَيْسِهِ وَقَالُوا فِي الْمُؤدَعِ إِذَا لَبِسَ ثَوْبَ الْوَدِيْعَةِ ثُمَّ تَزَعَهُ وَمِنْ بَيْتِهِ أَنْ يَعُوْدَ جب ودیعت کا کپڑا پہنا پھر اس کو نکال دیا اور اس کی نیت دوبارہ اس کے پہنے کی ہے تو ضمان سے بری نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح : ضمان کا ترتب نیت اور فعل میں سے صرف فعل پر ہے نیت پر نہیں اس کو مثال سے سمجھ لیجئے دوبارہ کپڑا پہننے کی وجہ سے دوسرا دم لازم ہو گیا تو ابی حنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں دم ادا کرنے ضروری ہوں گے جب کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک ایک ہی دم کافی ہوگا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم میں تداخل ہے۔ وقالوافي المودع . ودیعت کی حفاظت اپنے سامان کی حفاظت کی طرح ضروری ہے ورنہ تعدی پائے جانے کی صورت میں مورع پر تاوان ضروری ہوگا۔ فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے کسی کے پاس بطور ودیعت کوئی کپڑا رکھا۔ اور مودع نے وہ کپڑا پہن لیا اور پھر کوئی کمی اور نقص پیدا ہوئے بغیر اس کپڑے کو اتار کر حفاظت سے رکھدیا اور اس کے بعد وہ کپڑ ا ضائع ہو گیا یا اس میں نقص پیدا ہو گیا تو موزع پر ضمان نہیں ہے لیکن اگر کپڑا پہننے کی صورت میں وہ کپڑا ہلاک ہو گیا یا نقص پیدا ہو گیا یا کپڑا پہنا اور پھر اتار کر رکھ دیا اور دوبارہ اس کپڑے کو پہنچنے کا ارادہ ہے اور ان دونوں صورتوں میں اگر اس کپڑے میں کوئی نقص پیدا ہو گیا یا ضائع ہو گیا تو مودع ضمان سے برتی نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اتار کر رکھدینے کی صورت میں بھی چونکہ اس کا ارادہ پہننے کا ہے تو یہ سمجھا جائے گا کہ گویا وہ پہنے ہوئے ہی ہے تو چونکہ اس کی طرف سے تعدی پائی گئی اور اگر تعدی پائی جانے کی صورت میں ودیعت میں نقص پیدا ہو جائے یا ہلاک ہو جائے تو ضمان واجب ہو جاتا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی دو ضمان سے بری نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
And as for liability, does it become established in anything by mere intention without action? They said concerning the muhrim: if he wears a garment then removes it, and his intention is to return to it, there is no multiplicity of penalty; but if he intends not to return to it, then the penalty is multiplied by his wearing. And they said concerning the depositary: if he wears the garment of deposit then removes it, and his intention is to return to its wearing, he is not free from liability. Translation: And as for liability, does it become established in anything by mere intention without action? The jurists say concerning the muhrim: when he wears a garment then removes it, and his intention is to return to it, the penalty is not multiplied; but if he intended not to return to it, then the penalty is multiplied by his wearing. And concerning the depositary, the jurists say: when he wears the deposited garment then removes it, and his intention is to wear it again, he is not free from liability. Elaboration: Liability is attached only to action, not to intention. Understand this with an example: The jurists say that if a muhrim intends to wear a stitched garment but does not wear it, no dam is wajib upon him, because liability is not attached to mere intention without action. And if the muhrim wears a stitched garment for the whole day, then according to estimation, a dam becomes wajib. Then he intends to wear it again but does not wear it, no second dam is wajib by mere intention. If he wears it again, then a second dam becomes wajib, whether he intended to wear it again or not. If after paying the first dam the muhrim again wears the stitched garment, then by agreement a second dam must be given. And if he has not yet paid the first dam and a second dam becomes necessary due to wearing the garment again, then according to Abu Hanifa, both dams are necessary, whereas according to Imam Muhammad, one dam is sufficient because in his view there is tadakhul (overlap) in dam. And they said concerning the depositary: protecting the deposit is necessary like protecting one's own property; otherwise, if transgression is found, the depositary is liable. The jurists say: If a person deposits a garment with someone, and the depositary wears it, then without any loss or defect removes it and keeps it safely, and thereafter the garment is lost or damaged, then the depositary is not liable. But if the garment is destroyed while being worn, or damaged, or he wears it, removes it, and intends to wear it again, and in either case the garment is lost or damaged, then the depositary is not free from liability, because even after removing it, since he intends to wear it again, he is considered as if still wearing it. Since he committed transgression, if loss or damage occurs, liability becomes wajib. So in that case he is not free from liability; rather liability is wajib upon him.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage establishes a key qawida: liability (daman) is based on action, not mere intention. It applies this to two areas: (1) The muhrim who wears prohibited stitched clothing: if he wears and removes it, intending to wear again, no second penalty is incurred until he actually wears it again. But if he intended never to wear it again, his removal itself constitutes completion of the act, so penalty is incurred. (2) The depositary who wears a deposited garment: if he wears it, removes it, but intends to wear again, he is still considered in a state of transgression, so if the garment is later lost/damaged, he is liable. The passage also notes a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding multiple penalties when the first has not been paid: Abu Hanifa requires both, while Imam Muhammad holds that overlapping penalties are merged into one. This dispute is based on the principle of tadakhul.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensatory responsibility, often financial, arising from an action that causes loss or violates a prohibition.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, subject to specific prohibitions.
تداخل (tadakhul): Overlap or merging of multiple obligations into one due to similarity or connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida discussed, if a muhrim intends to wear stitched clothing but does not actually wear it, what is the ruling?
A) He must pay a dam because of his intention.
B) He does not have to pay a dam because liability requires action.
C) He must pay a dam only if he intends to wear it again.
D) He must pay half a dam.

Key Takeaway
Liability in Hanafi fiqh requires an action; intention alone does not obligate, but intention can affect the multiplicity or continuity of liability.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
beginner
6 min
Intention Not Required for Refraining from Prohibitions
Explaining the rule that refraining from a prohibition needs no intention; reward conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule 'refraining from a prohibited act does not require intention' and identify the conditions for earning reward when refraining from sin.

Core Idea
You don't need intention to avoid sin; reward requires active resistance with ability and fear of Allah.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's 'al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair' explains a key Hanafi legal maxim: mere cessation from a prohibited act fulfills the obligation without intention. However, earning divine reward is conditional—it requires the person to have desire and ability, yet consciously refrain out of fear of Allah. This distinction clarifies that not all acts of leaving a sin are equal in the sight of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between obligation and reward
The rule has two parts: (a) fulfilling the prohibition requires no intention; (b) earning reward requires kaff (restraint) with ability and fear. Recognize that these are separate inquiries.
2
Analyze the examples of no reward
Examine the three examples: a person praying refrains from zina (occupied with prayer), an impotent man, and a blind man. Identify the missing condition—either lack of desire/ability or lack of active restraint.
Each example illustrates a different reason for no reward.
3
Understand the exception (istithna')
When a person has desire and ability but restrains out of fear, that active restraint (kaff) is an act of the heart (fi'l al-nafs) earning reward. This is supported by Quranic and hadith evidence.
The exception does not invalidate the general rule; it clarifies a different scenario.
4
Connect to the broader qawida framework
This rule is a dabt (sub-maxim) restricting the scope of the major qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'. It governs how prohibitions are fulfilled and when reward is granted.
5
Apply the rule to new furuat
Given a new situation (e.g., a person refrains from backbiting while alone), determine whether the prohibition is fulfilled and whether reward is due based on ability, desire, and motive.

Source Text

الْوُضُوءِ۔ وَحَاصِلُهُ أَنَّ تَرْك الْمَنْهِي عَنْهُ لَا يَحْتَاجُ إلَى نِيَّةِ لِلْحُرُوج عَنْ عُهْدَةِ النّهى۔ ترجمہ : اور بہر حال تروک جیسے منہی عنہ کا ترک تو فقہاء نے اصول میں ان چیزوں کی بحث میں فَإِنْ كَانَ كَفَّا وَهُوَ أنْ تَدْعُوهُ النَّفْسُ إِلَيْهِ قَادِرًا عَلَىٰ فِعْلِهِ فِيكُتُ نفْسَهُ عَنْهُ خَوْفًا مَنْ رَّبِّهِ فَهُوَ مُثَابُ وَإِلَّا فَلَا ثَوَابَ عَلَىٰ تَرْكِهِ فَلَا يُتَابُ نماز پڑھنے کی حالت میں مصلی زنا سے رکا ر ہے تو ترک زنا پر واب مرتب نہ ہو گا اسی طرح منین کو ترک زنا پر ثواب نہ ملے گا اس لئے کہ اس کے اندر زنا کی قدرت ہی نہیں البتہ ہویں وکنار کی اس کو قدرت ہے اگر مواقع حاصل ہونے کے باوجود اپنے اختیار سے بوس و کنار سے رکا رہے تو اس کو پر ثواب حاصل ہوگا اسی طرح اگر کوئی نا بینا غیر محرم پر نظر ڈالنے سے رکا ہے تو اس کو بھی ثواب نہ ملے گا اس لئے کہ کرم پر نظر ڈالنے کی اس کے اندر قدرت ہی نہیں۔
And as for [things left (tark)] like leaving a prohibited act, they mentioned it in Usul under the discussion of what causes the reality to be left, when commenting on the hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat', and they mentioned it in the intention for wudu. The summary is that leaving a prohibited act does not require intention to exit from the obligation of the prohibition. Commentary: Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that for the servant to exit from the responsibility of refraining from what he is prohibited from doing, intention is not required, nor is there reward or punishment for refraining, because reward is for performing an act or leaving an act of command, and the prohibition relates to leaving, which is not an act required. Therefore, intention is not needed to exit responsibility. For reward: if it is a restraint (kaff) – that is, the soul incites him and he is able to do it, and he restrains himself out of fear of his Lord, then he is rewarded. Otherwise, there is no reward for leaving it. Thus, there is no reward for leaving zina while he is praying, nor for the impotent man leaving zina, nor for the blind man leaving looking at the forbidden. Commentary: It has been established that refraining from prohibitions does not require intention. However, if a person's nature inclines towards sins and he has full opportunities and ability, but he refrains out of fear of Allah, he will be rewarded. If he lacks ability, there is no reward. If one objects that reward is for acts, and leaving is not an act, the answer is that there are acts of the limbs and acts of the soul. When the soul incites to sin and one has ability but restrains his soul, that is an act of the soul, so reward is given. Evidence: Quran: 'Inna qawmi ittakhadhu hadha al-Qur'ana mahjuran' and the hadith of Abu Hudhayfa al-Suwa'i: 'Which deed is best? They were silent, so he said: Guarding the tongue.' These indicate that the soul also has acts like the limbs. Therefore, he is not rewarded for leaving zina while praying, nor the impotent for leaving zina, nor the blind for leaving looking at non-mahram because he lacks ability.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage, citing Ibn Nujaym, establishes a key principle in Hanafi usul: refraining from a prohibited act does not require intention to fulfill the prohibition. The reason is that the prohibition demands mere cessation, which is not an act requiring intention. However, reward (thawab) for leaving a sin is conditional: one must have the ability and desire to commit it but consciously refrain out of fear of Allah. This is considered an act of the heart (fi'l al-nafs). The passage provides examples: a person praying who refrains from zina gets no reward because his prayer occupies him; an impotent man (who cannot commit zina) gets no reward; a blind man who cannot see gets no reward for not looking at non-mahram. But if a person has desire and ability and refrains, he earns reward. The proof from Quran and Hadith shows that acts of the heart are recognized deeds.

Key Terms
ترک (tark): The act of leaving or refraining from an action, specifically a prohibited act in this context.
نیت (niyyah): Intention, which is required for acts of worship but not for mere refraining from prohibitions according to this rule.
ثواب (thawab): Divine reward, earned for acts of obedience, including heart acts like conscious refraining from sin when able.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which person earns no reward for refraining from zina?
A) A person who has the power and desire but refrains out of fear
B) A person who is praying and refrains from zina
C) A person who has no desire but full ability
D) A person who refrains but does not fear Allah

Key Takeaway
Refraining from a prohibited act fulfills the obligation without intention; reward requires active restraint with ability, desire, and fear of Allah.
