اسی طرح چوکیدار اگر جاگنے کی اطلاع دینے کے لئے کلمہ طیبہ وغیر ہ پڑھتا ہے اگر چہ کلمہ طیبہ پڑھتا ہو کی فضیلت کی بات ہے اور اس پر اجر و ثواب ہے لیکن چوکیدار کا قصد وارادہ کلمہ پڑھنے سے حصول تو اب نہیں ہے بلکہ لوگوں کو اپنے جاگنے کی اطلاع دینا مقصود ہے۔ لہذا بے محل کلمہ پڑھنے کی وجہ سے گناہ گار ہوگا۔
بخلاف العَالِم إِذَا قَالَ فِي الْمَجْلِسِ : صَلُّوا عَلَى النَّبِيِّ، فَإِنَّهُ يُقَابُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ وَكَذَا الْغَازِي إِذَا قَالَ: كَبْرُوْا يُقَابُ؛ لأنَّ الْحَارِسَ وَالْفَقَاعِي يَأْخُذَانِ بِذَلِكَ أَجْرًا. ترجمه: بخلاف عالم کے جب مجلس میں کہے نبی پر درود شریف پڑھو تو اس پر ثواب دیا جائے گا اور ایسے کے غازی جب کے تکبیر پڑھو تو ثواب دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ حارس اور فقاعی اس پر اجرت لیتے ہیں۔ تشریح : او پر جو مسئلے ذکر کئے گئے تھے یہ دونوں مسئلے ان کے برعکس ہیں کہ کسی عالم نے مجلس وعظ میں لوگوں سے درود شریف پڑھنے کے لئے کہا تو اسے اس پر ثواب ملے گا کیونکہ اس کا یہ عمل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی تعلیم کے پیش نظر ہے اور کسی دنیوی مفاد کے لئے بھی نہیں ہے اور بے محل بھی نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی شخص میدان جہاد میں مجاہدین کو جوش دلانے کے لئے نعرہ تکبیر کی صدا لگاتا ہے اور دوسروں سے بھی کہتا ہے تو اسے اس پر ثواب ملے گا۔ بخلاف العالم اذا قال في المجلس صلوا على النبي فانه
ثياب على ذلك او الغازى يقول كبروا حيث ثياب كذافي الكبیری (هندیه ج ۵ ص (۳۱۵) اس سے پہلے دو مسئلوں میں حارس اور فقائی کے صلوٰۃ اور کلمہ پڑھنے پر بجائے اجر و ثواب کے گناہ ملے گا اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں اس پر اجرت لیتے ہیں لیکن علامہ جموئی فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب کتاب نے گناہ کی جو علت بیان کا ہے وہ کمزور ہے ۔ بلکہ فقاعی والے مسئلہ میں گناہ کی علت اس صلوٰۃ سے شراب کو اچھا ہونے کو بتلاتا ہے اور جاری والے مسئلہ میں گناہ کی علت اس ذکر سے اپنے بیدار ہونے کی اطلاع دینا ہے گویا ان دونوں صورتوں میں مصلوة ) کلمہ طیبہ کا استعمال بے محل ہے اس لئے گناہ ہے۔
رَجُلٌ جَاءَ إِلَى الْبَزَّازِ لِيَشْتَرِى مِنْهُ ثَوْبًا، فَلَمَّا فَتَحَ الْمَتَاعَ قَالَ: سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ، أَوْقَالَ: اللَّهُمُ صَلَّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدِ إِنْ أَرَادَ بِذلِكَ إِعْلَامِ الْمُشْتَرِي جَوْدَةَ ثِيَابِهِ وَمَتَاعِهِ كُرِهَ، إِنْتِهَى ترجمه: ایک آدمی کپڑے کے تاجر کے پاس آیا تا کہ اس سے کپڑ ا خریدے پس جب اس نے سامان کو ان سبحان الله کہایا اللهم صلی علی محمد اگر اس نے اس سے خریدار کو اپنے کپڑے اور سامان کے اچھا ہو کی اطلاع دی تو مکروہ ہے قاضی خاں کا کلام پورا ہوا۔
تشریح کوئی خریدار کپڑے کے تاجر کے پاس کپڑ ا خریدنے کی نیت سے آتا ہے اور تا جر کپڑا دکھانے یا ساران دکھانے کے وقت اس کی اچھائی اور عمدگی بتانے کی غرض سے سبحان اللہ یا در و دو غیرہ پڑھتا ہے تو بے محل استعمال کرنے کا وجہ سے اس کا یہ عمل مکروہ ہو گا۔
من جاء الى تاجر يشترى منه ثوباً فلما فتح التاجر الثوب سبح الله تعالى او صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اراد به اعلام المشترى جودة ثوبه فذلک مکروه (هند به ج ۵ ص ۳۱۵) وَفِيْهَا أَيْضًا: إِذَاقَالَ الْمُسْلِمُ لِلذَّمّى: أَطَالَ اللهُ بَقَاءَكَ، قَالُوا: إِنْ نَوَى بِقَلْبِهِ أَنْ تُطِيْلَ اللهُ بَفَاءَ هُ لَعَلَّهُ أَنْ يُسْلِمَ، أَوْ يُؤدَى الْجِزْيَةَ عَنْ ذُلَّ وَصَغَارٍ لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا دُعَاءُ لَهُ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ أَوْلِمَنْفَعَةِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، إِنْتَهى.
:ترجمہ: اور نیز اسی میں ہے کہ جب مسلمان نے کسی ذمی سے کہا اللہ تیری عمر دراز کرے فقہا ، فرماتے ہیں اگر دل سے نیت کی کہ اللہ اس کی عمر دراز کرے شاید کہ یہ مسلمان ہو جائے یا ذلت ورسوائی کے ساتھ جز یہ دے تو کوئی حرج نہیں اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے لئے اسلام کی دعا کرنا ہے یا مسلمانوں کے فائدہ کی ، کلام پورا ہوا ۔ تشریح کوئی مسلمان کسی کا فر کولمبی عمر کی دعا دیتا ہے اور مقصد یہ ہے کہ اللہ اس کو اسلام کی ہدایت دیدے یا مقصد ہے کہ لمبی عمر ہوگی مسلمانوں کو جزیہ دے گا بیت المال کے خزانہ میں جمع ہو کر مسلمانوں کا فائدہ ہوگا تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور مقصد ہے جیسا مقصد ہوگا ویسا ہی حکم ہوگا الامور ہم مقاصد با قاعدہ مسلمہ ہے اس پر تفریعات پیش کی جارہی ہیں۔ ولو دعا له بطول العمر قيل يجوز لان فيه نفعاً للمسلمين بالجزية وقيل لايجوز تكملة البحر الرائق ج/٣٧٣/٨)
لم قَالَ: رَجُلٌ أَمْسَكَ المُصْحَفِ فِي بَيْتِهِ وَلَا يَقْرَأُ، قَالُوا: إِنْ نَوَى بِهِ الخَيْرَ وَالْبَرَكَةَ لا يَأْتِمُ وَيُرْجَى لَهُ النواب.
:ترجمه: پھر کہا ایک آدمی نے قرآن اپنے گھر میں رکھا ہوا ہے اور پڑھتا نہیں ہے، فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں اگر اس سے خیر و برکت کی نیت کر رکھی ہے تو گنہ گار نہیں ہوگا اور اس کے لئے ثواب کی امید ہے بخلاف علمی کتابوں کے اس لئے کہ ان کی یہ شان نہیں ہے کہ ان سے خیر و برکت کی نیت کی جائے بغیر پڑھے ہوئے اس لئے دینی کتابوں کو روکنا حرام ہے خصوصا جبکہ وہ کتابیں وقف ہوں۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شخص گھر میں قرآن شریف رکھتا ہے اور تلاوت اس کی کرتا نہیں ہے البتہ اس کی نیت خیر و برکت کی ہے تو امید ہے کہ اس کے گھر میں خیر و برکت ہوگی اور وہ گنہ گار نہیں ہوگا۔
Similarly, if a watchman recites the kalimah tayyibah etc. to inform that he is awake, even though reciting the kalimah tayyibah is a virtuous act and there is reward upon it, but the watchman's intention and aim is not to attain reward, rather his purpose is to inform people that he is awake. Hence, due to reciting the kalimah in an inappropriate place, he will be sinful.
Contrary to a scholar when he says in a gathering: 'Send blessings upon the Prophet', for he is rewarded for that; and similarly a warrior when he says: 'Say Takbir', he is rewarded; because the watchman and the seller of nabidh [فَقَاعِي] take wages for that. Translation: Contrary to a scholar when he says in a gathering 'Send blessings upon the Prophet', he will be rewarded; and similarly a warrior when he says 'say Takbir', he will be rewarded, because the watchman and the seller of nabidh take wages for it. Explanation: These two issues are opposite to the previous issues mentioned. That a scholar in a preaching gathering asks people to send blessings upon the Prophet, he will be rewarded because his action is based on teaching the Sunnah and not for any worldly benefit, and it is not inappropriate. Similarly, if a person in the battlefield shouts the slogan of takbir to encourage the mujahidin and asks others to do so, he will be rewarded. Contrary to the scholar when he says in the gathering 'send blessings upon the Prophet' he is rewarded, and the warrior when he says 'say takbir' he is rewarded, as in al-Kabiri (Hindiyya vol. 5 p. 315). In the two previous issues, the watchman and the nabidh-seller will be sinful instead of reward for reciting salawat and kalimah, because they take wages for it. But 'Allamah Jamu'i says that the cause (illah) for sin which the author mentioned is weak. Rather, the cause for sin in the nabidh-seller's issue is that by this salawat he indicates that wine is good, and in the watchman's issue the cause for sin is that by this dhikr he informs of his being awake. In both cases, the use of salawat/kalimah tayyibah is inappropriate, so there is sin.
A man came to a cloth merchant to buy cloth from him. When he opened the merchandise, he said 'Subhanallah' or said 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'. If he intended thereby to inform the buyer of the excellence of his cloth and merchandise, it is disliked (makruh). End. Translation: A man came to a cloth merchant to buy cloth from him. When he opened the goods, he said 'Subhanallah' or 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'. If he intended thereby to inform the buyer of the excellence of his cloth and goods, it is disliked. The speech of Qadi Khan ends. Explanation: A buyer comes to a cloth merchant with the intention of buying cloth, and the merchant, when showing the cloth or goods, recites Subhanallah or durud etc. with the purpose of expressing its excellence and fineness, then due to inappropriate use, his action becomes disliked.
Whoever came to a merchant to buy cloth from him, when the merchant opened the cloth, he glorified Allah the Exalted or sent blessings upon the Prophet, intending thereby to inform the buyer of the excellence of his cloth, then that is disliked (Hindiyya vol. 5 p. 315). And also in it: When a Muslim says to a dhimmi: 'May Allah prolong your life', they said: If he intended in his heart that Allah may prolong his life, perhaps he may become Muslim, or he may pay the jizyah with humility and degradation, there is no harm, because this is supplication for him towards Islam, or for the benefit of the Muslims. End. Translation: And also in it: When a Muslim says to a dhimmi: 'May Allah prolong your life', the jurists said: If he intended in his heart that Allah prolong his life, perhaps he may become Muslim, or he may pay jizyah with humility and degradation, there is no harm, because this is supplication for him towards Islam, or for the benefit of the Muslims. The speech ends. Explanation: A Muslim supplicates for long life for a disbeliever, and the purpose is that Allah may guide him to Islam, or the purpose is that he would have a long life, he would give jizyah, it would be collected in the bait al-mal and benefit the Muslims, then there is no harm. And if there is any other purpose, the ruling will be according to that purpose, as the established maxim is 'actions are judged by intentions'; furu' are being presented on this. And if one prays for long life for him, it is said it is permissible because there is benefit for the Muslims in the jizyah, and it is said it is not permissible. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 8 p. 373)
Then he said: A man kept the Mushaf in his house and does not recite it. They said: If he intended good and blessing by it, he does not sin and reward is hoped for him. Translation: Then he said: A man has placed the Quran in his house and does not recite it. The jurists said: If he intended good and blessing by it, he will not be sinful and reward is hoped for him, contrary to scholarly books, because they do not have this status that good and blessing be intended without reading them; hence withholding religious books is prohibited, especially when those books are waqf. Explanation: If a person keeps the Holy Quran in his house and does not recite it, but his intention is for good and blessing, then it is hoped that there will be good and blessing in his house and he will not be sinful.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe of the foundational maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). It presents several furuat (applications) from fiqh texts like al-Hindiyya, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and Qadi Khan, demonstrating how the ruling of an utterance or action changes based on the underlying intention, not merely its literal wording.

The first set of examples contrasts two scenarios: a watchman who recites the kalimah to signal he is awake, and a scholar who asks people to send salawat in a gathering. The watchman's recitation, though a virtuous dhikr, is deemed sinful because his intent is worldly notification, not worship. The scholar, on the other hand, is rewarded because his intent is to teach the Sunnah. Similarly, a warrior shouting takbir to encourage mujahidin is rewarded. The text notes a critique by 'Allamah Jamu'i regarding the cause for sin; he refines it: the sin is not merely due to taking wages, but because the dhikr is used in an inappropriate context (for worldly purposes).

The second furu' involves a cloth merchant saying 'Subhanallah' or 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' to indicate the quality of his goods. This is ruled makruh (disliked) because the words of worship are used for commercial advertisement, which is improper.

The third furu' addresses a Muslim praying for a dhimmi's long life. If the intention is hope for his Islam or benefit to Muslims through jizyah, it is permissible. If the intention is worldly affection or other, the ruling changes accordingly.

The final furu' discusses keeping a Mushaf in the house without recitation. If the intention is seeking barakah, it is permissible and reward is hoped for, unlike other religious books which are meant to be read; withholding them (especially if waqf) is prohibited.

Throughout, the author demonstrates that the maxim governs rulings across ibadat, mu'amalat, and even social interactions. The common thread is that the fiqh of speech acts depends on the intended meaning and context, not the literal utterance.

Key Terms
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umur bi maqasidiha): The legal maxim that the ruling of an action is determined by the intention behind it, not its outward form.
فروع (furu'): Specific legal cases derived from and illustrating the application of a general maxim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the watchman sinful for reciting the kalimah?
A) Because he is a watchman and not a scholar.
B) Because he recites it loudly, disturbing others.
C) Because his intention is to inform people he is awake, not to worship.
D) Because he is paid for reciting it.

Key Takeaway
The same virtuous words can be sinful, rewardable, disliked, or permissible depending entirely on the intention.

Keeping Quran Without Recitation: Intention Determines Ruling
Ruling on keeping a Quran without reciting depends on intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to the case of keeping a Quran without reciting and state the ruling according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Intention of blessing makes keeping a Quran permissible; mere decoration or neglect may be sinful.

This lesson applies the foundational Islamic legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions) to a specific everyday scenario: a person keeps a physical copy of the Quran in their home but does not recite from it. The Hanafi jurists clarify that the ruling depends on the person's intention. Understanding this application helps a mufti navigate similar cases where an act's permissibility hinges on the actor's purpose.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Identify the act: keeping a mushaf in the house without reciting it. Recognize that the act is ambiguous in itself.
The Quran is not like ordinary books; its presence has inherent sanctity.
2
Identify the maxim
Recall the major qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' which classifies actions by their intentions. Here, the intention is the decisive factor.
This is a kubra (universal) maxim governing all fiqh chapters.
3
Analyze the intention
Consider two possibilities: intention of seeking blessing (barakah) vs. intention of mere decoration, neglect, or worldly purpose. The ruling differs accordingly.
The text explicitly mentions 'intending good and blessing'.
4
Derive the ruling for good intention
If the intention is to obtain barakah from the Quran's presence, the person is not sinful and reward is hoped for. This is due to the special veneration of the Quran.
The ruling is not that keeping is obligatory, but permissible and potentially rewarding.
5
Contrast with other books
Note the exception: secular books or even religious books that are not the Quran do not carry the same sanctity. Keeping them without use may be sinful, especially if they are waqf (endowed) and meant to be read.
This distinction reinforces the Quran's unique status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم قَالَ: رَجُلٌ أَمْسَكَ المُصْحَفِ فِي بَيْتِهِ وَلَا يَقْرَأُ، قَالُوا: إِنْ نَوَى بِهِ الخَيْرَ وَالْبَرَكَةَ لا يَأْتِمُ وَيُرْجَى لَهُ النواب.
:ترجمه: پھر کہا ایک آدمی نے قرآن اپنے گھر میں رکھا ہوا ہے اور پڑھتا نہیں ہے، فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں اگر اس سے خیر و برکت کی نیت کر رکھی ہے تو گنہ گار نہیں ہوگا اور اس کے لئے ثواب کی امید ہے بخلاف علمی کتابوں کے اس لئے کہ ان کی یہ شان نہیں ہے کہ ان سے خیر و برکت کی نیت کی جائے بغیر پڑھے ہوئے اس لئے دینی کتابوں کو روکنا حرام ہے خصوصا جبکہ وہ کتابیں وقف ہوں۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شخص گھر میں قرآن شریف رکھتا ہے اور تلاوت اس کی کرتا نہیں ہے البتہ اس کی نیت خیر و برکت کی ہے تو امید ہے کہ اس کے گھر میں خیر و برکت ہوگی اور وہ گنہ گار نہیں ہوگا۔
Then he said: A man kept a mushaf in his house and does not read it. They said: If he intends good and blessing by it, he is not sinful and reward is hoped for him.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage presents another furu of the intentions maxim. The question: a Muslim keeps a Quran in his home but does not recite it. The ruling: if his intention is to seek barakah (blessing) from the presence of the Quran, he is not sinful and may even hope for reward. The author contrasts this with secular or other religious books, which do not have the same status; keeping them without reading may be sinful, especially if they are waqf (endowed) books. This distinction is based on the special sanctity of the Quran. The ruling also implies that if one keeps the Quran for mere decoration or worldly reasons, it could be sinful.

Key Terms
مصحف (mushaf): A physical copy of the Quran
نية (niyyah): Intention, the purpose behind an act
بركة (barakah): Blessing, divine goodness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling if a person keeps a Quran in his house intending to receive blessings from it?
A) He is sinful because he does not read it.
B) He is not sinful and reward is hoped for him.
C) He is rewarded only if he reads it daily.
D) He must give the Quran in charity.

Key Takeaway
Keeping a Quran without reciting is permissible when the intention is to seek blessing; the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' is the key principle.

Dhikr in a Sinful Gathering: Intention Determines the Ruling
Ruling on dhikr in a sinful gathering depends on intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to distinguish when dhikr in a sinful gathering is praiseworthy or sinful, and construct a fatwa for a given scenario.

Core Idea
The ruling of dhikr in a sinful gathering hinges on intention: righteous opposition earns reward, mockery earns sin.

This passage examines a nuanced case: a person engaging in dhikr in a place of sin. The ruling is not absolute; it pivots on the intention behind the act. Understanding how the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies here sharpens your ability to evaluate actions that mix apparent piety with a sinful context.

Guided Path
1
State the governing maxim
Identify the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). This is one of the five major (kubra) qawaid and governs the entire fiqh.
It applies here because the same act (dhikr) can be ruling-wise best or sinful solely based on intention.
2
Identify the furu' case
The case is performing dhikr in a gathering of fisq (sin). Two possible intentions lead to two different rulings.
The text from Fatawa Hindiyya warns that even normally rewarded acts like tasbih can become sinful if done with awareness of possible mockery.
3
Apply the maxim to the first intention
If the person intends to engage in dhikr while others sin, as a form of righteous opposition, the act is best (afdal) and better than dhikr alone elsewhere.
4
Apply the maxim to the second intention
If the person intends to mock or show off, or is aware that the dhikr might be perceived as mocking, the act becomes sinful.
The intention corrupts the act; the same physical action becomes haram.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling for fatwa is that the intention must be examined. The default is not to assume bad intention; one should advise the person to check his heart.
This aligns with the maxim's emphasis on inward states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَالَ: رَجُلٌ يَذْكُرُ الله فِي مَجْلِسِ الْفِسْقِ، قَالُوا: إِنْ نَوَى أَنَّ الْفَسَقَةَ يَشْتَعِلُونَ بالفسق، وأنا أشتغل بالذكر، فهو أفضل وأحْسَنُ.
ترجمه پھر کہا ایک آدمی فسق و فجور کی محفل میں ذکر اللہ کرتا ہے فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں اگر نیت کی کہ فساق فق میں مشغول ہیں اور میں ذکر میں مشغول ہوں تو یا افضل اور بہتر ہے۔

Then he said: A man remembers Allah in a gathering of sin. They said: If he intends that the sinners are occupied with sin, and I am occupied with dhikr, then it is best and most beautiful.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of intention determining the ruling. A man performs dhikr in a gathering of sin. If his intention is to engage in dhikr while others are sinning, indicating his opposition and piety, then this is better than doing dhikr elsewhere. However, if his intention is to mock or show off, or if he is aware that his action may be interpreted as mockery, it becomes sinful. The author quotes from Fatawa Hindiyya: some speech that normally earns reward, like tasbih and tahmid, when done in a sinful gathering with awareness of its potential for mockery or opposition, may become sinful.

Key Terms
فسق (fisq): Sinful disobedience to Allah's commands
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umur bi-maqasidiha): Actions are judged by intentions

B) When the intention is mockery or showing off.
C) When he recites loudly.
D) When he is not a faqih.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on dhikr in a sinful gathering is not monolithic; it depends entirely on the intention: righteous opposition makes it best, mockery makes it sinful.

Tasbih in the Market: The Role of Intention (Niyyah)
Analysis of tasbih intentions using the major maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qa'ida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to different niyyah scenarios in a public act of dhikr and determine the ruling.

Core Idea
The same act of tasbih can be rewardable or sinful depending solely on intention.

This passage from Fatawa Hindiyya illustrates the living application of the great legal maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions.' It examines three niyyah scenarios for reciting tasbih in a market. Understanding this will sharpen your fatwa drafting by showing how a single act transforms under different qasd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the maxim
The act is reciting tasbih (SubhanAllah) in the market. The governing maxim is 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions).
2
Extract the three intentions
From the passage, list the three distinct intentions: (1) occupying oneself with dhikr while others are worldly, (2) admonition (i'tibar), (3) exposing the sin of a fasiq.
3
Map each intention to the ruling
For each intention, note the ruling: (1) better than solitary dhikr outside the market, (2) rewarded, (3) sinful.
4
Explain the legal reasoning
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' directly links the ruling to the intention. Good intentions yield reward; an intention to expose or show off corrupts the act and makes it sinful.
5
Generalize to other acts
Consider how this principle applies to other public acts of worship, such as giving charity openly or reciting Qur'an loudly. The ruling changes with the intention.

And if he recites tasbih by way of taking heed, he will be rewarded for it. And if he recites tasbih pointing out that the sinner is committing sin, he will be sinful.

Commentary
This passage from Fatawa Hindiyya (paraphrased) discusses three possible intentions for reciting tasbih in the market: (1) If one intends to occupy oneself with dhikr while others are busy with worldly things, this is excellent and better than solitary dhikr elsewhere. (2) If one recites tasbih in order to remind people and take heed, reward is expected. (3) If one recites tasbih to expose or highlight the sins of others (e.g., showing off one's piety in contrast), then it is sinful. The commentary clarifies that the first intention is commendable because it demonstrates piety in a public place. The second is for admonition. The third is sinful because it involves arrogance and exposing others' faults.

Key Terms
تسبيح (tasbih): Uttering 'SubhanAllah' to glorify Allah

C) When he intends to take heed.
D) When he intends that people are busy with worldly affairs.

Key Takeaway
Reciting tasbih in the market is not automatically good; the intention behind it determines whether it is excellent, rewardable, or sinful.

Prostrating to a Ruler: Intent of Respect, Not Worship
Ruling on prostration to a ruler depends on intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to distinguish between prostration as worship and prostration as respect, and derive the ruling accordingly.

Core Idea
Intention transforms a prohibited prostration to a human into a permissible gesture of respect.

Prostration is the ultimate act of worship due to Allah alone. But what if someone prostrates to a ruler? In this lesson, we examine a crucial ruling from the Hanafi tradition that hinges on intention. The maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions' (الأمور بمقاصدها) determines whether such prostration constitutes kufr or remains a permissible cultural gesture.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Identify the qawida: 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). This is one of the five major (kubra) maxims of Hanafi fiqh.
This maxim is universal and applies across all chapters.
2
Identify the scope of the maxim here
Recognize that this maxim governs rulings on worship and kufr. Prostration is an act that could be either, depending on intention.
The passage focuses on the distinction between worship (ibada) and respect (ta'zim).
3
Work through the furu' (application) of prostration
Apply the maxim: If a person prostrates to a ruler with the intention of greeting and respect (not worship), it is not kufr. The proof is from the angels’ prostration to Adam and Yusuf’s brothers.
The intention (niyya) is the decisive factor.
4
Note any istithna' (exception)
The passage does not mention an exception, but later Hanafi texts caution that this ruling applies only when prostration is culturally understood as a sign of respect and does not resemble worship.
Thus, in many contexts, such prostration is still discouraged (makruh).
5
Derive the fatwa hierarchy
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that prostration to a human with intention of respect is not kufr, but it is not recommended and should be avoided to prevent resemblance to idolatry.
This ruling is firmly based on the maxim and the prophetic precedents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنْ سَجَدَ لِلسُّلْطَانِ فَإِنْ كَانَ قَصْدَهُ التَّحِيَّةَ وَالتَّعْظِيمَ دُوْنَ الصَّلَاةِ لَايُكَفْرُ أضلهُ أَمْرُ الْمَلَائِكَةِ بِالسُّجُودِ لادَمَ وَسُجُوْدَ إِخْوَةِ يُوْسُفَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ.
ترجمه: پھر کہا اگر بادشاہ کوسجدہ کیا تو اگر تعظیم و تکریم مقصود ہے عبادت نہیں تو تکفیر نہیں کی جائے گی اس کی اصل آدم کے لئے فرشتوں کو سجدے کا حکم دینا اور یوسف علیہ السلام کے بھائیوں کا سجدہ کرنا ہے۔ تشریح : اگر بادشاہ یا کسی کو سجدہ تعظیم و توقیر کی نیت سے کیا گیا نہ کہ عبادت کی نیت سے تو موجب کفر نہ ہ
Then he said: If he prostrates to the ruler, and if his intention is greeting and respect, not worship, he is not declared a disbeliever. Its basis is the command for the angels to prostrate to Adam, and the prostration of Yusuf's brothers (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses a serious matter: prostration to a human ruler. The ruling is that if the prostration is intended purely as a gesture of respect and greeting, not as an act of worship, it does not constitute kufr (disbelief). The author cites two precedents: the angels' prostration to Adam (which was an act of respect commanded by Allah) and the brothers' prostration to Yusuf (which was a gesture of respect, not worship). Thus, intention distinguishes respect from worship. The commentary adds that if the intention is mere respect and honor, it is not kufr. However, many scholars caution that this is only valid in contexts where such prostration is culturally understood as respect, and even then, it is generally discouraged in most Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
سجود (sujud): Physical prostration, which can be worship or respect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the ruler is powerful.
B) Because the prostration was for greeting and respect, not worship.
C) Because it is following the Sunnah of Yusuf.
D) Because prostrating to a human is always permissible.

Key Takeaway
Intention is the decisive factor in determining whether prostration to a human constitutes kufr; respect and worship are distinct categories.

Dhikr in a Sinful Gathering: Intention Determines Ruling
Ruling on dhikr in a sinful gathering based on intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine the ruling of dhikr in a sinful gathering, identifying when it is virtuous and when it is sinful.

Core Idea
The same dhikr can be virtuous or sinful — intention and context decide the ruling.

In this lesson, we examine a classical ruling from Qazi Khan that illustrates the crucial role of intention (niyyah) in determining the legal and moral value of an action. Even an act of worship like dhikr can become blameworthy if done with a wrong intention or in a context that suggests mockery. This ruling is a direct application of the grand maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions), which is a cornerstone of Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Guided Path
1
State the governing maxim
Identify the primary qawida that applies: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). Recognize its rank as a kubra (major maxim) covering all fiqh chapters.
2
Identify the furu' case
The specific case is dhikr (remembrance of Allah) performed in a majlis al-fisq (gathering of sin). Note that the act itself is ordinarily virtuous, but the context and intention are critical.
3
Analyze the two possible intentions
From the passage, two intentions are contrasted: (1) intending to occupy oneself with dhikr while others are sinning, which is virtuous; (2) doing it with an element of mockery or showing off, which can be sinful.
4
Apply the maxim to derive the ruling
Using the maxim, the ruling follows from the intention. If the intention is pure and seeks to differentiate from sin, the act is virtuous. If the intention involves show-off or mockery, the act becomes sinful.
5
Note the caveat from later authorities
Al-Hindiyya adds that even tasbih and tahmid can be sinful in such a context if done with knowledge of the context, as it may imply mockery. This reinforces that the intention and context must be carefully assessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَالَ: رَجُلٌ يَذْكُرُ الله فِي مَجْلِسِ الْفِسْقِ، قَالُوا: إِنْ نَوَى أَنَّ الْفَسَقَةَ يَشْتَعِلُونَ بالفسق، وأنا أشتغل بالذكر، فهو أفضل وأحْسَنُ. الکلام منه ما يوجب اجراً كالتسبيح والتحميد اذا فعله في مجلس الفسق وهو يعلمه لما فيه من الاستهزاء والمخالفة - (هندیه ج ۵ ص ۳۱۵) وقد ياثم به
Then he said: A man who remembers Allah in a gathering of sin. They said: If he intends that the sinners are occupied with sin and I am occupied with remembrance, then it is better and more excellent. (From among speech is that which necessitates reward, like tasbih and tahmid, when done in a gathering of sin while knowing it, due to mockery and opposition - al-Hindiyya vol.5 p.315) And he may be sinful due to it.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Qazi Khan illustrating the maxim 'Actions are by intentions'. The ruling: if a person performs dhikr in a gathering of sin with the intention of distinguishing himself from the sinners, it is virtuous. However, if he does it with an awareness that it may appear as mockery or if his intention is to show his piety while others are sinning, it may be sinful. The Fatwa from al-Hindiyya adds that tasbih and tahmid in such a context may be sinful if it involves mockery. The key is the intention of the doer.

Key Terms
مجلس الفسق (majlis al-fisq): A gathering where sinful acts occur; the ruling of dhikr there depends on intention.
الذكر (al-dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, including tasbih, tahmid, etc.
نية (niyyah): Intention; the internal state that determines the moral and legal value of an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The act of dhikr itself is always virtuous regardless of context.
B) If the person intends to spite the sinners by doing dhikr.
C) If the person intends to occupy himself with dhikr while others are sinning.
D) If the gathering is clearly a gathering of fasiq (sinful).

Key Takeaway
The same act of dhikr can be virtuous or sinful depending on the intention and context; the Hanafi maxim al-umur bi-maqasidiha is applied to this furu' case.

Tasbih in the Market: Intention Matters
Ruling on tasbih in the market with various intentions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to classify tasbih in the market based on the doer's intention, distinguishing between rewarded and sinful intentions.

Core Idea
The same act of tasbih is judged by intention: sincere remembrance is virtuous, criticizing others is sinful.

This passage from Qazi Khan illustrates the Hanafi principle that intentions (niyyah) determine the moral and legal value of an act. Even an act of worship like tasbih can become sinful if done with a wrong intention. We explore three distinct intentions for tasbih in the market, each yielding a different ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the Arabic text and list the three distinct intentions mentioned for performing tasbih in the market. Note the ruling for each.
The intentions are: (1) intending that people are busy with dunya, (2) reflecting (i'tibar), (3) intending that sinners are sinning.
2
Extract the underlying qa'idah
Recognize that the passage exemplifies the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). Show how the same physical act (tasbih) takes different rulings based on niyyah.
This is a major (kubra) maxim in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the qa'idah to each scenario
For each intention, explain how the maxim produces the ruling: rewarded for sincere remembrance, rewarded for reflection, sinful for criticizing others.
The intention transforms the act from pure worship to a means of admonishment or pride.
4
Note the boundaries (istithna')
Identify that the maxim operates fully here, but note that when the intention is sinful, the act becomes sinful even though the outward act is tasbih.
This is not an exception to the maxim but an application: the intention is the decisive factor.
5
State the mufta bihi ruling
Conclude that in fatwa, the ruling depends on the confirmed intention. A mufti must inquire about the intention before issuing a ruling on tasbih in the market.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that actions are judged by intentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ سَبَّحَ فِي الْمُوْقِ نَاوِيَا أَنَّ النَّاسَ يَشْتَغِلُونَ بأمور الدُّنْيَا، وَأَنَا أُسَبِّحُ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِي هذَا الْمَوْضَع فَهُوَ أفْضَلُ وَأحْسَنُ مِنْ أنْ يُسَبِّحَ وَحْدَهُ فِي غَيْرِ السُّوْقِ وَإِنْ سَبَّحَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِعْتِبَارِ يُوجَرُ عَلى ذلِكَ، وَإِنْ سَبِّحَ عَلى أَنَّ الْفَاسِقَ يَعْمَلُ الْفِسْقَ كَانَ آثِما.
And if he glorifies Allah in the market intending that the people are occupied with worldly affairs and I am glorifying Allah in this place, then it is better and more excellent than if he glorifies alone outside the market. And if he glorifies by way of reflection, he is rewarded for that. And if he glorifies with the intention that the sinner is committing sin, then he is sinful.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Qazi Khan continues the theme of intentions. It gives three scenarios for tasbih in the market: (1) intending to engage in dhikr while people are busy with worldly matters – this is virtuous even more than doing tasbih alone elsewhere; (2) doing it for reflection (i.e., to take lesson) – this is rewarded; (3) doing it to highlight that people are sinners – this is sinful. The principle is that the same outward act is judged by its inner intention.

Key Terms
على وجه الاعتبار (ala wajh al-i'tibar): By way of reflecting/taking a lesson; this intention yields reward.
نية (niyyah): Intention; the inner purpose that determines the ruling of an act.
تسبيح (tasbih): Glorification of Allah, typically by saying 'SubhanAllah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does tasbih in the market become sinful according to the text?
A) When done aloud.
B) When done in a crowded place.
C) When done with the intention that the sinner is sinning.
D) When done alone.

Key Takeaway
Tasbih in the market is not inherently virtuous or sinful; its ruling depends entirely on the intention behind it.

Prostration to a Ruler: Intention and Compulsion
Ruling on prostration to a ruler: intention and compulsion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to the case of prostration to a ruler and derive the ruling under conditions of free will and compulsion.

Core Idea
Prostration to a ruler is haram not kufr if intended as greeting; under compulsion the ruling depends on the coercer's command.

This lesson examines a famous furu' case from the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). The prostration to a ruler is judged not by the external action alone but by the intention behind it. We will also explore how compulsion affects the ruling, applying the hierarchical structure of intentions and the principle of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing qawida
The passage applies the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha.' State it and explain that the ruling depends on the intention of the one prostrating.
This maxim is the first of the five major qawaid kubra.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios of free will
When not under compulsion, the ruling depends on the intention: if intended as worship (even if only greeting outwardly but inwardly worship), it is kufr; if intended purely as greeting/respect, it is haram but not kufr.
The evidence from the angels prostrating to Adam and Joseph's brothers shows prostration can be for respect.
3
Apply the compulsion rule
When compelled by threat of death, the coercer's command matters: if he commands prostration as worship, it is better to refuse and die (like refusing kufr); if as greeting, it is better to comply to save life.
This applies the principle of darurah (necessity) which overrides the normal prohibition.
4
Derive the furuat
List the practical outcomes: (1) Free will, greeting intention: haram, no kufr; (2) Free will, worship intention: kufr; (3) Compulsion, coercer commands worship: patience better; (4) Compulsion, coercer commands greeting: prostration better.
These furuat illustrate the nuanced application of the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنْ سَجَدَ لِلسُّلْطَانِ فَإِنْ كَانَ قَصْدَهُ التَّحِيَّةَ وَالتَّعْظِيمَ دُوْنَ الصَّلَاةِ لَايُكَفْرُ أضلهُ أَمْرُ الْمَلَائِكَةِ بِالسُّجُودِ لادَمَ وَسُجُوْدَ إِخْوَةِ يُوْسُفَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ. ولا يجوز السجود الا لله تعالى ومن سجد على وجه التحية اوقبل الارض بين يديه لا يكفر ولكن ياثم (هندیہ ج ۵ ص ۳۶) ولو أكرة على السُّجُودِ لِلْمَلِكِ بِالْقَتْلِ فَإِنْ أَمَرُوْهُ بِهِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْعِبَادَةِ فَالْأَفْضَلُ الصَّبْرُ، كَمَنْ أَكْرَة عَلَى الكُفْرِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ لِلنّحِيَّةِ، فَالْأفْضَلُ السُّجُوْدُ، انتهى.
Then he said: If he prostrates to the ruler, if his intention is greeting and respect, not prayer, he is not deemed a disbeliever. His evidence is the command to the angels to prostrate to Adam and the prostration of the brothers of Joseph (peace be upon him). And prostration is not permissible except to Allah Almighty. Whoever prostrates by way of greeting or kisses the ground before him is not deemed a disbeliever but is sinful. (al-Hindiyya vol.5 p.36) And if he is compelled by threat of death to prostrate to the king: if they commanded him to do it as worship, then patience is better, like one compelled to disbelief. And if it is for greeting, then prostrating is better. End.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of prostrating to a ruler. Two aspects: intention and compulsion. If the intention is greeting/respect, not worship, it is not kufr but is sinful (haram). The evidence is the precedent of the angels prostrating to Adam and Joseph's brothers, which were acts of respect, not worship. Under compulsion: if forced to prostrate as worship, it is better to endure death (like refusing kufr under coercion). If forced to prostrate for greeting, it is better to comply to save one's life. The maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' governs: the ruling depends on the intention of the doer, not the command of the coercer.

Key Terms
سجدة التحية (sajdat al-tahiyya): Prostration of greeting/showing respect, not an act of worship.
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umur bi maqasidiha): Actions are judged by their intentions.
إكراه (ikrah): Compulsion or duress that affects legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under compulsion by death, what is the better option if forced to prostrate to a king as a greeting?
A) Refuse and accept death.
B) Prostrate to save life.
C) Prostrate but intend worship.
D) Escape if possible.

Key Takeaway
Intention distinguishes haram from kufr in prostration; under compulsion, the coercer's intention determines the better course.

Intention Determines the Ruling of Eating Beyond Fullness
Expansion of a qawida with illustrative furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine the ruling of eating beyond fullness based on the intention of the eater.

Core Idea
The same act can be haram or mustahab depending on the intention.

This passage illustrates the powerful effect of intention on the ruling of an act. Eating beyond satiation is generally considered excessive, but when done with a noble purpose, it becomes recommended. Understanding how intention transforms the hukm is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas on everyday matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is eating beyond fullness (fawq al-shaba'). Without any specific intention, such excess is generally disliked or even prohibited. But the text gives two intentional variants.
The default is a baseline; intention overrides it.
2
State the two opposing intentions
First, eating purely for lust/pleasure (qasd al-shahwa). Second, eating to gain strength for an act of worship (like fasting) or to honor a guest.
The text explicitly contrasts these two cases.
3
Apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'
The maxim means that the legal ruling of an act is based on the intention behind it. Here, the same physical act receives opposite rulings because the intentions differ.
4
Derive the ruling for each intention
With the intention of pleasure, the act becomes haram. With the intention of seeking strength for worship or hospitality, it becomes mustahab (recommended).
The ruling flips from prohibited to recommended solely due to intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا الأكل فوق الشَّبْع حَرَامٌ بِقَصْدِ الشَّهْوَةِ، وَإِنْ فَصَدَ بِهِ التَّقَوّى عَلَى الصَّوْمِ أَوْمُواكَلَة الطَّيْف فَمُسْتَحَب.
And they said: Eating beyond satiation is forbidden with the intention of lust/pleasure. And if he intends by it strength for fasting or feeding the guest, then it is recommended.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage further illustrates the maxim that actions are judged by intentions. The same act – eating more than necessary – can be haram, mustahab, or permissible depending on the intention. If done purely for pleasure, it is haram. If done to gain strength for an obligatory act like fasting, or to honor a guest, it becomes mustahab (recommended). This shows that even an excessive act can be virtuous with the right intention.

Key Terms
فوق الشبع (fawq al-shaba'): Eating beyond the point of satiation; its ruling changes with intention.
مُسْتَحَب (mustahab): Recommended act; performing it brings reward, omitting it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Enjoying the taste of food.
B) Showing off generosity.
C) Gaining strength for fasting or feeding a guest.
D) Eating out of boredom.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on eating beyond fullness is entirely dependent on the intention: haram for pleasure, mustahab for worship or hospitality.

Shooting a Kafir Using a Muslim Shield: The Role of Intention
Ruling on jihad with intention as criterion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shooting a kafir who uses a Muslim as a human shield and identify how the intention (qasd) determines the permissibility.

Core Idea
Intention determines permissibility: killing the shield is haram, killing the enemy is not.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the fiqh of jihad. The text presents a case where a kafir uses a Muslim as a shield, and a Muslim must decide whether to shoot. The Hanafi position, based on the principle that actions are judged by intentions (al-umuru bi maqasidiha), makes the ruling hinge on the shooter's intention. Understanding this nuance is critical for muftis dealing with modern dilemmas of collateral harm in conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the Arabic text. The scenario is: a kafir uses a Muslim as a human shield (tatarruṣ). A Muslim shooter faces a decision to shoot at the kafir.
The shield is a victim, not a combatant.
2
Isolate the two intentions
The text contrasts two possible intentions (qasd): intending to kill the Muslim shield, or intending to kill the kafir.
The act of shooting is identical in both cases.
3
State the ruling for each intention
If the shooter intends to kill the Muslim shield, the shooting is haram. If the intent is to kill the kafir, it is not haram (i.e., permissible).
No mention of collateral damage; only direct intention matters.
4
Connect to the underlying principle
This ruling is a furu' (branch) of the legal maxim 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their intentions). The permissibility of the act depends on the shooter's true objective.
This maxim is kubra (major) and applies across fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوْا الْكَافِرُ إِذَا تَتَرَّسَ بِمُسْلِمٍ، فَإِنْ رَمَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ قَتْلَ الْمُسْلِمِ حَرُمَ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ قَتْلَ الْكَافِرِ لَا يَحْرُمُ.
ترجمه : فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کا فر نے جب کسی مسلمان کو ڈھال بنا لیا اگر مسلم نے تیر چلایا اور مسلمان کے مار نے کا ارادہ کیا تو حرام ہے اور اگر کافر کے قتل کا ارادہ کیا تو حرام نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : اگر کافر ہی نے مسلمان کو پکڑ کر ڈھال اور آر بنا لیا اور دوسری طرف مسلمان نے کافروں پر تیراندازی کی اگر مسلمانوں نے تیراندازی سے اس مسلمان کو قتل کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے جس کو کافروں نے پکڑ کر ڈھال بنا رکھا ہے تو یہ تیراندازی کرنی حرام ہے اور اگر مسلمانوں کا مقصد تیراندازی سے کافر ہی ہیں مسلمان نہیں تو حرام نہیں ہے۔
And they (the fuqaha) said: When a kafir takes a Muslim as a shield, then if a Muslim shoots at him, if he intends to kill the Muslim, it is haram; if he intends to kill the kafir, it is not haram. Translation: The jurists say: When a kafir uses a Muslim as a shield, if a Muslim shoots and intends to kill the Muslim, it is haram; if he intends to kill the kafir, it is not haram. Commentary: If the kafir has seized a Muslim and made him a shield, and then Muslims shoot at the kafirs, if the Muslims intend by their shooting to kill that Muslim who has been taken as a shield, then that shooting is haram; if their purpose is to kill the kafirs, not the Muslim, then it is not haram.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a specific ruling in the chapter of jihad. It applies the general principle that actions are judged by intentions (al-umuru bi maqasidiha). The act of shooting is neutral; its permissibility depends on the intention. If the shooter intends to kill the Muslim hostage, it is haram because it directly targets a Muslim. If the intention is to kill the kafir enemy, it is not haram even if the Muslim might be inadvertently killed? The text seems to focus on the direct intention, not on incidental harm. The commentary reiterates the same ruling in simpler terms.

Key Terms
تترس (tatarruṣ): Using a person as a human shield in warfare
قصد (qaṣd): Intention; the specific aim of the act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a kafir using a Muslim as a shield, what makes the Muslim's shooting haram?
A) The mere act of shooting.
B) The intention to kill the Muslim shield.
C) The intention to kill the kafir.
D) The presence of the Muslim shield.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on a kafir using a Muslim shield hinges on the shooter's intention: aiming at the Muslim is haram, aiming at the kafir is permissible.

Levels of Eating Based on Intention
Describes the hukm of eating from fard to haram based on intention and need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine the ruling of eating in various scenarios of intention and need, and construct a fatwa hierarchy for the levels of eating.

Core Idea
The same act of eating can be fard, mubah, haram, or mustahabb depending on your intention.

This passage by Allama Hamawi is a classic illustration of the great qawida 'Matters are judged by their intentions' (al-umur bi maqasidiha). It shows that a single act—eating—takes on different rulings (fard, mubah, haram, ja'iz, mustahabb) based on the intention and circumstances. By studying these furuat, you will learn how a mufti applies this overarching maxim to concrete cases, distinguishing between obligation, permission, prohibition, and recommendation.

Guided Path
1
State the Governing Qawida
Identify the overarching qawida that governs all the rulings in this passage. State its rank (kubra) and scope.
The qawida is 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (الأمور بمقاصدها), a major (kubra) maxim that applies to all fiqh chapters.
2
List the Levels of Eating
From the passage, extract the five distinct levels of eating with their rulings: fard (survival), mubah (up to satiation), haram (excess without reason), ja'iz (excess for fasting strength), mustahabb (excess to spare guest's feelings). Also note the ruling on eating too little.
Each level is defined by a specific intention or need.
3
Identify the Proofs (Dalil)
For each ruling, note the dalil cited: Quranic verse (42:40) for hospitality complaint, hadith on being gentle with the soul, and hadith on the strong believer. Explain how each proof supports the derived ruling.
These are dalil naqli (textual proofs).
4
Analyze the Istithna' (Exceptions)
The baseline is that eating beyond satiation is haram. The passage gives two exceptions: for fasting strength and for guest hospitality. Identify the reason for each exception and how the intention changes the ruling.
The exceptions are not ziyadah (additions) but specific cases where the ruling is lifted.
5
Apply the Fatwa Hierarchy
Determine the mufta bihi (operative) positions for each scenario. The fard level (survival) is obligatory; the mustahabb level (guest) is recommended; the haram level (excess without need) is prohibited. Understand how a mufti would prioritize these intentions when issuing a fatwa.
The strongest ruling (fard) overrides permissibility when life is at stake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح : علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کھانا کھانے کے چند مراتب ہیں اتنا کھانا کہ جس کے ذریعہ ہلاکت سے بچ جائے اور نماز کھڑے ہو کر ادا کر سکے تو فرض ہے اور اس سے زائد پیٹ بھر تک کھانا مباح ہے البتہ پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھانا حرام ہے البتہ دو موقعوں پر (۱) کہ روزے پر تقویت حاصل ہو اس لئے پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھا رہا ہے تو جائز ہے۔ (۲) یا اس نیت سے پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھا رہا ہے کہ اگر وہ کھانے سے رک گیا تو جو مہمان اس کے ساتھ کھا رہا ہے وہ بھی شرم کے مارے رک جائے گا اور وہ بھوکا رہ جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھانا مستحب ہے اس لئے کہ مہمان نوازی نہ کرنا شریعت کی نظر میں برا ہے۔ اور مہمان نوازی نہ کرنے والے کی شکایت کا اظہار کرسکتا ہے جس کی دلیل یہ آیت "لا يحب الله الجهر بالسوء من القول إلا من ظلم". علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ اتنا کم کھانا جس سے کمزوری کے سبب عبادت کی ادائیگی بھی نہ کر سکے جائز نہیں ہے دلیل یہ حدیث ہے "لـقـولـه علیه الصلاة و السلام نفسک مطيئتک فارفق بھا" اور حدیث سے مراد یہ ہے کہ نفس کو نہ تو اذیت دے اور نہ اس کو اتنا بھوکا رکھو کہ وہ ہلاک یا ہلاکت کے قریب پہنچ جائے۔ نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا " المؤمن القوى خير من المؤمن الضعيف"، طاقت ور مؤمن کمزور مؤمن سے افضل ہے۔ اگر کسی نے کھانا پینا ترک کر دیا تو انہوں نے شریعت اسلامیہ کے حکم کی خلاف ورزی کی۔ حالت مخمصہ میں اگر مردار کھا کر جان نہ بچائی اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو عاصی ہو کر مرا تو تمہارا اس کے بارے میں کیا خیال ہے جو حلال کو ترک کر دے اور بھوک کی وجہ سے مرجائے بخلاف اس کے اگر کسی کو دست لگ گئے یا پیچس یا آنکھ دکھنے لگی اور علاج نہ کرایا حتی کہ مر گیا۔
علامہ جموعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس سے ان صوفی جہلاء کا حکم بھی معلوم ہو جاتا ہے جو بغرض ریاضت حلال کھانا چھوڑ دیتے ہیں اور اتنے کمزور اور لاغر ہو جاتے ہیں کہ اللہ کے ذکر اور عبادت کو بھی بچا نہیں لائے اور اس کو قربت وعبادت تصور کر دیتے ہیں۔ اس جزئیہ کو ذہن میں اچھی طرح بٹھالینا بہت کام آئے گا۔
Commentary: Allama Hamawi says that eating has several levels: eating enough to avoid destruction and to be able to perform standing prayer is fard; eating more than that up to satiation is mubah; but eating beyond satiation is haram, except in two situations: (1) if one eats beyond satiation to gain strength for fasting, then it is permissible; (2) if one eats beyond satiation with the intention that if he stops eating, the guest eating with him would also stop out of shyness and remain hungry, then eating beyond satiation is mustahabb, because not showing hospitality is bad in the sight of Shari'ah, and one can complain about the one who does not show hospitality; the proof is the verse 'Allah does not like the public mention of evil except by one who has been wronged.' Allama Hamawi says that eating so little that one cannot perform worship due to weakness is not permissible; the proof is the hadith: 'Your soul is your mount, so be gentle with it' meaning do not harm your soul nor starve it to destruction or near destruction. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A strong believer is better than a weak believer.' If someone abandons eating and drinking, he has violated the command of Islamic Shari'ah. In a state of necessity, if one does not eat carrion to save his life and dies, he dies as a sinner. What do you think of one who abandons halal food and dies of hunger? As opposed to one who gets diarrhea, dysentery, or eye pain and does not seek treatment until he dies. Allama Jamu'i says that from this the ruling of those ignorant Sufis becomes known who abandon halal food for the purpose of asceticism and become so weak that they cannot even engage in dhikr and worship of Allah, considering that as worship. Keep this issue firmly in mind; it will be very useful.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a detailed application of the qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to the act of eating. The author, Allama Hamawi, explains that the ruling on eating is not uniform but varies according to the intention and necessity. He outlines five levels: (1) fard (obligatory) – eating just enough to survive and be able to perform standing prayer; (2) mubah (permissible) – eating up to satiation without excess; (3) haram (prohibited) – eating beyond satiation without valid reason; (4) permissible (ja'iz) – eating beyond satiation to gain strength for fasting; (5) mustahabb (recommended) – eating beyond satiation to prevent a guest from stopping out of shyness. This shows that a single act (eating excess) takes different rulings based on the niyyah. The supporting proofs include a Quranic verse (42:40) about complaining against those who fail in hospitality, and a hadith about being gentle with one's soul. The passage also warns against eating so little that one cannot worship, citing another hadith: 'A strong believer is better than a weak believer.' It further discusses the sin of abandoning halal food to the point of death, and criticizes ignorant Sufis who neglect their bodies under the guise of asceticism. This illustrates that the Shari'ah values both spiritual and physical well-being, and that intentions can turn a normally haram act (excess eating) into a recommended one.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): The level of eating required to preserve life and ability to perform obligatory acts like standing in prayer.
مباح (mubah): Eating up to satiation without excess, where the act is legally permissible without reward or punishment.
حرام (haram): Eating beyond satiation without a valid reason or intention, which is prohibited and sinful.
مستحب (mustahabb): Eating beyond satiation with the intention of saving a guest from awkwardness, considered recommended and rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allama Hamawi, what is the ruling on eating beyond satiation if done to prevent a guest from stopping out of shyness?
A) Haram
B) Mubah
C) Mustahabb
D) Fard

Key Takeaway
The intention behind eating can change its ruling from haram to mustahabb, illustrating the power of the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.

Shooting Enemies Using Muslim Shields: Intention Determines Ruling
Presents the fiqh ruling on targeting kuffar who use Muslims as human shields.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intention-based ruling in tatarruṣ cases and apply the qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
When enemies use a Muslim shield, the shooter's intention determines permissibility.

This passage from al-Hidayah demonstrates how the great maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' operates in the context of jihad. The Hanafi school distinguishes between aiming at the enemy and aiming at the Muslim shield, with the crucial factor being the shooter's intention. This lesson will explore the ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Recall the qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). Identify that it is a kulliya (universal) and kubra (major) maxim covering all fiqh chapters, especially jihad.
2
Identify the case and two scenarios
The case is when enemies (kuffar) use a Muslim as a human shield (tatarruṣ). Two scenarios based on the shooter's intention: intending to kill the Muslim shield vs. intending to kill the enemy.
3
Apply the maxim to derive rulings
Apply 'al-umur bi maqasidiha': if intention is to kill the Muslim → haram; if intention is to kill the kafir → not haram (ja'iz). The maxim directly links the ruling to the intent.
4
Examine the underlying reasoning
The reasoning balances general harm (repelling the enemy, defending bayḍat al-Islam) against specific harm (killing the Muslim shield). The general benefit outweighs the specific harm, and refraining would close the door of jihad.
5
Note the practical consequence
In practice, Hanafi law permits striking such targets as long as the intention is to kill the enemy, even if a Muslim is unintentionally killed. This is the mufta bihi position as per al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوْا الْكَافِرُ إِذَاتَتَرَّسَ بِمُسْلِمٍ، فَإِنْ رَمَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ قَتْلَ الْمُسْلِمِ حَرُمَ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ قَتْلَ الْكَافِرِ لا .
ترجمه : فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کا فر نے جب کسی مسلمان کو ڈھال بنا لیا اگر مسلم نے تیر چلایا اور مسلمان کے مار نے کا ارادہ کیا تو حرام ہے اور اگر کافر کے قتل کا ارادہ کیا تو حرام نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : اگر کافر ہی نے مسلمان کو پکڑ کر ڈھال اور آر بنا لیا اور دوسری طرف مسلمان نے کافروں پر تیراندازی کی اگر مسلمانوں نے تیراندازی سے اس مسلمان کو قتل کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے جس کو کافروں نے پکڑ کر ڈھال بنا رکھا ہے تو یہ تیراندازی کرنی حرام ہے اور اگر مسلمانوں کا مقصد تیراندازی سے کافر ہی ہیں مسلمان نہیں تو حرام نہیں ہے۔
ولا بأس برميهم وان كان فيهم مسلم اسيرا وتاجر لان الرمى دفع الضرر العام بالذب عن بيضة الاسلام وقتل الاسير والتاجر ضرر خاص ولانه فلما يخلو حصن عن مسلم فلو امتنع باعتباره لانسد بابه وان تترسوا بصييان المسلمين او بالاسارى لم يكفو عن رميهم لما بينا و يقصدون بالرمي الكفار. (هدایه ج ۲ ص ۵۶۱)
وَلَوْلَا خَوْفُ الْإِطَالَةِ لَأَوْرَدْنَا فُرُوْعًا كَثِيرَةً شَاهِدَةً لِمَا اسْتَنْبَطْنَاهُ مِنَ الْقَاعِدَةِ، وَهِيَ الأُمُورُ بِمَقَاصِدِهَا.
And they said: When a disbeliever takes a Muslim as a shield, if a Muslim shoots at him, if he intends to kill the Muslim, it is haram; if he intends to kill the disbeliever, it is not haram. Translation: The jurists say: When a disbeliever makes a Muslim a shield, if a Muslim shoots an arrow and intends to kill the Muslim, it is haram; if he intends to kill the disbeliever, it is not haram. Commentary: If the disbeliever catches a Muslim and makes him a shield and barrier, and on the other side the Muslim shoots arrows at the disbelievers: if the Muslims, by shooting, intend to kill that Muslim who has been caught and made a shield by the disbelievers, then this shooting is haram; if the Muslims' objective in shooting is the disbelievers and not the Muslim, then it is not haram. And there is no harm in shooting at them even if there is a Muslim captive or trader among them, because the shooting repels general harm by defending the territory of Islam, while killing the captive or trader is a specific harm, and because rarely is a fortress free of a Muslim, so if one refrained for that reason, the door would be closed. And if they shield themselves with Muslim children or captives, they are not to be refrained from shooting at them for the reason we stated, and they aim at the disbelievers with the shooting. (Hidayah vol. 2, p. 561) And if not for fear of prolongation, we would have brought many derived cases witnessing to the qa'idah we have deduced, which is: al-umur bi maqasidiha (matters are judged by intentions).
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an application of the qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to the issue of warfare when the enemy uses Muslims as human shields. The Hanafi ruling, as cited from al-Hidayah, distinguishes based on the intention of the shooter. If a Muslim soldier shoots at a group that includes a Muslim shield (captive or trader) and the soldier intends to kill that particular Muslim, the act is haram. However, if the soldier's intention is to kill the disbeliever enemy, the act is not haram, even though the Muslim shield may be hit unintentionally. The reasoning is that the general benefit of repelling the enemy outweighs the specific harm to the captive, and if one were to refrain from shooting due to the presence of Muslims, it would undermine jihad. The passage also mentions that even if children or captives are used as shields, the same ruling applies. The author then notes that this is just one example of the many furu' that could be derived from the maxim, but he does not prolong.

Key Terms
تترس (tatarruṣ): The act of using another person as a shield for protection from attack.
بيضة الإسلام (bayḍat al-Islam): The core territory or heartland of the Islamic state that must be defended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling about enemies using a Muslim as a shield, what makes the shooting haram?
A) The presence of a Muslim shield
B) The intention to kill the Muslim shield
C) The absence of a valid military objective
D) The use of arrows instead of other weapons

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the permissibility of shooting at enemies using Muslim shields hinges on the shooter's intention, applying the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.

Ruling on Luqata Based on Intention
Application of qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to luqata

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to classify the finder of lost property as either a trustee (amin) or a usurper (ghasib) and determine subsequent obligations.

Core Idea
Intention transforms luqata from permissible trust to sinful usurpation.

This passage demonstrates the powerful effect of intention (niyyah) in a concrete case: picking up a lost item. The same physical act—lifting an object—becomes either lawful or unlawful solely based on what the finder intends to do with it. This is a classic application of the first major maxim, 'Matters are judged by their intentions.' We will explore how the finder's state of mind determines the ruling, the conditions for permissible picking, and the special exceptions for the poor and trivial items.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Recall the qa'idah kubra: 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'. This maxim governs all actions where intention distinguishes one legal category from another. Here it applies to luqata.
2
Identify the two intentions and their rulings
From the passage: intention to return = halal; intention to keep = haram and sinful (ghasib). Note that the ruling on the act of picking up itself is based on the simultaneous intention.
3
Trace the procedure after lawful picking
If picked with correct intention, the finder must announce, search for the owner, and if unsuccessful, give it in charity. If the item perishes after charity, he must compensate unless he is poor.
4
Recognize the exceptions
The passage mentions two exceptions: (1) if the finder is poor, he may use the item himself; (2) if the item is trivial (something the owner would not search for), the finder may keep it. These are istithna'at of the maxim.
5
Apply the maxim to a new scenario
Given a similar case, identify the intention first, then determine the ruling and obligations. This is the core skill of applying qawaid to furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوْا فِي بَابِ اللُّقْطَةِ : إِنْ أَخَذَهَا بِنِيَّةِ رَدْهَا ، حَلَّ لَهُ رَفْعُهَا وَإِنْ أَخَذَهَا بِنِيَّةِ نَفْسِهِ كَانَ غاصِبا آثِماً .
ترجمه: فقہاء فرماتے ہیں لفظہ کے بارے میں اگر واپسی کی نیت سے اٹھایا ہے تو اس کے لئے اس کا اٹھانا حلال ہے اور اگر اس نے اپنی ہی نیت سے اٹھایا ہے تو غاصب اور گنہگار ہوگا۔
تشريح اللقطة بفتح القاف على اللغة المشهورة التي قالها الجمهور واللغة الثانية .باسكانها. والثالثة لقاطة بضم اللام والرابعة لقط بفتح اللام والقاف . هي اسم وضع للمال المتبقـط وشرعاً مال يوجد ضائعاً وفى المحيط رفع شئ ضائع للحفظ على الغير لا للتملك
(شامی یاس (۴۳۰)
ا راستہ میں پڑھی ہوئی چیز اس نیت سے اٹھائی ہے کہ اس کو مالک تک پہنچانے کی پوری جد و جہد کروں گا تو اس کے لئے اس لقطہ کا اٹھانا جائز ہے۔ تواس کا اعلان وغیرہ کرنے اور اس کے مالک تک اس کو پہنچانے کی پوری جدوجہد کرے۔ مالک کے نہ ملنے پر صدقہ کر دے اور اگر صدقہ کرنے پر وہ چیز ہلاک ہو جائے یا ختم ہو جائے اور اس کے بعد مالک آجائے تو لاقط اس کا تاوان اپنی جیب سے ادا کرے گا اور اگر لاقط غریب ہے تو خود بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے یا کوئی معمولی چیز ہے جس کو مالک تلاش نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کو اٹھا لینے والا خود بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔
And they said in the chapter of luqata: If he picks it up with the intention of returning it, it is halal for him to pick it up; and if he picks it up with the intention of keeping it, he is a usurper and sinful. Translation: The jurists say regarding luqata: If he picks it up with the intention of returning it, then picking it up is halal; and if he picks it up with the intention of keeping it for himself, he is a usurper and sinful. Commentary: Luqata (with fatha on qaf according to the well-known language of the majority; the second language is with sukun; the third is luqata with dammah on lam; the fourth is luqat with fatha on lam and qaf) is a term for property that is found. And legally it is property found lost. In al-Muhit: picking up a lost thing for preservation for someone else, not for ownership. (Shami? 430) So if one picks up a lost item on the road with the intention of striving fully to return it to its owner, then picking it up is permissible. He should make announcement and fully strive to return it to its owner. If the owner is not found, he should give it in charity. If after giving charity the item perishes or is lost and then the owner comes, the finder (laqit) must compensate from his own pocket. If the finder is poor, he may use it himself. Or if it is a trivial item that the owner would not search for, then the finder may use it himself.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is another application of the qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' specifically in the chapter of luqata (lost property). The ruling is clear: the permissibility of picking up a lost item depends entirely on the intention. If the finder intends to return it to its owner, the act of picking it up is permissible and even commendable. However, if the finder intends to keep it for himself from the outset, he is considered a ghasib (usurper) and commits a sin. The author then provides definitions of luqata, citing the Muhit and Shami. He elaborates on the procedures: the finder must make an effort to find the owner, and if unsuccessful, should give it in charity. If the item perishes after charity and the owner later appears, the finder must compensate. Exceptions are made if the finder is poor (he may use it) or if the item is trivial (he may keep it). This shows how intention determines the initial ruling and subsequent obligations.

Key Terms
لقطة (luqata): Property that is found and lost, which one picks up with the intention of preserving it for the owner.
غاصب (ghasib): One who takes another's property unlawfully with intent to keep it; a usurper.
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umur bi maqasidiha): Matters are judged by their intentions; the first grand maxim of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person picks up a lost item with the intention of keeping it for himself?
A) It is halal but makruh.
B) It is haram; he is a usurper (ghasib) and sinful.
C) It is permissible if he later donates it to charity.
D) It is wajib to pick it up to prevent loss.

Key Takeaway
Intention is the decisive factor: picking up lost property is permissible only when one intends to return it to the owner; otherwise, it is an act of usurpation with sin and liability.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Applying the Maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' in Daily Acts
Furuat applying the maxim to pillows, trees, coins, and sacks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to diverse furuat and identify when intention changes the ruling, and when an exception (istithna') overrides.

Core Idea
Intention transforms the legal status of everyday acts: the same physical action can be recommended, permissible, disliked, or even kufr based solely on the qasd.

The great maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' is not limited to the purity of worship; it governs mundane actions like sitting, planting, and handling coins. In this lesson, we explore several rulings from authoritative Hanafi works that show how a single act—like using a book as a pillow—can be either neutral or prohibited depending on the intention behind it. Understanding these furuat equips the mufti to apply the maxim correctly in new cases.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Begin by recalling the maxim: 'Acts are judged by intentions' (al-umur bi maqasidiha). This is a major qa'idah that applies across all fiqh chapters.
Ensure the student can articulate the maxim in Arabic and English.
2
Identify the act and two possible intentions
For each furu' in the text, list the physical action and contrast the two intentions that lead to different rulings (e.g., preservation vs. disrespect).
The same act can have opposite rulings based solely on qasd.
3
Apply the maxim to derive the ruling
Using the maxim, determine the ruling for each intention. For example, if the intent is preservation (hifz), the act is permissible; if the intent is disrespect (ihaanah) or personal benefit without necessity, the act becomes disliked or even haram.
The maxim acts as the operative principle connecting intention to hukm.
4
Check for the istithna' (exception)
Acknowledge that when the act inherently involves clear disrespect (e.g., deliberate contempt for sacred texts or names), the ruling becomes kufr regardless of intent, as the act itself outweighs the intended purpose.
This istithna' is based on the principle 'al-darar yuzal' and the need to protect the sacred.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
For each furu', identify the operative ruling for fatwa. The Hanafi position is that intention is the decisive factor, except when the act is inherently contemptuous.
All rulings in the text are from reliable later Hanafi sources (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رفع شيئ ضائع للحفظ على الغير لا للتملك ندب رفعها لصاحبها ان امن على نفسه تعريفها والا فالترک اولى وفي البدائع وان اخذ لنفسه حرم لانها كالغصب ( نور الابصار [؟] ) وَفِي التَّاتَارُ خَانِيَةِ : فِى الْحَظَرِ وَالْإِبَاحَةِ إِذا تَوَسَّدَ الْكِتَابَ، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحِفْظُ لَا يَكْرَهُ، وَإِلَّا يَكْرَهُ. مَعَه خريطة فيها كتب من اخبار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم او كتب ابي حنيفة أو غیره فتوسد خريطة ان قصد الحفظ لا يكره . اذ ليس فيه ترك التعظيم وإن لم يقصد الحفظ يكره لان فيه ترك التعظيم (المحيط البرهاني ج ۶ ص / ۴۹) وَإِنْ غَرَسَ فِى الْمَسْجِدِ، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ الظَّلِ لَا يَكْرَهُ وَإِنْ قَصَدَ مَنْفَعَةً أُخْرَى يَكْرَهُ. وعنه ايضاً فيمن غرس الاستجار في المسجد ان كان يفعل ذلك للظل لا بأس وان كان يفعل ذلك لبيع الاوراق او لمنفعة اخرى يكره اذا كانت تضيق على الناس مسجدهم لصلاتهم او يقع فيه تفريق الصفوف (المحيط البرهاني ج ۲ ص / ۵۳۹) وَكِتَابَةُ إِسْمِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى الدَّرْهَمِ إِنْ كَانَ بِقَصْدِ الْعَلَامَةِ لَا يَكْرَهُ، وَلِلنَّهَاوُنِ يَكْرَهُ وَالْجُلُوْسُ عَلَى جَوْلِقٍ فِيْهِ مُصْحَفٌ إِنْ قَصَدَ الْحِفْظِ لَا يَكْرَهُ، وَإِلَّا يَكْرَهُ. ولا باس بكتابة اسم الله تعالى على الدراهم لان قصد صاحبه العلامة لا التهاون (هندیه ج ۳۲۳۵) وإذا كان للرجل جوالق وفيها مراسم مكتوب فيها شي من القرآن او كان فى الحوالق كتب الفقه او كتب التفسير او المصحف فجلس عليها او نام فان كان من قصده الحفظ فلا بأس (المحيط البرهاني ج / ٥ ص / ٥١)
To raise a lost item for preservation on behalf of the owner, not for ownership: it is recommended to return it to its owner if safe from harm, otherwise leaving it is better. In al-Bada'i': if he takes it for himself, it is forbidden because it is like usurpation. In al-Tatar Khaniyya, in the chapter on prohibition and permission: when he uses a book as a pillow, if he intends preservation, it is not disliked; otherwise it is disliked. A man with a bag containing books of reports of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or books of Abu Hanifa or others, and he uses the bag as a pillow: if he intends preservation, it is not disliked, because there is no lack of respect in it; if he does not intend preservation, it is disliked, because it contains lack of respect (al-Muhit al-Burhani, vol. 6, p. 49). And if he plants a tree in the mosque: if he intends shade, it is not disliked; if he intends other benefit, it is disliked. Also from him: for someone who plants a tree in the mosque for the purpose of shade, there is no harm; if he does that to sell the leaves or for other benefit, it is disliked if it narrows the mosque for the people's prayer or causes splitting of the rows (al-Muhit al-Burhani, vol. 2, p. 539). Writing the name of Allah the Exalted on a coin: if it is with the intention of a mark, it is not disliked; if for disrespect, it is disliked. And sitting on a sack in which there is a Quran: if he intends preservation, it is not disliked; otherwise it is disliked. There is no harm in writing the name of Allah on coins because the intent of the owner is marking, not disrespect (al-Hindiya, vol. 3, p. 235). If a man has a sack and in it are writings containing something of the Quran, or in the sack there are books of fiqh, tafsir, or the Quran, and he sits on it or sleeps: if his intention is preservation, there is no harm (al-Muhit al-Burhani, vol. 5, p. 51).
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a collection of furuat (applications) of the major qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (acts are judged by intentions). The author lists several rulings from authoritative Hanafi works, each illustrating how the permissibility or prohibition of an act hinges on the underlying intent. The first ruling concerns a lost item: picking it up for preservation is recommended, but taking it for oneself is haram. Then, using a book or a bag containing sacred texts as a pillow: if the intent is preservation (e.g., from theft), it is not makruh; otherwise, it is makruh because it shows disrespect. Similarly, planting a tree in the mosque is not disliked if the intent is to provide shade; but if the intent is profit (e.g., selling leaves) and it causes inconvenience to worshippers, it becomes makruh. Writing Allah's name on coins is not disliked if done as a mark of Muslim sovereignty; otherwise, if done casually, it is makruh, and if with deliberate disrespect, it is kufr. Sitting on a sack containing a Quran or Islamic books is permissible if the intent is preservation, but otherwise makruh. All these rulings demonstrate that the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' governs not just worship but all areas of fiqh, from lost property to mosque etiquette to financial transactions.

Key Terms
قصد (qasd): The intention or purpose behind an act that determines its legal ruling.
مقاصد (maqasid): Plural of maqsad, meaning objectives or purposes; here referring to the ends that the shari'ah considers in human actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is using a book as a pillow permissible in one case and disliked in another?
A) The type of book determines the ruling
B) The intention behind using it determines the ruling
C) It depends on whether the book is borrowed or owned
D) It is always disliked because books should be respected

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' continuously shapes the rulings of daily acts, but must be weighed against the inherent dignity of sacred objects.
