Purpose of Niyyah: Distinguishing Worship from Habits
Explains why niyyah is legislated: distinguishing worship from habits and different worships.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim about niyyah to classify ambiguous actions as worship or habit and issue a fatwa accordingly.

Core Idea
Niyyah transforms a neutral habit into a rewarded act of worship; without it, the same action remains mere custom.

Why does Shari'ah require us to make niyyah (intention) before acts of worship? This lesson unpacks a foundational Hanafi rule: niyyah is not a mere formality—it is the mechanism that separates ibadah from adat. We will explore examples of actions that can be either habit or worship depending solely on intent, and see how this principle guides a mufti's ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Articulate the purpose of niyyah as given in the classical texts: 'The purpose of niyyah is to distinguish acts of worship from habitual acts and to distinguish some acts of worship from others.'
This maxim is a dabt (sub-maxim) under the major qa'idah 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Identify the two functions
The maxim covers two functions: (1) separating worship from habit (e.g., refraining from food could be diet or fasting), and (2) separating different acts of worship that share a physical form (e.g., zuhr prayer vs. asr prayer).
3
Work through the furuat
Apply the maxim to the examples in the text: imsak (refraining from food), sitting in the mosque, and slaughtering an animal. For each, note how intention changes the ruling.
These examples illustrate the practical application of the maxim.
4
Recognize the istithna
Note that acts inherently worship (like tawaf) require niyyah even if they resemble habits, because no similar habitual act exists. This exception is governed by the qa'idah 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
The istithna reinforces the maxim rather than contradicting it.
5
Apply as a mufti
When issuing a fatwa on an ambiguous action, first identify the physical act. Then determine the intention of the person. Use the maxim to classify the act and assign the corresponding hukm.
The mufti must inquire about the person's intent if it is unclear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَلْقَانِي فِي بَيَانِ مَا شُرِعَتْ لِأجْلِهِ، قَالُوْا الْمَقْصُوْدُ مِنْهَا تَمْيِيْزُ الْعِبَادَاتِ مِنَ الْعَادَاتِ وَتَمْيِيْزُ بَعْضِ الْعِبَادَاتِ عَنْ بَعْضٍ، كَمَا فِي النّهَايَةِ وَفَتْحِ الْقَدِيْرِ كَالْإِمْسَاكِ عَنِ الْمُفْطِرَاتِ، قَدْ يَكُونُ حِمْيَةً، أَوْ تَدَاوِيًا، أَوْ لِعَدْمِ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَيْهِ. وَالْجُلُوْسُ فِى الْمَسْجِدِ قَدْ يَكُونُ لِلْإِسْتِرَاحَةِ، وَقَدْ يَكُوْنُ قُرْبَةً، كَزَكَاةٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ. وَالذَّبْحُ قَدْ يَكُونَ لِلأَكُلِ، فَيَكُونُ مُبَاحًا أَوْ مَنْدُوبًا، أَوْ لِلْأضْحِيَّةِ، فَيَكُوْنُ عِبَادَةً، أَوْ لِقُدُومِ أَمِيْرٍ، فَيَكُوْنُ حَرَامًا، أَوْ كُفْرًا عَلَى قَوْلٍ.
He placed before me an explanation of why it (niyyah) is legislated. They said: Its purpose is to distinguish acts of worship from habitual acts and to distinguish some acts of worship from others, as in an-Nihayah and Fath al-Qadir. For example, refraining from things that break the fast may be for dieting, or treatment, or lack of need for it. And sitting in the mosque may be for rest, and may be for closeness, like [giving] zakah or charity. And slaughtering may be for eating, so it is permissible or recommended, or for the sacrifice, so it is worship, or for the arrival of an amir, so it is forbidden, or disbelief according to one opinion.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage explains the second discussion: the purpose (maqsud) of legislating niyyah. The scholars state that niyyah serves two primary functions: first, to distinguish acts of worship (ibadat) from habitual acts (adat); second, to differentiate between different acts of worship. The text provides examples from classical Hanafi works like an-Nihayah and Fath al-Qadir. Refraining from food and drink (imsak) could be for health reasons (himyah), medical treatment, or because one lacks need—all are habits—or it could be for the sake of fasting, which is worship. Similarly, sitting in the mosque could be for rest (adat) or for worship (qurbah) like giving charity. Slaughtering an animal could be for food (mubah or mandub), for the Eid sacrifice (ibadah), for welcoming a ruler (haram), or even kufr if done in a certain way. Thus, niyyah is essential to determine the legal nature of an act. The Hanafi school emphasizes that intentions convert neutral or habitual actions into acts of devotion, and without intent, the same physical action remains a mere custom.

Key Terms
تمييز (tamyiz): Distinguishing; the function of niyyah to differentiate between types of acts.
عبادات (ibadat): Acts of worship; actions performed with the intention of drawing closer to Allah.
عادة (adah): Habitual act; an action done without religious intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim, what is one purpose of niyyah?
A) To make an action physically valid
B) To distinguish acts of worship from habitual acts
C) To increase reward only
D) To ensure the action is done on time

Key Takeaway
Niyyah is the essential mechanism that separates worship from habit; without it, the same physical act remains a mere custom with a different ruling.

Definition of Niyyah: Addressing Objections and Qadi Baydawi's Definitions
Addresses objection to comprehensiveness of shar'i definition and presents Qadi Baydawi's definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of niyyah to distinguish between ibadah and adat, and explain why refraining from sin with intention qualifies as an act of the heart.

Core Idea
Niyyah is a heart-action: refraining from sin with intention is also a creation of an act, because 'fi'l' includes heart actions.

In this lesson, we examine the definition of niyyah (intention) as understood in the Hanafi school. An objection is raised that the common shar'i definition—'creation of an action'—excludes refraining from sin. We explore the response that 'action' encompasses heart actions, supported by a hadith. We then study Qadi Baydawi's separate lughawi and shar'i definitions, which clarify the scope of niyyah in both worship and everyday acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the first part of the passage. What is the definition being criticized, and why is it claimed to be non-comprehensive?
The objection hinges on the word 'creation' (ijad) and its apparent limitation to physical actions.
2
Analyze the Response
Study the response from Allamah Jamuti. How does he expand the meaning of 'fi'l' to include heart actions? What evidence does he provide?
The hadith about avoiding prohibitions is used to show that refraining is an act of worship.
3
Distinguish the Two Definitions
Compare Qadi Baydawi's lughawi and shar'i definitions. Note the key elements: shar'i includes seeking Allah's pleasure and obeying His command; lughawi includes any heart direction for benefit or harm, immediate or delayed.
The lughawi is broader and includes worldly intentions.
4
Apply the Definitions
Take a scenario (e.g., someone abstains from food for health reasons vs. for fasting). Determine which falls under the shar'i definition and why.
The presence of intention for divine command is the distinguishing factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایجـاد
جو شرعی تعریف کی ہے وہ جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں ایجاد فعل کی بات کہی گئی ہے جبکہ کسی گناہ کے کام سے رکنے میں نکھل نہیں ہوتا ۔ اس کا جواب علامہ جموٹی نے یہ دیا ہے کہ لفظ فعل جوارح اور قلب دونوں کے فعل کو عام ہے لہذا اب ستنی فعل سے اطاعت خداوندی کی وجہ سے رک جانا بھی فعل قلب کے ایجاد کے تحت آجائے گا جیسا کہ حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے " عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من يا خذ من امتى خمس حصال فيعمل بهن او يعلمهن من يعمل بهن قال قلت انا يا رسول الله قال فاخذ بيدى فعدهن ثم قال اتق المحارم تكن اعبد الناس (مسند الامام احمد بن مغیل ج رص (۳۱۰)
قاضی بیضاوی کی تعریفات: علامہ قاضی بیضاوی نے نیت کی لغوی و شرعی دونوں تعریف الگ الگ ذکر کی ہیں چنانچہ ان کے نزدیک شرعانیت کا مفہوم ہے اللہ تعالی کی خوشنودی کے حصول اور اس کے حکم کی اتباع میں کسی فعل کی طرف متوجہ ہونے والا ارادہ جبکہ لغوی اعتبار سے دل کا کسی ایسے ھی کی طرف متوجہ ہو جانا جس کو وہ اپنی غرض کے موافق پاتا ہو خواہ اس کی یہ غرض جلب منفعت کی شکل میں ہو یا دفع ضرر کی شکل میں اسی طرح خواہ اس کی یہ غرض فورا حاصل ہو رہی ہو یا دیر سے حاصل ہو رہی ہو۔
Creation. The shar'i definition that has been given is not comprehensive because it mentions the creation of an action, whereas refraining from a sinful act does not involve creation. The response of Allamah Jamuti is that the word 'action' is general to the actions of the limbs and the heart, so refraining due to obedience to Allah comes under the creation of an action of the heart, as is known from the hadith: 'On the authority of Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Who will take from my ummah five practices and act upon them or teach them to someone who acts upon them? I said: I, O Messenger of Allah. He said: He took my hand and counted them, then said: Avoid the prohibitions, you will be the most worshipping of people.' (Musnad Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, vol. 3, p. 310). The definitions of Qadi Baydawi: Allamah Qadi Baydawi has mentioned both the lughawi and shar'i definitions separately. According to him, the shar'i meaning of niyyah is: an intention directed towards an action in seeking the pleasure of Allah and following His command. As for the lughawi meaning: the heart's direction towards something that it finds suitable for its purpose, whether that purpose is to attain benefit or repel harm, and whether that purpose is immediate or delayed.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and legal definition analysis of niyyah (intention). The author begins by addressing an objection to a prior shar'i definition: that definition required 'creation of an action' (ijad fi'l), but refraining from sin (imsak) is not an action in the usual sense. The response, attributed to Allamah Jamuti, clarifies that 'fi'l' includes both physical and heart actions, so refraining with intention is a heart action. A hadith from Musnad Ahmad is cited to support this broad understanding. Then Qadi Baydawi's definitions are presented: shar'i niyyah is the intention directed toward an action for Allah's pleasure and obedience; lughawi niyyah is the heart's inclination toward something that serves one's purpose, whether for gain or prevention, immediate or delayed. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul because niyyah is required for distinguishing worship from custom, and it is defined with precision to cover all acts.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Shar'an: an intention directed toward an action seeking Allah's pleasure and obeying His command. Lughatan: the heart's direction toward something that serves its purpose.
إيجاد فعل (ijad fi'l): The creation or bringing into existence of an action, whether by limbs or heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the response of Allamah Jamuti, why does refraining from a sinful act fall under the definition of 'creation of an action' (ijad fi'l)?
A) Because refraining is a physical action of the limbs.
B) Because the word 'action' includes actions of the heart.
C) Because the hadith explicitly mentions refraining.
D) Because refraining is always done with intention.

Key Takeaway
Niyyah is a heart action; refraining from sin with intention is considered an act of worship because 'fi'l' includes physical and spiritual actions.

Pure Worship Does Not Require Intention
Explaining a Hanafi legal maxim with applications and scholarly consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida for pure worship and apply it to given examples from the text.

Core Idea
Purely devotional acts are self-distinguishing; intention is only needed when worship and custom could be confused.

This lesson explores a fundamental maxim: acts that are exclusively worship require no separate intention because their nature inherently distinguishes them from habitual actions. We will examine the ruling, its evidence (ijma), and several furu' applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
Locate the core rule in the passage: 'ما كان صرف عبادة لا يحتاج إلى النية'. Understand its scope: applies only when there is no possibility of confusion with custom.
This is a sughra (minor) qawida and a dabt (restrictive) rule.
2
Examine the Evidence
The author cites consensus (ijma) on recitation, adhan, and remembrances. Also, he uses analogy (qiyas) to extend the rule from explicit faith to other pure acts.
The ijma is reported by al-Mu'ini in his Sharh al-Bukhari.
3
Apply to the Furuat
Consider each example: iman, tilawah, adhkar, adhan. For each, the ruling is that intention is not required for validity. Note that adhan has a dispute on reward.
The text explicitly states these examples.
4
Apply the Limiting Condition
The qawida only applies when there is no confusion between worship and custom. If an act is both, intention becomes necessary. This is the underlying rationale.
This condition is stated in the dabt: 'إلا إذا كان هناك التباس بين العبادة والعادة'.

میں بیت کنند و ای چینے جیسے تلاوت، اذکار اور اذان وغیرہ۔ لیکن علامہ موی فرماتے ہیں کہ علامہ منی کا فرمانا کہا ان میں بھی نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے یہ قاعدہ رہا۔ خلاف ہے جس میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ اذان میں تحصیل ثواب کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے علامہ مولی فرماتے ہیں ۔ ما قبل میں ہی ہم نے اس پر متنبہ کر دیا تھا اس کو دیکھ لیا جائے ۔
Therefore, upon this is derived that what is purely worship and has no confusion with other matters, then that condition (i.e., intention) is not required, like believing in Allah as we have previously explained, and knowledge, fear, hope, intention, reciting Quran, and remembrances, because these are distinct and have no confusion with other matters. And besides faith, I have not seen explicit text [for these], but they are deduced by analogy to faith that is explicitly stated. Then I saw that Ibn Wahban said in Sharh al-Manzuma that what is purely worship does not need intention, and also mentioned that intention does not need intention, and al-Mu'ini in his commentary on Bukhari narrated consensus that recitation, remembrances, and adhan do not need intention. Explanation: In Shari'ah worship, by which means nearness to Allah is attained, there are several levels: some are fard, some nafl, some wajib. To distinguish all of them from each other, intention was instituted. The author has derived that acts that are purely worship and have no possibility of being custom, then there is no risk of confusion between worship and custom; and where there is no risk of confusion, intention is not necessary because intention is for distinguishing between worship and custom. As belief in Allah, which we have mentioned; although the author mentioned Islam here, not belief, but there is no difference. 'And besides faith, I have not seen' - the author says that by analogy to faith he mentioned some other acts in which intention is not deemed necessary, but for faith he found explicitness that it is not necessary, but for other particulars he had no explicitness; rather he analogized them to explicit faith. Allamah Jawi says that besides faith, other things like remembrances, Quran recitation etc. which were mentioned as not needing intention, Allamah Samah Misi in Fath al-Qadir has made them explicit. He said: If one has taken a vow to recite Quran, then intention is necessary to distinguish the obligatory from non-obligatory. 'Intention does not need intention': because if intention required intention, then infinite regress would follow. But Allamah Hamawi commented on this cause. Some researchers mentioned that intention does not need intention because intention, by its very form, directs towards Allah; that is why mere intention gives reward, but action without intention gives no reward because action fluctuates between Allah and other than Him. Yes, mere intention gives one reward, and action gives reward when intention is also there, because actions are means to goals. But this reward is from Shari'ah, so that objections do not arise on mere intention. Then I saw... [OCR unclear]... But Allamah Mawi says that the ruling of Allamah Mini that they do not need intention is contrary to what is mentioned that intention for reward in adhan is necessary. Allamah Mawi says: We have already alerted to this earlier, so it should be seen.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage discusses a key Hanafi qawida: acts of worship that are purely devotional and not mixed with habitual actions do not require a separate intention (niyyah) because intention is primarily to distinguish worship from custom. The author cites examples such as belief in Allah, knowledge of Him, recitation of Quran, and adhan, and notes that scholars have reached consensus on some of these. However, an exception arises when an act becomes obligatory due to a vow, requiring intention to distinguish the obligatory from the voluntary. The passage also addresses the meta-rule that intention itself does not require another intention to avoid infinite regress. Later scholars differ on the necessity of intention for adhan, with some holding it necessary for reward. The commentary follows the structure of the original text, first stating the rule, then providing applications, and finally discussing scholarly disagreements.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship
صرف عبادة (sirf ibadah): An act that is purely devotional with no customary aspect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qawida, which of the following acts does NOT require intention?
A) Performing the obligatory Fajr prayer
B) Reciting Quran without a vow
C) Giving Zakat
D) Fasting in Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Acts that are purely worship and not mixed with custom do not require intention because their nature makes them distinct.

intermediate
6 min
Exceptions and Meta-Rule for Intention
Highlighting exceptions and meta-legal issues in the qawida.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when intention becomes required for pure acts and explain why intention itself does not need intention.

Core Idea
When a pure act becomes obligatory by vow, intention is needed; and intention is self-intending to avoid infinite regress.

This lesson addresses two nuanced points from the text: first, the exception to the qawida when a pure act is made wajib via a vow (nathr); second, the meta-rule that intention itself does not require another intention, as that would lead to infinite regress. We also explore a dispute among later Hanafis regarding adhan.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Exception
Identify the istithna in the passage: if someone vows to recite Quran, intention becomes necessary to distinguish the wajib from nafl recitation.
This is based on the qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Examine the Reasoning
The need for intention arises because the act now has two possible categories: obligatory or voluntary. Without intention, one cannot know which is being performed.
This exception does not contradict the original qawida; it activates it.
3
Analyze the Meta-Rule
The text states 'النية لا تحتاج إلى النية' (intention does not need intention). Understand the argument: requiring intention for intention leads to infinite regress (tasalsul).
Some scholars argue that intention is inherently directed towards Allah, so it is self-validating.
4
Review the Dispute on Adhan
Some later scholars differed on whether adhan requires intention for reward. The majority holds it is valid without, but intention is recommended.
This shows that the qawida is applied consistently, but reward may be conditional on intention.

Therefore, upon this is derived that what is purely worship and has no confusion with other matters, then that condition (i.e., intention) is not required, like believing in Allah as we have previously explained, and knowledge, fear, hope, intention, reciting Quran, and remembrances, because these are distinct and have no confusion with other matters. And besides faith, I have not seen explicit text [for these], but they are deduced by analogy to faith that is explicitly stated. Then I saw that Ibn Wahban said in Sharh al-Manzuma that what is purely worship does not need intention, and also mentioned that intention does not need intention, and al-Mu'ini in his commentary on Bukhari narrated consensus that recitation, remembrances, and adhan do not need intention. Explanation: In Shari'ah worship, by which means nearness to Allah is attained, there are several levels: some are fard, some nafl, some wajib. To distinguish all of them from each other, intention was instituted. The author has derived that acts that are purely worship and have no possibility of being custom, then there is no risk of confusion between worship and custom; and where there is no risk of confusion, intention is not necessary because intention is for distinguishing between worship and custom. As belief in Allah, which we have mentioned; although the author mentioned Islam here, not belief, but there is no difference. 'And besides faith, I have not seen' - the author says that by analogy to faith he mentioned some other acts in which intention is not deemed necessary, but for faith he found explicitness that it is not necessary, but for other particulars he had no explicitness; rather he analogized them to explicit faith. Allamah Jawi says that besides faith, other things like remembrances, Quran recitation etc. which were mentioned as not needing intention, Allamah Samah Misi in Fath al-Qadir has made them explicit. He said: If one has taken a vow to recite Quran, then intention is necessary to distinguish the obligatory from non-obligatory. 'Intention does not need intention': because if intention required intention, then infinite regress would follow. But Allamah Hamawi commented on this cause. Some researchers mentioned that intention does not need intention because intention, by its very form, directs towards Allah; that is why mere intention gives reward, but action without intention gives no reward because action fluctuates between Allah and other than Him. Yes, mere intention gives one reward, and action gives reward when intention is also there, because actions are means to goals. But this reward is from Shari'ah, so that objections do not arise on mere intention. Then I saw... [OCR unclear]... But Allamah Mawi says that the ruling of Allamah Mini that they do not need intention is contrary to what is mentioned that intention for reward in adhan is necessary. Allamah Mawi says: We have already alerted to this earlier, so it should be seen.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage discusses a key Hanafi qawida: acts of worship that are purely devotional and not mixed with habitual actions do not require a separate intention (niyyah) because intention is primarily to distinguish worship from custom. The author cites examples such as belief in Allah, knowledge of Him, recitation of Quran, and adhan, and notes that scholars have reached consensus on some of these. However, an exception arises when an act becomes obligatory due to a vow, requiring intention to distinguish the obligatory from the voluntary. The passage also addresses the meta-rule that intention itself does not require another intention to avoid infinite regress. Later scholars differ on the necessity of intention for adhan, with some holding it necessary for reward. The commentary follows the structure of the original text, first stating the rule, then providing applications, and finally discussing scholarly disagreements.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship
صرف عبادة (sirf ibadah): An act that is purely devotional with no customary aspect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does intention itself not require another intention according to Hanafi scholars?
A) Because intention is not an act of worship
B) To avoid infinite regress (tasalsul)
C) Because the Quran commands it
D) Because intention is a condition, not an act

Key Takeaway
Intention is only required when an act could be confused with another; it is not self-requiring to avoid infinite regress.

Intention Specification Based on Time Types
Rule on intention specification based on time types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that distinguishes container, enveloping, and problematic times to determine whether specification of intention is required in acts of worship.

Core Idea
If time holds multiple acts, specify; if time is consumed by the act, no specification.

In Hanafi fiqh, the necessity of specifying the exact worship in one's intention (ta'yin) depends on the nature of the time in which the worship is performed. The jurists have classified times into three categories: container (zarf), enveloping (miyar), and problematic (mushkil). This lesson explains the rule and its application to prayer, fasting, and Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification
The author divides the time of worship into three categories: zarf (container), miyar (enveloping), and mushkil (problematic).
2
Understand each category
Zarf: the time can accommodate multiple similar acts (e.g., prayer times). Miyar: the act completely occupies the time, leaving no room for another (e.g., Ramadan). Mushkil: time has aspects of both (e.g., Hajj months).
3
Note the ruling
For zarf, specification is required (wajib). For miyar and mushkil, specification is not required.
The rule is derived from the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' and qiyas.
4
Apply to examples
Prayer (Zuhr, Asr, etc.) requires specification. Fasting in Ramadan does not; a nafl intention becomes Ramadan fast. Hajj does not require specification.
Example from the passage: 'Zuhr of today' suffices even if time exits, but 'Zuhr of the time' fails if time exits and person is unaware.

منا کوئی آدمی ظہر کی نماز پڑھ رہا ہے تو دن کی طرف نسبت کر دینا ہی کافی ہے کہ میں آج کی ظہر پڑھ رہا ہوں تو یہ نسبت اس کے لئے کافی ہو گی خواہ وہ وقت میں نماز ادا کرے یا وقت نکل جانے کے بعد لیکن اگر گذشته ایم میں سے کسی دن کی عصر کی نماز پڑھے اور ظہر الیوم کی نیت کرے تو اسے آج کی عصر کہنا درست نہ ہو گا اس لئے یہ نیت درست نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر اس نے ظہر کی نسبت وقت کی طرف کی تو اگر وقت میں ہی نماز ادا کر لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی اور اگر وقت ظہر کی نیت تو کی لیکن ظہر کا وقت نکل چکا اور وہ اسے بھول گیا کہ وقت نکل چکا ہے تو پھر اس کی ظہر کی نماز صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ فرض الوقت: اگر کسی نے وقت ظہر کہا یا وقت فرض کہا تو دونوں کا ماحصل ایک ہی ہے لہذا وقت میں نماز ادا کر صحیح ہو جائے گا اور اگر وقت فعل عبادت کے لئے معیار ہے۔ معیار ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فعل عبادت وقت کو گھیر لے اور اس عبادت کے بعد وقت باقی نہ بچے کہ اس جیسی دوسری عبادت ادا کر سکے تو اس میں تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے جیسے رمضان کا مہینہ رمضان کے روزوں کے لئے معیار ہے تو اس میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے لہذا رمضان میں نفلی روزہ کی نیت کر لے تو نفلی روزہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر فعل عبادت کے لئے وقت مشکل ہو یعنی پورے وقت میں ایک ہی عبادت ادا کی جائے لیکن فعلِ اد وقت کا احاطہ نہ کرے بلکہ فعل عبادت کی ادائیگی کے بعد وقت بچ جائے ، جیسے حج کا وقت حج کے لئے مشکل ہے۔ کیونکہ اشہر حج میں صرف ایک ہی حج ادا کر سکتا ہے زیادہ نہیں اس اعتبار سے معیار ہے اور حج ادا کرنے کے بعد بھی وقت بچا رہتا ہے اس اعتبار سے ظرف ہے تو چونکہ حج کے وقت میں دونوں جہتیں ہیں اس لئے حج کے وقت کو فعل حج کے لئے مشکل قرار دیا گیا ہے اور جب یہ وقت حج کے لئے معیار بھی ہے تو مطلق حج کی نیت سے حج ادا ہو جائے گا تعین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور حج کا وقت فعل حج کے لئے ظرف بھی ہے جس طرح نماز ادا کرنے کے بعد وقت بیچ جاتا ہے اسی طرح افعال حج کے بعد وقت بچ جاتا ہے۔
إِلَّا فِي الْجُمُعَةِ فَإِنَّهَا بَدَّلْ لَا أَصْل إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ إِعْتِقَادُهُ أَنَّهَا فَرْضُ الْوَقْتِ، فَإِنَّ نَوَىٰ الظهر لَا غَيْرَ ، أَخْتلِف فِيهِ وَالأَصْحُ الجَوَاز. :ترجمه مگر جمعہ میں اس لئے کہ وہ بدل ہے اصل نہیں مگر یہ کہ اس کا اعتقاد ہو کہ وہی فرض وقت ہے پس اگر ظہر کی نیت کی نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ کی تو اس میں اختلاف ہے اور جواز اصح ہے۔
تشریح: جمعہ کے دن جمعہ اصل ہے یا بدل ہے؟ شیخین علیہم الرحمہ کے نزدیک جمعہ کے دن جمعہ بدل ہے اور ظیر اصل ہے البتہ جمعہ ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے ظہر ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گی ، علامہ حصکفی اور علامہ ابن عابدین کی بھی سیکی رائے ہے، امام محمد کے نزدیک جمعہ کے روز جمعہ ہی اصل ہے البتہ ظہر کی ادائیگی سے جمعہ کو ساقط کیا جاسکتا ہے امام اقر کے نزدیک جمعہ ہی اصل ہے اور ظہر جمعہ کے فوت ہونے کی صورت میں بدل بن سکتا ہے بعض فقہاء کے نزدیک
Third section: On the explanation of specification of the intended (action) and its absence. The principle with us is that the intended (action) is either from acts of worship or not. If it is an act of worship, then if its time is a container (zarf) for the performance, meaning it accommodates it and other (similar acts), then specification is necessary, like prayer, such that one intends Zuhr. If he couples it with the day, like 'Zuhr of today', it is valid even if the time exits; or with the time and the time has not exited; if it exits and he is unaware, it does not suffice in the correct view. And 'the obligation of the time' is like 'Zuhr of the time'... [Urdu commentary follows] ...Except for Friday, for it is a substitute (badal) not an original (asl), unless he believes it is the obligation of the time. If he intends Zuhr only, there is disagreement, and the more correct is permissibility.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental Hanafi rule regarding the specification (ta'yin) of intention (niyyah) in acts of worship based on the nature of the time in which the worship is performed. The rule distinguishes three types of time: container (zarf), enveloping (miyar), and problematic (mushkil). 

1. **Container (zarf):** The time can accommodate multiple similar acts. Example: Prayer times (e.g., Zuhr time can accommodate both Zuhr and any makeup prayers). Here, specification of which prayer is intended is obligatory because without it, the act cannot be distinguished. The hadith 'Actions are by intentions' is cited as proof. 

2. **Enveloping (miyar):** The time is completely filled by the act, leaving no room for another similar act. Example: The month of Ramadan for fasting. If one intends a nafl fast in Ramadan, it counts as the Ramadan fast, not nafl, because the time is exclusively for Ramadan. No specification is needed. 

3. **Problematic (mushkil):** The time has aspects of both container and enveloping. Example: The months of Hajj. Only one Hajj can be performed in a year (like miyar), but time remains after Hajj (like zarf). Here, specification is not required; an absolute intention of Hajj suffices. 

**Exception – Friday Prayer:** Friday prayer is a substitute (badal) for Zuhr in the view of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to them, the original obligation is Zuhr, but Friday fulfills it. Therefore, if one intends Zuhr for Friday prayer, it is valid. There is a difference of opinion: Imam Muhammad considers Friday the original, but even then, intending Zuhr may not invalidate it. The relied-upon position (asahh) is permissibility. The passage also cites later Hanafi authorities like Haskafi and Ibn Abidin supporting this. 

This rule is a precise application of the broader maxim 'Al-Umuru bi Maqasidiha' (Actions are by intentions) and is essential for muftis when issuing fatwas about the validity of worship.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): A time that can accommodate more than one similar act of worship; the act does not exhaust the time.
معیار (miyar): A time that is completely filled by the act of worship; no room for another similar act.
مشکل (mushkil): A time that has aspects of both zarf and miyar; it accommodates only one act but leaves leftover time.
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of the exact act of worship in intention (e.g., 'I am praying Zuhr').
بدل (badal): A substitute for the original obligation; here Friday prayer is a substitute for Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following requires specification (ta'yin) of intention according to the Hanafi rule?
A) Fasting in Ramadan
B) Hajj
C) Zuhr prayer
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The necessity of specification in intention depends on the time type: container requires it, enveloping and problematic do not.

10 min
Exception for Friday: Substitution and Intention
Exception to the intention rule: Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that Friday prayer is a substitute for Zuhr and evaluate the intra-madhhab difference regarding intention specification for Friday.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is badal for Zuhr; intending Zuhr suffices per the soundest view.

Friday prayer appears to follow the general rule of a container time, but the Hanafi school treats it as an exception because it is a substitute (badal) for the original obligation of Zuhr. This creates a dispute within the school: some hold that Friday is the original obligation, leading to different requirements for intention. This lesson explores the ikhtilaf and the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the exception
The passage states: 'Except for Friday, for it is a substitute, not an original, unless he believes it is the obligation of the time.'
The general rule would require specification because prayer time is zarf, but Friday is exceptional.
2
Understand the basis: Friday as badal
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) and later scholars like Haskafi and Ibn Abidin, Friday is a substitute for Zuhr. The original obligation is Zuhr, but Friday fulfills it.
This view relies on hadith and qiyas jali.
3
Know the alternate view
Imam Muhammad (in one narration) holds that Friday itself is the original obligation. This leads to a stricter stance on intention.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The soundest (asahh) position is permissibility: if one intends Zuhr for Friday prayer, it is valid. This is because the real obligation is the Friday act, and intending Zuhr with the belief that Friday is the obligation of the time suffices.
Fatwa is given on this view.

Third section: On the explanation of specification of the intended (action) and its absence. The principle with us is that the intended (action) is either from acts of worship or not. If he couples it with the day, like 'Zuhr of today', it is valid even if the time exits; or with the time and the time has not exited; if it exits and he is unaware, it does not suffice in the correct view. And 'the obligation of the time' is like 'Zuhr of the time'... Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental Hanafi rule regarding the specification (ta'yin) of intention (niyyah) in acts of worship based on the nature of the time in which the worship is performed. The rule distinguishes three types of time: container (zarf), enveloping (miyar), and problematic (mushkil). 

1. **Container (zarf):** The time can accommodate multiple similar acts. Example: Prayer times (e.g., Zuhr time can accommodate both Zuhr and any makeup prayers). Here, specification of which prayer is intended is obligatory because without it, the act cannot be distinguished. The hadith 'Actions are by intentions' is cited as proof. 

2. **Enveloping (miyar):** The time is completely filled by the act, leaving no room for another similar act. Example: The month of Ramadan for fasting. If one intends a nafl fast in Ramadan, it counts as the Ramadan fast, not nafl, because the time is exclusively for Ramadan. No specification is needed. 

3. **Problematic (mushkil):** The time has aspects of both container and enveloping. Example: The months of Hajj. Only one Hajj can be performed in a year (like miyar), but time remains after Hajj (like zarf). Here, specification is not required; an absolute intention of Hajj suffices. 

**Exception – Friday Prayer:** Friday prayer is a substitute (badal) for Zuhr in the view of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to them, the original obligation is Zuhr, but Friday fulfills it. Therefore, if one intends Zuhr for Friday prayer, it is valid. There is a difference of opinion: Imam Muhammad considers Friday the original, but even then, intending Zuhr may not invalidate it. The relied-upon position (asahh) is permissibility. The passage also cites later Hanafi authorities like Haskafi and Ibn Abidin supporting this. 

This rule is a precise application of the broader maxim 'Al-Umuru bi Maqasidiha' (Actions are by intentions) and is essential for muftis when issuing fatwas about the validity of worship.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): A substitute for the original obligation; here Friday prayer is a substitute for Zuhr.
أصل (asl): Original obligation; Zuhr is the asl, Friday is badal according to the two shaykhs.
الأصح (al-asahh): The more correct view; used for tarjih within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position regarding a person who intends 'Zuhr' for Friday prayer?
A) Invalid because Friday is an original obligation
B) Valid because Friday is a substitute for Zuhr
C) Valid only if he also intended Friday
D) Invalid because the intention must be for Friday

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is an exception to the specification rule; intending Zuhr is valid per the relied-upon view.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
The Determined Needs No Specification: Fasting in Ramadan
Qawida with furuat: maxim application to fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-muta'ayyin la yahtaj ila al-ta'yin' to cases of fasting and identify exceptions for the traveler.

Core Idea
When time exclusively determines the act, no specification in intention is needed.

In Hanafi fiqh, the role of intention (niyyah) is nuanced. While intention is generally required, specifying the exact type of worship (ta'yin) is not always necessary. This lesson explores a key sub-maxim: when the time of an act is a pure measure (mi'yar) that accommodates no other similar act, the law deems the act already determined, making ta'yin futile. The classic example is fasting in Ramadan for a healthy resident. Understanding this maxim empowers a mufti to correctly rule on cases where intention is ambiguous or misdirected.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mi'yar from zarf
Identify whether the time of an act is a measure (mi'yar) that exclusively fits one act or a container (zarf) that can host multiple acts. This distinction governs the need for ta'yin.
Mi'yar: time that does not accommodate any other similar worship, e.g., Ramadan day for a healthy resident. Zarf: time that can accommodate other fasts, e.g., any other day.
2
State the ruling for the healthy resident
Apply the maxim: for a healthy resident, no specification is required. Any intention (even supererogatory or another obligatory) results in the Ramadan fast.
This is the core ruling from the text.
3
Analyze the exceptions: sick and traveler
Examine the different rulings for a sick person and a traveler. For a sick person, the correct view is that it still counts as Ramadan. For a traveler, if he intends another obligatory, it counts as that; if he intends supererogatory, the correct view is it falls for Ramadan.
These nuances show the depth of the maxim and its limits.
4
Identify the underlying illah (reason)
The illah is that the time is already determined (muta'ayyin) by the Shari'ah for that specific act, so the servant's specification becomes redundant (laghw).
The maxim 'al-muta'ayyin la yahtaj ila al-ta'yin' is derived from this.
5
Apply the maxim to similar cases
Understand that this maxim applies to other ibadat where the time is exclusive, such as the five daily prayers in their prescribed times (though with some nuances).
The scope of the maxim includes fasting and may extend to other acts.

Source Text

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس کا وقت اس کے لئے معیار ہو بائیں معنی کہ اس کے علاوہ کی گنجائش نہ رکھتا ہو جیسے رمضان کے دن میں روز ور رکھنا تو عین ضروری نہیں ہے، اگر روزہ رکھنے والا تندرست اور مقیم ہو ، تو مطلق نیست نفل کی نیت اور واجب آخر کی نیت سے روز ہ صحیح ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ متعین میں تعیین لغو ہے۔
تشریح : او پر یہ بیان کیا گیا تھا کہ اگر وقت عبادت کے لئے ظرف ہے جس میں اس جنس کی دوسری عبادت کی گنجائش ہے تو اس میں تعیین ضروری ہے۔ اور اگر وقت عبادت کے لئے معیار ہے جس میں اس جنس کی دوسری عبادت کی گنجائش نہیں ہے جیسے رمضان کے دن میں رمضان کا روزہ تو اس میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایام رمضان شارع علیہ السلام کی طرف سے رمضان کے روزوں کے لئے متعین ہیں لہذا بندہ کی طرف سے تین لغو ہوگی کی وجہ ہے اگر کوئی شخص صیح اور مقیم ہو تو ایام رمضان میں جس روزہ کی بھی نیت کرے گا تو رمضان ہی کا روزہ شمار ہوگا اگر چہ وہ اس کی تعیین نہ کرے۔
و اذانوى واجبا آخر فى يوم رمضان يقع عن رمضان (هندیه ج ۱ ص ۱۹۶) الان رمضان معيار لم يشرع فيه صوم آخر فكان متعيناً للفرض والمتعين لا يحتاج الى التعيين (شامی زکریاج۳ ص ۳۲۲)
رمضان کا وقت معیار ہے جس کی وجہ سے صحیح اور مقیم کے لئے رمضان کے مہینہ میں روزہ کی تعیین کرنا کہ فرض سے بانٹل ہے یا واجب ہے لیو ہے کیونکہ تین غیر متعین میں ہوتی ہے اور یہاں پہلے ہی متعین ہے لہذا متعین میں نیت کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ تعین کرنا ایک لغوفعل قرار پائے گا۔
ولو صام مقيم عن غير رمضان ولو لجهله بهای رمضان فهو عنه لاعما نوى لحديث اذا جاء رمضان فلا صوم الا عن رمضان (الدر مع تنویر الابصار، ج ۳ ص / ۳۴۴)
وَإِن كَانَ مَرِيضاً، فَفِيهِ رَوَايَتَانِ وَالصَّحِيحُ وَقَوْعُهُ عَنْ رَمَضَانَ سَوَاءٌ نَّوى وَاجِباً آخَرَ أَوْ نَفْلًا وَأَمَّا الْمُسَافِرُ : فَإِنْ نَوَى عَنْ وَاجِبِ آخَرَ وَقَعَ عَمَّا نَوَاهُ لَا عَنْ رَمَضَانَ، وَفِي النَّفْلِ روايتان، وَالصَّحِيحُ وُقُوعُهُ عَنْ رَمَضَانَ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر وہ بیمار ہو تو اس میں دور و استیں ہیں اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اس کا وقوع رمضان کی طرف سے ہوگا خواہ اس نے دوسرے واجب کی نیت کی یا نفل کی۔ اور بہر حال مسافر پس اگر اس نے دوسرے واجب کی نیت کی تو اس کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا جس کی نیت کی نہ کہ رمضان کا اور نفل میں دور واسیتیں ہیں صحیح یہ ہے کہ اس کا وقوع رضان کی طرف سے ہوگا۔
تشریح رمضان المبارک کے ماہ میں اگر کوئی مریض روزہ رکھتا ہے لیکن وہ رمضان کے روزہ کے علاوہ کسی اور کے روزہ کی نیت کر لیتا ہے تو رمضان کا روزہ ہوگا یا جس روزہ کی اس نے نیت کی ہے وہ روزہ ہوگا اس سلسلہ میں تمین قول علامہ جموئی نے نقل کئے ہیں۔ (۱) رمضان کے ماہ مقدس میں اگر رمضان کے روزوں کے علاوہ کسی اور روزے کی نیت کرے تب بھی رمضان شن کے روزے ہونگے شیخ الاسلام اور شمس الائمہ نے اس کو پسند کیا ہے اور مجمع میں اس کی تصحیح کی گئی ہے صاحب اشباہ کے نزدیک بھی یہی پسند یدہ ہے۔
And if its time is a measure for it, meaning that it does not accommodate any other, like fasting on a day of Ramadan, then specification is not a condition if the fasting person is healthy and resident. So it is valid with absolute intention, intention of supererogatory, and intention of another obligatory, because specification in the already determined is futile. Translation: And if its time is a measure for it, meaning it does not allow any other, like fasting on a day of Ramadan, then specification is not necessary. If the fasting person is healthy and resident, then the fast is valid with absolute intention, intention of supererogatory, and intention of another obligatory, because specification in the determined is futile. Elaboration: Above it was stated that if the time is a container for the act, allowing another act of the same type, then specification is necessary. And if the time is a measure for the act, not allowing another of the same type, like Ramadan day for Ramadan fast, then specification is not needed because the days of Ramadan are determined by the Shari'ah for Ramadan fasts, so the servant's specification is futile. So if a person is healthy and resident, whatever fast he intends on Ramadan days, it counts as Ramadan fast even if he does not specify. And if he intends another obligatory fast on a day of Ramadan, it falls for Ramadan (Hindiyya vol. 1 p. 196) because Ramadan is a measure, no other fast is legislated in it, so it is determined for the obligatory, and the determined does not need specification (Shami Zakariyya vol. 3 p. 322). The time of Ramadan is a measure, due to which for a healthy resident, specifying the fast as obligatory or supererogatory is futile, because specification occurs in the non-determined, and here it is already determined, so no need for intention in the determined; rather, specifying is a futile act. And if a resident fasts for other than Ramadan, even out of ignorance of Ramadan, it is from Ramadan, not what he intended, because of the hadith: When Ramadan comes, there is no fast except from Ramadan (al-Durr with Tanwir al-Absar, vol. 3 p. 344). And if he is sick, then there are two narrations, and the correct is that it falls for Ramadan whether he intended another obligatory or supererogatory. As for the traveler: if he intended another obligatory, it falls for what he intended, not for Ramadan; and in supererogatory, there are two narrations, and the correct is that it falls for Ramadan. Translation: And if he is sick, then there are two narrations, and the correct is that it falls for Ramadan whether he intended another obligatory or supererogatory. As for the traveler: if he intended another obligatory, it falls for what he intended, not for Ramadan; and in supererogatory, there are two narrations, the correct is that it falls for Ramadan. Elaboration: In the month of Ramadan, if a sick person fasts but intends a fast other than Ramadan, then whether it counts as Ramadan or what he intended: there are three sayings transmitted by Allama Jamawi. (1) In the sacred month of Ramadan, if he intends a fast other than Ramadan, still it will be Ramadan fasts; Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma preferred this, and it was corrected in Majma'; the author of Ashbah also prefers this.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents the qawida that when the time of an act is a measure (mi'yar) exclusive to that act, ta'yin (specification) is not required. The example is fasting in Ramadan: the time of Ramadan is a measure because no other fast is legislated for that time for a healthy resident. Therefore, if a healthy resident fasts with any intention (absolute, supererogatory, or another obligatory), it counts as the Ramadan fast. The text then discusses exceptions: for a sick person, the correct view is it still counts as Ramadan; for a traveler, if he intends another obligatory, it counts as that, but if he intends supererogatory, the correct view is it counts as Ramadan. This is a key application of the maxim 'المعين لا يحتاج إلى التعيين' (the determined does not need specification).

Key Terms
متعين (muta'ayyin): That which is already determined by a clear indicator, such as time or shari'ah ruling.
تعيين (ta'yin): The act of specifying the type of worship in intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a healthy resident fasts on a day in Ramadan with the intention of making up a missed obligatory fast from another month, what fast is counted?
A) The make-up fast he intended.
B) The Ramadan fast.
C) Both fasts.
D) No fast is valid because intention is wrong.

Key Takeaway
When time is a measure (mi'yar) exclusive to a specific worship, ta'yin (specification) is not required; the act is already determined.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Ramadan as a Self-Determining Standard: The Maxim of Ta'yin
Explanation of the maxim with furuat and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Ramadan is a standard' to determine the ruling for a fasting person's intention in various conditions (healthy resident, sick, traveler).

Core Idea
Ramadan itself determines the fast; specific intention (ta'yin) is not needed for a healthy resident.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi maxim from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: 'Ramadan is a standard; no other fast is legislated in it, so it is self-determined for the obligatory fast.' The passage explores how this maxim governs the validity of a fasting person's intention when they inadvertently or deliberately intend another fast. We will analyze the furuat (branches) for the healthy resident, the sick, and the traveler, noting the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the reliance on complementary qawaid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its core components
State the maxim in Arabic and English. Identify the key terms: mi'yar (standard), ta'yin (determination), and the claim that the self-determined does not need determination.
The maxim is a dabṭ (restrictive principle) under the major qawāʿid.
2
Apply the maxim to the healthy resident
Apply the maxim to a healthy resident: whatever he intends in Ramadan counts as Ramadan. Explain why ta'yin is futile.
This is the default ruling with strong evidence (hadith).
3
Examine exceptions: sick and traveler
For the sick, distinguish between beneficial fasting (counts as Ramadan) and harmful fasting (follows intention). For the traveler, note the ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa says it follows intention, Sahibayn say it counts as Ramadan.
These exceptions involve the rukhsa (concession) of travel/sickness.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf for the traveler
Analyze the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) in terms of which obligation is fulfilled.
This ikhtilaf arises from conflicting applications of the maxim and the rukhsa.
5
Relate to complementary qawaid and istithna'at
Link the maxim to its istithna'at: traveler intending another wajib (overridden by rukhsa) and sick with harm (overridden by harm removal). Note related maxims: اليقين لا يزول بالشك and الأمور بمقاصدها.
The exceptions do not invalidate the maxim but specify its scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولو صام مقيم عن غير رمضان ولو لجهله بكونه رمضان فهو عنه لا عما نوى لحديث اذا جاء رمضان فلا صوم الا عن رمضان (الدر مع تنویر الابصار، ج ۳ ص / ۳۴۴)
وَإِن كَانَ مَرِيضاً، فَفِيهِ رَوَايَتَانِ وَالصَّحِيحُ وَقَوْعُهُ عَنْ رَمَضَانَ سَوَاءٌ نَّوى وَاجِباً آخَرَ أَوْ نَفْلًا وَأَمَّا الْمُسَافِرُ : فَإِنْ نَوَى عَنْ وَاجِبِ آخَرَ وَقَعَ عَمَّا نَوَاهُ لَا عَنْ رَمَضَانَ، وَفِي النَّفْلِ روايتان، وَالصَّحِيحُ وُقُوعُهُ عَنْ رَمَضَانَ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر وہ بیمار ہو تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اس کا وقوع رمضان کی طرف سے ہوگا خواہ اس نے دوسرے واجب کی نیت کی یا نفل کی۔ اور بہر حال مسافر پس اگر اس نے دوسرے واجب کی نیت کی تو اس کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا جس کی نیت کی نہ کہ رمضان کا اور نفل میں دو روایتیں ہیں صحیح یہ ہے کہ اس کا وقوع رمضان کی طرف سے ہوگا۔
تشریح رمضان المبارک کے ماہ میں اگر کوئی مریض روزہ رکھتا ہے لیکن وہ رمضان کے روزہ کے علاوہ کسی اور کے روزہ کی نیت کر لیتا ہے تو رمضان کا روزہ ہوگا یا جس روزہ کی اس نے نیت کی ہے وہ روزہ ہوگا اس سلسلہ میں تین قول علامہ حموی نے نقل کئے ہیں۔ (۱) رمضان کے ماہ مقدس میں اگر رمضان کے روزوں کے علاوہ کسی اور روزے کی نیت کرے تب بھی رمضان ہی کے روزے ہونگے شیخ الاسلام اور شمس الائمہ نے اس کو پسند کیا ہے اور مجمع میں اس کی تصحیح کی گئی ہے صاحب اشباہ کے نزدیک بھی یہی پسندیدہ ہے۔
(۲) جس روزہ کی نیت کرے گا اس کے مطابق روزہ ہوگا صاحب ہدایہ اور اکثر مشائخ نے اس کو اختیار کی ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ شیخ محمد بن عبد اللہ التمر تاشی نے اپنی مختصر تنویر الابصار میں اسی پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ (۳) تیسری قسم میں تفصیل ہے وہ یہ کہ فرض کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) بیماری اس قسم کی ہے کہ جس میں روزہ رکھنا مفید ہے جیسے بدہضمی، ہیضہ وغیرہ۔ تو اس صورت میں روزہ اگر رکھا تو رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا، اوراگر روزہ رکھنے سے نقصان پہنچنے کا اندیشہ ہے جیسے آنکھ درد سر درد اس صورت میں اس کی نیت کے مطابق روزہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال مریض روزہ رکھنے سے عاجز ہوگا یا مرض کے بڑھنے کا اندیشہ ہے ازدیادہ مرض کی صورت میں وہ مسافر کی طرح ہے کہ جس روزہ کی نیت کرے گا اسی کے مطابق ہوگا۔ اور عجز کی صورت میں اگر اس نے روزہ رکھا تو وہ صحیح کی طرح ہے لہذا اس کا روزہ رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا اس کو رخصت عجز کی وجہ سے دی گئی تھی لیکن جب اس نے روزہ رکھ لیا تو یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ وہ عاجز نہیں ہے البتہ اسی کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا۔
تطبيق : شیخ الاسلام اور شمس الائمہ اور صاحب ہدایہ اور اکثر مشائخ کے قول میں تضاد نہیں ہے۔ شیخ الاسلام اور شمس الائمہ کا قول روزہ رکھنے کی صورت میں بجز صوم کی صورت پر محمول ہوگا اور صاحب ہدایہ اور اکثر مشائخ کے قول کو ازدیادہ مرض کی صورت پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ وأما المسافر : اگر مسافر نے رمضان کے مہینہ میں کسی واجب آخر کی نیت کر لی تو رمضان کا روزہ ہوگا یا واجب آخر کا علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ جس کی وہ نیت کرے گا وہی روزہ ہوگا کیونکہ سفر کی وجہ سے جب اس کو روزہ نہ رکھنے کی اجازت ہے تو اس کو اس بات کی بھی اجازت ہے کہ وہ واجب آخر کی نیت سے کوئی روزہ رکھ لے کیونکہ سبب رخصت سفر اس کے حق میں اب بھی موجود ہے البتہ عند الصاحبین رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا ، اس لئے رخصت ترک میں مسافر مقیم سے جدا ہوتا ہے لیکن جب اس نے رخصت ترک پر عمل نہیں کیا تو اب وہ مسافر مثل مقیم کے ہو گیا اس لئے اس کا روزہ جو اس نے واجب آخر کی نیت سے رکھا تھا رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا علامہ تمر تاشی کی جامع صغیر کی شرح میں اس طرح ہی ہے " أما في حق المسافر فان نوى واجباً آخر يقع عنه عند الامام" (شامی زکریا ج ۳ ص ۴۲۳) علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ مسافر اور مریض کے لئے رمضان کے روزہ کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے عند الصاحبین ۔ قاضی خان فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر انہوں نے رات میں نیت نہ کی اور طلوع فجر کے بعد نیت کر لی تو امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک کافی ہے اور اسی کو حسن نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ صاحب اشباہ نے اس پر کوئی تنبیہ نہیں کی ہے، لیکن علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب الاشباہ والنظائر نے شرح کنز میں وضاحت کی ہے کہ رمضان اور نذر معین کے روزہ کے لئے رات میں اگر نیت کر سکے تو نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے روزہ کی نیت کر سکتا ہے بشرطیکہ کچھ کھایا پیا نہ ہواور
There is no scope for worship [without intention] — like the fast of Ramadan in the days of Ramadan, there is no need for determination (ta'yin) because the days of Ramadan are determined by the Lawgiver (peace be upon him) for the fasts of Ramadan. Therefore, from the servant's side, determination is futile. The reason: if a person is healthy and resident, whatever fast he intends in the days of Ramadan, it will count as the fast of Ramadan, even if he does not determine it. And if he intends another obligatory fast on a day of Ramadan, it falls for Ramadan (Hindiyya vol. 1 p. 196). Indeed, Ramadan is a standard (mi'yar); no other fast is legislated in it, so it is self-determined for the obligatory fast, and the self-determined does not need determination (Shami Zakariyya vol. 3 p. 322). The time of Ramadan is a standard; therefore, for a healthy resident in the month of Ramadan, determining the intention whether it is from fard or wajib is futile because determination occurs in the non-determined, and here it is already determined. Hence, there is no need for intention in the determined; rather determining is a futile act. And if a resident fasts for other than Ramadan, even out of ignorance that it is Ramadan, it is for Ramadan and not for what he intended, due to the hadith: 'When Ramadan comes, there is no fast except for Ramadan' (al-Durr with Tanwir al-Absar, vol. 3 p. 344). And if he is sick, there are two narrations and the correct view is that it falls for Ramadan, whether he intended another obligatory fast or a supererogatory one. As for the traveler: if he intended another obligatory fast, it falls for what he intended, not for Ramadan. In the case of supererogatory, there are two narrations, and the correct view is that it falls for Ramadan. Translation: And if he is sick, there are two narrations and the correct is that it occurs for Ramadan, whether he intended another wajib or nafl. And as for the traveler, if he intended another wajib, it occurs for what he intended, not for Ramadan; and in nafl there are two narrations, the correct is that it occurs for Ramadan. Elaboration: In the blessed month of Ramadan, if a sick person fasts but intends a fast other than Ramadan, will it be a fast of Ramadan or the fast he intended? Regarding this, three statements are transmitted by Allamah Hamawi: (1) In the sacred month of Ramadan, if he intends a fast other than Ramadan, it will still be a fast of Ramadan; Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma preferred this, and it is corrected in the Majma'; and Sahib Ashbah also prefers this. (2) The fast will be according to his intention; Sahib Hidaya and most mashayikh chose this, and it is said that this is Zahir al-Riwayah. Shaykh Muhammad bin Abdullah al-Tamartashi relied on this in his Mukhtasar Tanwir al-Absar. (3) The third type has detail: there are two types of sickness: (i) that in which fasting is beneficial, like indigestion, cholera, etc. — in this case, if he fasts, it will be a fast of Ramadan; and (ii) if there is fear of harm from fasting, like eye pain, headache — in this case, it will be according to his intention. In any case, the sick person is either unable to fast or fears increase of sickness. In the case of increase of sickness, he is like a traveler: whatever fast he intends, it will be accordingly. In the case of inability, if he fasts, he is like a healthy person, so his fast will be that of Ramadan; he was given a concession due to inability, but when he fasted, it became apparent that he was not unable, so he is attached to the ruling of a healthy person. Application: There is no contradiction between the statements of Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma and that of Sahib Hidaya and most mashayikh. The statement of Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma is carried on the case of fasting (i.e., without harm), while the statement of Sahib Hidaya and most mashayikh is carried on the case of increase of sickness. And as for the traveler: if a traveler intends another obligatory fast in the month of Ramadan, will it be a fast of Ramadan or the other wajib? Allamah Hamawi says it will be according to his intention because when he is permitted not to fast due to travel, he is also permitted to fast for another wajib, since the cause of concession (travel) still exists. However, according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it will be a fast of Ramadan because the traveler differs from the resident in the concession of not fasting, but when he did not act upon the concession of leaving the fast, he becomes like a resident. Therefore, his fast which he intended for another wajib will be a fast of Ramadan. In the commentary of Jami' al-Saghir by Allamah Tamartashi, it is like this: 'As for the traveler, if he intends another wajib, it falls for what he intended according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]' (Shami Zakariyya vol. 3 p. 423). Allamah Hamawi says that for a traveler and sick person, it is necessary to intend from the night for the fast of Ramadan according to the Sahibayn. Qadi Khan says that if they did not intend at night and intended after dawn, it is sufficient according to Imam Abu Yusuf, and Hasan chose this. Sahib Ashbah did not warn about this, but Allamah Hamawi says that Sahib al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair clarified in Sharh al-Kanz that for the fast of Ramadan and a specified vow, if he can intend at night, he may intend the fast before midday, provided he has not eaten or drunk anything.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi legal maxim that the month of Ramadan itself is a determining factor (mi'yar) for the fast of Ramadan, making specific intention (ta'yin) unnecessary for a healthy resident. The passage begins by stating the general rule: if a healthy resident intends any fast during Ramadan, it automatically counts as the Ramadan fast, even if he intends another obligatory or nafl fast. This is because the time itself is designated by the Lawgiver for Ramadan, so any other intention is futile. The justification is that ta'yin is only needed when the act is not already determined; here, the time is already determined. The hadith 'When Ramadan comes, there is no fast except for Ramadan' supports this. The passage then differentiates between the cases of a sick person and a traveler. For a sick person, there are two narrations: one that it counts as Ramadan regardless, and the other that it counts according to his intention. The correct view is that it counts as Ramadan. For a traveler, if he intends another obligatory fast, it counts as that intended fast according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to the Sahibayn, it counts as Ramadan. There is also discussion of different opinions: some early scholars (Shaykh al-Islam, Shams al-A'imma) rule that it always counts as Ramadan, while others (Sahib Hidaya, majority) rule that it follows intention, and this latter is from Zahir al-Riwayah. A third detailed view resolves the apparent contradiction by distinguishing between sickness where fasting is beneficial (counts as Ramadan) versus harmful (follows intention). The traveler's case is further nuanced: the concession (rukhsa) of not fasting does not automatically allow him to substitute another fast; according to the Sahibayn, when he chooses to fast, the ruling of a resident applies. The passage ends with a note on the timing of intention: for Ramadan and specified vows, intention from night is obligatory according to Sahibayn, but Imam Abu Yusuf allows it after dawn if nothing was consumed. This lesson exemplifies the Hanafi method of applying a qa'ida (maxim) to various scenarios and reconciling apparent conflicts through takhsis (specification).

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of intention to a particular fast, e.g., intending a qada or nadhr fast instead of Ramadan.
معيار (mi'yar): A standard that automatically determines the ruling; here, the month of Ramadan itself serves as the standard for the obligatory fast.
رخصت (rukhsa): Concession allowing a traveler or sick person not to fast; its continued existence may affect the ruling when they choose to fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim discussed, if a healthy resident intentionally intends a nafl fast on a day of Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is valid as a nafl fast.
B) The fast counts as the obligatory Ramadan fast.
C) The fast is invalid due to incorrect intention.
D) The fast is suspended until he re-intends.

Key Takeaway
The month of Ramadan itself is a self-determining standard; for a healthy resident, any intention is overridden, but for a traveler and sick, concessions may alter the ruling.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
Effect of Intention on Fasting in Ramadan for Traveler and Sick
Explains how intention determines the type of fast for traveler/sick in Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine the type of fast for a traveler or sick person in Ramadan, and identify the differences among Hanafi imams on timing and default rulings.

Core Idea
Intention determines the fast, except when the person's condition makes them like a resident.

This passage applies the foundational maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) to the fasting of those granted concessions: the traveler and the sick. However, the application is not straightforward—there are disputes among Hanafi authorities about whether the intention always prevails or sometimes defaults to the Ramadan obligation. Understanding these nuances is essential for a mufti to issue correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its authority
The passage opens with the general rule from Sahib al-Hidaya: the fast corresponds to the intention. Note that this rule is said to be from Zahir al-Riwayah and chosen by the mashayikh.
Consider the authority level: Zahir al-Riwayah is the most authoritative.
2
Distinguish the two cases for the sick person
Read the subdivision: (a) if fasting is beneficial (e.g., indigestion), it counts as Ramadan; (b) if there is fear of harm, it follows intention. Further, differentiate between actual incapacity (makes fast like qada) and fear of increase of illness (makes fast like traveler).
This shows that the ruling depends on the nature of the sickness.
3
Analyze the traveler dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the traveler's intention determines the fast because the concession (rukhsa) of travel remains. The Sahibayn argue that by fasting, the traveler forgoes the concession and becomes like a resident, so the fast defaults to Ramadan. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
This ikhtilaf affects the mufta bihi position.
4
Examine the timing of intention
Review the different opinions: Sahibayn require night intention; Abu Yusuf allows after dawn; Zufar's strict view is rejected. Note how the passage resolves contradictions by applying statements to different scenarios.
Timing is a separate issue from the type determination.
5
Apply to voluntary (nafl) fasts and vowed fasts
The correct view is that a voluntary fast in Ramadan counts as Ramadan due to the importance of the time. Similar reasoning applies to vowed fasts on specific days.
This demonstrates how the maxim interacts with other principles.

قاضی خان فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر انہوں نے رات میں نیت نہ کی اور طلوع فجر کے بعد نیت کر لی تو امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک کافی ہے اور اسی کو حسن نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ صاحب اشباہ نے اس پر کوئی تنبیہ نہیں کی ہے، لیکن علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب الاشباہ والنظائر نے شرح کنز میں وضاحت کی ہے کہ رمضان اور نذرمعین کے روزہ کے لئے رات میں اگر نیت کر سکے تو نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے روزہ کی نیت کر سکتا ہے بشر طیکہ کچھ کھایا پیا نہ ہواور انہوں نے مریض ، مسافر اور مقیم کے درمیان کوئی تفصیل ذکر نہیں کی ہے۔ حیث قال فانه لا فرق بين الصحيح والمريض والمسافر والمقيم لانه لا يفصل فيما ذكرنا من الليل. امام زفر رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسافر اور مریض کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے رنے کی ادائیگی ان پر واجب نہیں ہے تو یہ مثل قضا کے ہیں جیسے قضاء روزے کی ادائیگی کے لئے رات سے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اسی طرح ان کے لئے رمضان کے روزے کی ادائیگی کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ امام زفر کے اس قول کو یہ کہہ کر رد کر دیا گیا ہے کہ اس میں تغلیظ ہے جب کہ مسافر اور مریض کے لئے مناسب تخفیف ہے۔ قنیہ میں نقل کیا گیا ہے کہ اگر مریض اور مسافر نے ماہ رمضان میں رات میں روزہ کی نیت نہ کی اور نصف النہار سے قبل روزہ کی نیت کر لی تو عندابی یوسف صحیح ہے۔ اور حسن نے بھی اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ صاحب کشف کبیر فرماتے ہیں کہ عندالی یوسف کے ذکر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امام محمد اور امام ابی حنیفہ کے نزدیک مریض اور مسافر کے لئے رمضان کے روزہ کے لئے رات سے ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کے نزدیک بھی اگر طلوع فجر کے بعد روزہ کی نیت یہ حضرات کرلیں تو رمضان کا روزہ ہو جائے گا۔ مبسوط نہا یہ اور ولوالجیہ میں اسی طرح مذکور ہے۔ وفي النفل روايتان: اگر کسی نے رمضان کے ماہ میں نقل کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا تو اس میں دور وایتیں ہیں۔ (۱) نفل کا روزہ ہوگا۔ (۲) رمضان کا شمار ہوگا اور یہی صحیح ہے۔ تمر تاشی کی جامع صغیر کی شرح میں ہے کہ اگر مسافر نے رمضان کے ماہ میں نفلی روزہ رکھا تو ان سے دو روایتوں میں سے اصح یہ ہے کہ رمضان کا روزہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ رمضان کا روز ہ زیادہ اہم ہے۔ امام کرتی نے مریض کو بھی اسی پر محمول کیا ہے، ایک قول یہ ہے کہ چاہے وہ جس کی نیت کرے رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا بالاتفاق اس لئے کہ مریض کو روزہ نہ رکھنے کی اجازت بجز کی وجہ سے تھی اور روزہ رکھنے سے یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ وہ عاجز نہیں ہے۔ اور مسافر کے حق میں صحیح سفر ہے اور وہ اب بھی موجود ہے۔ اور اس میں ایک مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے متعین دن کے روزہ رکھنے کی نذر مانی اور اس دن میں نفل کی نیت سے روزہ رکھا تو امام ابو یوسف کی روایت یہ ہے کہ نذر کا روزہ ہوگا اور اگر کسی واجب آخر کی نیت کی تو اس کی نیت کے مطابق روزہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ نفل اس کے لئے مشروع ہے اور فرض اس پر مشروع ہے اور بندہ شریعت کی طرف سے اپنے اوپر عائد کردہ وقت کو تبدیل کرنے کا اختیار نہیں رکھتا۔ وَإِنْ كَانَ وَقْتُهَا مُشْكِلاً كَوَقْتِ الْحَجِّ يَشْبَهُ الْمِعْيَارَ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَصْحُ فِي السَّنَةِ إِلَّا حَجَّةً وَاحِدَةً، وَالطَّرْفَ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّ أَفْعَالَهُ لَا تَسْتَغْرِقْ وَقَتَهُ فَيُصَابُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ نَظراً إلَى الْمِعْبَارِيَّةِ وإن نوى نَفْلًا وَقَعَ عَمَا نَوَى نَظُراً إلى الطَّرْفِيَّةِ. وَلَا يَسْقُطُ التَّخَيْنُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ لِصِيْنِ الْوَقْتِ لأنَّ السَعَةَ بَاقِيَة أَنَّهُ لَوْ شَرَعَ مُتَنَفَلا صَحٌ، وَ إِنْ كَانَ حَرَاماً.
(2) The fast will be according to whichever intention he makes – this is the position of Sahib al-Hidaya and the mashayikh have chosen it, and it is said that this is Zahir al-Riwayah. Shaykh Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Tamartashi relied on this in his Mukhtasar Tanwir al-Absar. (3) The third category has detail: that obligatory fasts are of two types. (1) Illness: of the type in which fasting is beneficial, like indigestion, cholera, etc. In that case, if he fasts, it will be the fast of Ramadan; but if there is fear of harm from fasting, like eye pain, headache, then in that case it will be according to his intention. In any case, the sick person is incapable of fasting or there is fear of the illness increasing. In the case of increase of illness, he is like a traveler – whichever fast he intends, it will be according to that. And in the case of incapability, if he fasts, he is like a person observing a missed (qada) fast; therefore, his fast will be the fast of Ramadan. The concession was given due to incapability, but when he fasted, it became apparent that he is not incapable, so it attaches to it. Application: There is no contradiction between the statement of Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma and Sahib al-Hidaya and most mashayikh. The statement of Shaykh al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma will be applied to the case of fasting in the manner of a missed fast, and the statement of Sahib al-Hidaya and most mashayikh will be applied to the case of increase of illness. As for the traveler: If a traveler intends some other obligatory fast in the month of Ramadan, will it be the fast of Ramadan or the other obligatory? 'Allamah Hamawi says: whichever he intends, that fast will be, because since he is permitted not to fast due to travel, he is also permitted to fast with the intention of another obligatory fast, because the cause of concession (travel) still exists for him. However, according to the Sahibayn, it will be the fast of Ramadan because the traveler is distinguished from the resident in the concession of not fasting, but when he did not act upon the concession of not fasting, he became like a resident, so his fast that he intended for another obligatory will be the fast of Ramadan. In the commentary of Jami' al-Saghir by 'Allamah Tamartashi, it is like this: 'As for the traveler, if he intends another obligatory, it occurs for him according to Imam.' [Rashami Zakariyya, vol. 3, p. 423]. 'Allamah Hamawi says: For the traveler and the sick, it is necessary to make intention from the night for the fast of Ramadan according to the Sahibayn. Qadi Khan says: If they did not intend at night and intended after dawn, it is sufficient according to Imam Abu Yusuf, and Hasan chose this. Sahib al-Ashbah did not caution about this, but 'Allamah Hamawi says that Sahib al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir clarified in Sharh al-Kanz that for the fast of Ramadan and a specified vow, if he can intend at night, he may intend the fast before midday provided he did not eat or drink, and he did not mention any detail between sick, traveler, and resident, where he said: 'There is no difference between healthy, sick, traveler, and resident, because he does not differentiate in what we mentioned from the night.' Imam Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) says: For the traveler and the sick, it is necessary to intend from the night, because the performance of Ramadan is not obligatory upon them, so they are like make-up (qada) fasts – just as for performing qada fasts, intention from the night is necessary, similarly for them to perform the fast of Ramadan, intention from the night is necessary. Imam Zufar's statement is refuted by saying that it involves strictness, whereas leniency is appropriate for the traveler and sick. In al-Qunyah, it is narrated: If the sick and traveler did not intend the fast at night in the month of Ramadan and intended before midday, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf, and Hasan chose this. Sahib Kashf Kabir says: From the mention of 'according to Abu Yusuf', it seems that according to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa, it is necessary for the sick and traveler to intend from the night, but this is not so; rather, according to them as well, if they intend after dawn, the fast will be of Ramadan. It is mentioned similarly in Mabsoot, Nahayah, and Walwajiyyah. And regarding voluntary (nafl) fasts, there are two narrations: If someone fasts with the intention of nafl in the month of Ramadan, there are two narrations: (1) It will be a nafl fast; (2) It will count as Ramadan, and this is correct. In the commentary of Jami' al-Saghir by Tamartashi, it is stated: If a traveler fasts voluntarily in the month of Ramadan, among the two narrations the most correct is that it will be the fast of Ramadan, because the fast of Ramadan is more important. Imam Kurti applied the same to the sick. One opinion says: Whichever he intends, it will be the fast of Ramadan by consensus, because the sick was permitted not to fast due to incapability, and by fasting it became clear that he is not incapable. And regarding the traveler, travel is valid and still exists. And in this, there is an issue: If someone vowed to fast on a specific day and on that day he fasted with the intention of nafl, then according to the narration of Imam Abu Yusuf, it will be the vow fast; and if he intended another obligatory fast, it will be according to his intention, because nafl is legitimate for him and obligatory is legitimate upon him, and the servant does not have the authority to change the time assigned to him by the Shari'ah. And if its time is problematic, like the time of Hajj, it resembles a standard (mi'yar) in that only one Hajj per year is valid, and it resembles a part (taraf) in that its actions do not occupy the whole time, so it is achieved by absolute intention considering the standard aspect; and if he intends nafl, it occurs as what he intended considering the part aspect. And the option does not drop in prayer due to the sanctity of time, because scope remains – if he begins voluntarily, it is valid, even if it is prohibited.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on how intention (niyya) affects the fast of Ramadan for those who have a concession to not fast, namely the traveler (musafir) and the sick (marid). The author is expanding on the application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) in the context of fasting. The passage begins by stating the general rule from Sahib al-Hidaya that the fast corresponds to the intention. It then categorizes the sick person into two scenarios: (1) where fasting is beneficial – here the fast counts as Ramadan; (2) where there is fear of harm – here it follows intention. The sick person is either actually incapable or fears increase of illness. In the latter case, he is like a traveler; in the former, like someone making up a missed fast. The commentary resolves an apparent contradiction among scholars by applying their statements to different scenarios. For the traveler, there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa (and al-Hamawi) say the intention determines the fast, while the Sahibayn say it defaults to Ramadan because the traveler's failure to use the concession makes him like a resident. The passage then discusses the timing of intention: according to the Sahibayn, intention must be made at night for Ramadan fast; Abu Yusuf allows it after dawn. Zufar's stricter view is rejected as inappropriate. Finally, the passage treats voluntary (nafl) fasts in Ramadan: the correct view is that it counts as Ramadan due to the importance of the time. An analogous issue is mentioned about vowed fasts. The Arabic excerpt at the end appears to be from the original text of al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, comparing the time of Hajj to a standard (mi'yar) and a part (taraf), and stating that absolute intention suffices for Hajj, but if one intends nafl, it counts as nafl. The commentary emphasizes that the sanctity of the time does not prevent voluntary acts, but the time is not exclusive to the obligatory act.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyya): Intent – the determination in the heart to perform a specific act of worship; its effect determines which fast is counted.
المسافر (al-musafir): Traveler – one who travels a distance of three days (approx. 48 miles) with a permissible purpose, eligible for concessions like not fasting in Ramadan.
المريض (al-marīḍ): Sick person – one whose health would be harmed or recovery delayed by fasting; eligible for concession.
النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary (supererogatory) act – here, a voluntary fast not obligatory.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books – the most authoritative level in Hanafi school.
الصاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a traveler fasts voluntarily (nafl) in Ramadan?
A) It counts as a nafl fast.
B) It counts as the fast of Ramadan, and this is the more correct view.
C) It is invalid because intention is required from the night.
D) It counts as a make-up (qada) fast.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on fasting during Ramadan for those with a concession depends on their specific condition and intention, with the mufta bihi being that intention determines the fast for travelers and for sick who fear harm.
